    稽神录　五代 徐铉

    　　●卷一

    　　○朱拯

    　　伪吴玉山主簿朱拯赴选至扬都（《广记》作“州”）。梦入官署，堂上一紫衣，正坐旁一绿衣。紫衣起揖拯（《广记》无“拯”字）曰：“君当以十千钱见与。”拯拜许诺，遂寤。顷之（毛本无“之”字），补安福令。既至，谒城隍神，庙宇神像皆如梦中。其神座后，屋漏梁坏。拯叹曰：“十千岂非此耶？”即以私财葺之，费如其（《广记》无“其”字）数。（《广记》卷二百八十一）

    　　○韦建

    　　江南戎帅韦建，自统军除武昌节度使。将行，梦一朱衣人，导从数十来诣韦曰：“闻公将镇鄂渚，仆所居在焉。栋宇颓毁，风雨不蔽。非公不能为仆修完也。”韦许诺。及至镇，访之，乃宋无忌庙，视其像，即梦中所见，因新其庙。祠祀数有灵验云。（《广记》卷二百八十一）

    Explanation

    1

    Record of Spirits
    Five Dynasties, Xu Xuan

    Volume One

    Chapter: Zhu Zheng

    Zhu Zheng, a minor official of the pseudo-Wu state serving as the main clerk of Yushan, traveled to Yangzhou for selection (as recorded in the Encyclopedia of the Mysterious, it is written as "state"). In a dream, he entered an official office, where a purple-clad figure sat on the main seat, and a green-clad figure stood beside him. The purple-clad figure rose and bowed to Zhu Zheng (the Encyclopedia of the Mysterious omits "Zhu Zheng"), saying, "You should give me ten thousand coins." Zhu Zheng bowed and agreed, then awoke. Shortly after (the Mao edition omits "after"), he was appointed as the magistrate of Anfu. Upon arriving, he worshipped the city god, and the temple and its statues were all as he had seen in his dream. Behind the god's seat, the roof was leaking, and the beams were broken. Zhu Zheng sighed, "Are the ten thousand coins not for this?" He immediately used his own funds to repair it, spending exactly that amount (the Encyclopedia of the Mysterious omits "that").

    Chapter: Wei Jian

    Wei Jian, the military commander of southern Jiangnan, was promoted from general to military governor of Wuchang. Before departing, he dreamed of a red-clad figure, accompanied by dozens of attendants, who approached him and said, "I have heard that you will be stationed at Ezhǔ. My residence is there. The buildings are in ruins, and they cannot shelter from wind and rain. Only you can repair them for me." Wei Jian agreed. Upon arriving at his post, he sought it out and found it to be the Temple of Song Wujì. Upon seeing the statue, he recognized it as the one he had seen in his dream, and he proceeded to renovate the temple. The temple has been repeatedly shown to be effective (as recorded in the Encyclopedia of the Mysterious, Volume 281).

    2

    ○郑就

    　　寿春屠者郑就，家至贫，尝（《广记》作“常”）梦一人，自称廉颇，谓就（《广记》作“己”）曰：“可于里（《广记》作屋，曾慥《类说》同）东掘地，取吾宝剑，当令汝富，然不得改旧业。”就如其言，果获之，逾年遂富。后泄其事，于是失剑。（《广记》卷二百八十一，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    　　○董昌

    　　董昌未遇前，有山阴县老人伪上言于昌曰：“今大王善政及人，愿万岁帝为越，以福兆庶。三十年前，已有谣言，正合今日，故来献。其言曰：‘欲识圣人姓，千里草青青；欲知圣人名，日从曰上生。’”昌得之大喜，因读曰：“天命早已归我，我为天子矣。”乃赠老人百缣，仍免其征赋。先遣道士朱思远，立坛醮上帝。忽一夕云，天符降于雨中，有碧纸朱书，其文人不可识。思远言：“天命合兴董氏。”又有王守贞者，俗谓之王百艺，极机巧。初立生祠，雕刻形像、塑绘宫嫔，及设兵卫，状若鬼神，皆百艺所为也。

    Explanation

    2

    ○ Vang Ju

    A butcher named Vang Ju in Shuchun was extremely poor. Once, he dreamed of a person who introduced himself as Lian Po, saying to Vang Ju, "You can dig in the east of your village to find my precious sword. It will make you wealthy, but you must not change your occupation." Vang Ju followed his instructions and indeed found the sword. After a year, he became wealthy. Later, when he revealed the story, he lost the sword.

    ○ Dong Chang

    Before Dong Chang rose to power, an elderly man from Shanyin County pretended to tell him, "Your great virtue and good governance have reached the people. I wish you would reign for ten thousand years as the ruler of Yue, bringing blessings to the people. Thirty years ago, there was a prophecy that matches today's situation, so I came to offer it. The prophecy says: 'To know the name of the sage, look at the grass that is a thousand miles long; to know the name of the sage, look at the sun rising from the east.' Dong Chang was very pleased and read it as, 'Heaven has already decreed that the throne should belong to me, and I am destined to be the emperor.' He then rewarded the old man with a hundred bolts of silk and exempted him from taxes. He first sent the Taoist priest Zhu Siyuan to set up an altar and perform a ritual to worship the supreme deity. One night, a divine message descended in the rain, written on blue paper with red ink, which no one could understand. Zhu Siyuan said, "The Mandate of Heaven supports the rise of the Dong family." There was also a man named Wang Shouzhen, commonly known as Wang Baiyi, who was extremely skilled and ingenious. Initially, he built a shrine for Dong Chang, carving images of deities, painting palace attendants, and setting up guards that looked like ghosts and gods, all created by Wang Baiyi.

    3

    妖伪之际，尤兴百艺幻惑之术。昌每言：“我闻‘兔子上金床’，谶我也。我卯生，来岁属卯，二月二日亦卯，即卯年卯月卯日，仍当以卯时，万世之业利在于此。”乾宁二年二月二日，率军俗数万人，僭衮冕仪卫，登子城门楼，赦境内，改伪号罗平国，年号天册，自称圣人。及令官属将校等，皆呼圣人万岁，俯而曰言云云，毕，复欲舞蹈，昌乃连声止之，曰：“卿道得这许多言语，压得朕头疼无奈何也。”盖缘工人所制平天冠稍重，故有是言也。时人闻者皆大笑之。（《广记》卷二百九十引《会稽典录》，当删。因系原本误收，姑存以备考）

    Explanation

    3

    During a time of chaos and false pretenses, various arts of illusion and deception especially flourished. The speaker often said, "I heard the prophecy 'a rabbit on a golden bed,' which means I am the subject of the prophecy. I was born in the hour of the rabbit, and next year will also be the year of the rabbit, and the second day of the second month is also the hour of the rabbit, so it will be in the hour of the rabbit. The benefit for the millennia lies in this." In the second year of the Tianning reign, on the second day of the second month, the speaker led tens of thousands of soldiers and civilians, wearing the ceremonial robes and insignia of a high official, ascended the city gate tower, proclaimed amnesty throughout the domain, changed the false title to the state of Luo Ping and the era name to Tian Ce, and proclaimed himself a sage. Those present called out "Long live the sage!" The speaker bowed and said various things, and when he finished, he wanted to dance, but the speaker loudly stopped him, saying, "You've said so many words, it's pressing on my head and I can't help it." This was because the hat made by the craftsmen was a bit heavy. Those who heard it all laughed at him.

    4

    ○熊博

    　　熊博者，本建安津吏。岸崩出（《广记》作“得”）一古冢，藤蔓缠其棺，傍有石铭云：“欲陷不陷被藤缚，欲落不落被沙阁，五百年后遇熊博。”博使平光寺（四字《广记》作“时贫老”三字）僧为率钱葬之。博后至建州刺史。（《广记》卷三百九十二）

    　　○彭城佛寺

    　　国初杨汀自言，天祐初（《广记》作“某”）在彭城避暑于佛寺，雨雹方甚，忽闻大声震地，走视门下（《广记》作外），乃下一大雹于街中，其高广与寺楼等，入地可丈余。顷之，雨止，则炎风赫日。经月雹乃消尽。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    4

    ○Xiong Bo

    Xiong Bo, originally a customs officer from Jian'an, had an ancient tomb revealed when the bank collapsed. A vine wrapped around the coffin, and beside it was a stone inscription that read: "Wishing to sink but not sinking, bound by vines; wishing to fall but not falling, held by sand; five hundred years later, to meet Xiong Bo." Xiong Bo ordered the monks of Pingguang Temple to lead the fundraising for the burial. Later, Xiong Bo became the governor of Jianzhou. (From the Guangji Volume 392)

    ○The Buddhist Temple in Pengcheng

    During the early years of the Tianyou era, Yang Ting said that he was seeking refuge from the heat in a Buddhist temple in Pengcheng. At that time, a severe hailstorm was occurring, and a loud thunderclap shook the ground. He rushed outside to see a large hailstone fall in the street. Its height and width were equal to the temple tower, and it left a hole in the ground that was over ten feet deep. Soon after, the rain stopped, and the hot winds and blazing sun returned. After a month, the hail finally melted away. (From the Guangji Volume 395)

    5

    ○欧阳氏

    　　广陵孔目吏欧阳某者，居决守寺之前。其妻少遇乱失其父母，至是有老父诣门，使白其妻“我汝父也。”妻见其贫陋，不悦，拒绝之。父又言其名字及中外亲族甚悉，妻竟不听。又曰：“吾自远来，今无所归矣，若尔，权寄门下信宿，可乎？”妻又不从，其夫劝（《广记》有之字），又不可。父乃曰（《广记》曰字在去字下）：“去吾将讼尔矣。”左右以为公（毛本误作“何”）讼耳，亦不介意。明日午，暴风雨从南方来，有（毛本误作自）震霆入欧阳氏之居，牵其妻至中庭，击杀之。大水平地数尺，邻里皆漂（《广记》作“震”）荡不自持。后数日，欧阳之人至后土庙神座前得一书，即老父讼女文也。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    5

    The Ouyang Family:

    In Guangling, there was a clerk named Ouyang who lived in front of the Deciding and Guarding Temple. His wife, when she was young, lost her parents in the chaos. One day, an old man came to their door and asked the clerk to tell his wife, "I am your father." The wife, seeing that he was poor and unattractive, was not pleased and refused him. The old man then said, "I know your name and your family's lineage very well." But the wife still did not listen. He then said, "If you refuse me, I will sue you." The people around thought he was just making a threat and did not take it seriously. The next day, a violent storm came from the south. A bolt of lightning struck the Ouyang household, pulling the wife into the courtyard and killing her. The flood waters rose several feet above the ground, sweeping away the neighbors and leaving them helpless. Several days later, a person from the Ouyang family found a book at the altar of the Earth God temple. The book was the old man's complaint against his daughter.

    6

    ○庐山卖油者

    　　庐山下卖油者，养其母甚孝谨。为暴雷震死，其母自以无罪，日号泣于九天使者之祠，愿知其故。一夕，梦绯（《广记》作“朱”）衣人告曰：“汝子恒以鱼膏杂油中，以图厚利。且庙中斋醮常（《广记》作“恒”）用其（《广记》作“此”）油，腥气薰蒸，灵仙不降。其（《广记》无“其”字）震死宜矣。”母知其事，遂止。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    　　○李诚

    　　江南军使苏建雄，有别墅在毗陵，常（《广记》作“恒”）使傔人李诚来往检事（《广记》作“视”）。乙卯岁（案：乙卯当周显德二年）六月，诚自墅中回，至句容县西，时盛暑赫日，持伞自覆，忽起（《广记》作“值”）大风，飞沙（《广记》作“石”）拔木，卷其伞盖而去，惟持伞柄，行数十步，雷（《广记》作“云”）雨大至，方忧濡湿，忽有飘席至其所，因取覆之。

    Explanation

    6

    Translation

    The Oil Seller of Mount Lu

    A man who sold oil lived at the foot of Mount Lu. He was very filial and respectful to his mother. One day, he was struck dead by a violent thunderbolt. His mother, believing herself to be innocent, wept daily at the temple of the Nine Heavenly Messengers, wishing to know the reason for his death. One night, she dreamed of a person dressed in red (or vermilion) clothing who told her, "Your son always mixed fish fat into the oil to gain greater profit. Moreover, the temple often used this oil for rituals and offerings. The stench of fish fat was so strong that it prevented the spirits from descending. It was fitting that he was struck dead." Upon learning this, the mother stopped the practice. (From The Record of the Supernatural, Volume 395)

    Li Cheng

    Su Jianxiong, a military governor in southern China, had a villa in Piling (modern-day Changzhou). He often sent his servant Li Cheng to check on matters. In the sixth month of the year 955 CE, Li Cheng returned from the villa and reached the western part of Jurong County. It was a hot summer day, and he carried an umbrella to shield himself. Suddenly, he encountered a strong wind that carried sand (or stones) and uprooted trees, carrying away his umbrella. He only held the umbrella handle and walked several steps. A heavy rain and thunderstorm suddenly arrived, and he was worried about getting wet. Suddenly, a floating mat arrived there, and he took it and used it to cover himself.

    7

    俄而，雷震地道傍数家之中，卷去（《广记》无“去”字）一家屋室，向东北而去。顷之，震（《广记》“震”字作“遂霁”二字）。其居荡然无复遗者，老幼十余皆聚桑林中，一无所伤。舍前有足迹，长三尺。诚又西行数里，遇一人求买所覆席，即与之。复（《广记》作“又”）里余后（《广记》作“复”）遇一人，求买所持伞柄，诚乃异之，曰：“此物无用，尔何为者乃（《广记》作“而”）买之？”其人但求乞甚切，终不言其故，随行数百步，与之，乃去。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    7

    Soon after, a thunderstorm struck an underground passage near several houses, rolling away the entire house of one family, carrying it off to the northeast. Shortly thereafter, the storm subsided (in some versions, "震" is replaced with "遂霁," meaning "it then cleared up"). The dwelling place was completely destroyed, leaving nothing behind, yet the family of more than ten members, including the elderly and children, gathered in a mulberry grove, unharmed. There were footprints in front of the house, each three feet long. Cheng then walked several miles westward, where he encountered a person who asked to buy the cover of a mat, and he gave it to him. A little further on, he met another person who asked to buy the handle of an umbrella. Cheng found this strange and said, "This thing is useless. Why are you buying it?" The person only begged very earnestly, never explaining the reason, and followed him for several hundred steps before he gave it to him and they parted ways. (From Volume 395 of the "Guangji")

    8

    ○茅山牛

    　　庚寅岁（曾慥《类说》作大和中。案：庚寅为唐长兴元年，当吴大和二年），有（《广记》“有”字在“山”字下）茅山村中儿牧牛，洗所著汗衫，曝于草上而假寐。及觉（《广记》作“寤”），失之，惟一邻儿在傍，以为窃去，因相喧竞。邻儿父见之，怒曰：“生儿为盗，将安用汝？”（《广记》作“之”）即投水中，邻儿匍匐出水，呼天称冤者不已（《广记》“不已”作“数四”，曾慥《类说》同）。复欲投之。俄而，雷雨暴至，震死其牛，汗衫乃自牛口中呕出，儿乃得免。（《广记》卷三百九十五，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    8

    A Calf in Mount Mao

    In the year of Gengyin (930 CE, the first year of the Longxing era during the Later Tang dynasty, corresponding to the second year of the Dahu period in the Wu state), there was a child in a village in Mount Mao who was herding a calf. The child washed his damp shirt and laid it out on the grass, then dozed off briefly. When he woke up, the calf was gone, and only a neighboring child was nearby. The child thought the calf had been stolen and began to argue loudly with the neighbor. The father of the neighboring child saw this and became angry, saying, "Your child is a thief; what use is he to you?" He then threw his son into the water. The child struggled to get out, repeatedly crying out in distress. The father tried to throw him back in. Suddenly, a violent storm broke out, and the calf was struck by lightning and died. The damp shirt was then vomited out of the calf's mouth, and the child was saved. (This story is recorded in volume 395 of the "Guangji" and also in Zeng Zao's "Lishuo.")

    9

    ○番禺村女

    　　庚申岁（案：庚申当宋建隆元年），番禺村有老姥与其女饷田。忽云雨晦冥，及霁，乃失其女。姥号哭，求访，邻里相与寻之不能得。后月余，复云雨昼晦，及霁，而庭中陈列筵席，有鹿脯、乾鱼、果实、酒醢，甚丰腆（《广记》作“洁”）。其女盛服而至。姥惊喜持之，女自言，为雷师所娶，将至一石室中，亲族甚众，婚姻之礼，一同人间。今使归返，而（《广记》作“面”）他日不可再归矣。姥问：“雷郎可得见耶？”曰：“不可得。”（《广记》无“得”字）留数宿，一夕复风雨晦冥，遂不可（《广记》“可”作“复”）见矣。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    9

    The Girl of Fanyu Village

    In the year of Gengshen (which corresponds to the first year of the Song Dynasty, Jianlong), there was an elderly woman and her daughter in Fanyu Village who went to the fields to provide food for the workers. Suddenly, dark clouds and rain appeared, and when the rain cleared, her daughter had disappeared. The old woman cried out in grief and searched for her, but the neighbors could not find her. After more than a month, dark clouds and rain appeared again during the day, and when the rain cleared, a banquet was set up in the courtyard with venison jerky, dried fish, fruits, and alcoholic condiments, all very abundant and rich. Her daughter arrived in fine attire. The old woman was overjoyed and held her daughter. The daughter said that she had been taken by a thunder god, who was taking her to a stone chamber, where there were many relatives, and the marriage rituals were the same as in human society. She was now being sent back, but she would not be able to return again. The old woman asked, "Can I see the Thunder Lord?" The daughter replied, "No, you cannot." (In the Guangji, the word "得" is omitted.) She stayed for several nights, and one night, dark clouds and rain appeared again, and she was no longer seen. (From Guangji, Volume 395)

    10

    ○江西村妪

    　　江西村中雷震，一老妪为电火所烧，一臂尽伤。即而，空中有呼曰：“误矣。”即坠一瓶，瓶有药如膏，曰：“以此傅之，即瘥。”（《广记》作“差”）妪（《广记》无“妪”字）如其言，随傅而愈。家人共议此神丹（《广记》作“药”）也，将取藏之，数人共举其瓶不能动。顷之，复有雷雨，摄（《广记》作“收”）之而去。又有一（《广记》无“一”字）村人亦（《广记》无“亦”字）震死，（《广记》有“既而”二字）空中人呼曰：“误矣。可急（《广记》无“急”字）取蚯蚓，捣烂傅（《广记》作“覆”，曾慥《类说》同）脐中，当瘥。”如言傅之乃（《广记》作遂）苏。（《广记》卷三百九十五，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    10

    An Old Woman from Jiangxi Village

    In a village in Jiangxi, a thunderclap struck, and an old woman was burned by the electric fire, severely injuring one of her arms. Immediately after, a voice called out from the air, saying, "A mistake has been made." A bottle then fell from the sky, containing a medicine-like ointment, which said, "Apply this to her, and she will recover." (In the Guangji, it is written as "recover.") The old woman (the Guangji omits the word "old woman") followed the instructions, and she recovered instantly. Her family discussed the miraculous medicine (the Guangji writes it as "medicine"), intending to take and store it. Several people tried to lift the bottle but could not move it. Soon after, another thunderstorm came, and the bottle was taken away. Another villager (the Guangji omits the word "villager") was also killed by the thunder. (The Guangji adds the words "soon after.") A voice from the air called out, saying, "A mistake has been made. Quickly take earthworms, grind them into a paste, and apply it to the navel, and he will recover." Following the instructions, the villager revived. (This is recorded in volume 395 of the Guangji and also cited in Zeng Zao's Leishuo.)

    11

    ○甘露寺

    　　道士范可保，夏月独游浙西甘露寺，出殿后门，将登北轩。忽有人，衣故褐衣，自其傍入，肩帔相拂。范素好洁，新衣恐污（四字《广记》作“衣新服”三字），心不悦。俄而，牵一黄犬（《广记》作“狗”），又摩（《广记》作“驾”）肩而出。范怒形于色，褐衣回顾张目，其光如电，范始畏惧。顷之，山下人至，曰：“向者（《广记》无“者”字）山上（《广记》作“下”）霹雳取龙，子闻（《广记》“子”作“不”，“闻”“作”“知”）之乎？”范固不知（《广记》作“闻”）也。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    11

    Translation:

    The Temple of Sweet Dew

    Taoist priest Fan Kebao was strolling alone in the Temple of Sweet Dew in western Zhejiang during the summer. He stepped out of the back door of the hall and was about to ascend to the northern pavilion. Suddenly, a person appeared, wearing old coarse clothing, and entered from the side, brushing against his shoulder and cloak. Fan, who was always fond of cleanliness, was concerned that his new clothes might be soiled, and he was displeased. Soon after, the person dragged a yellow dog and brushed past him again. Fan's anger showed on his face. The person with the coarse clothing turned back, widened his eyes, and his gaze was like lightning. Fan began to fear. Shortly after, a person from the mountain below approached and said, "Did you hear about the thunderbolt that captured a dragon on the mountain just now?" Fan still did not know about it.

    12

    ○南康县令

    　　辛酉（案：辛酉当宋建隆二年）五月四日，有使过南康县，令胡侃置酒于县南莲华馆水轩。忽有暴雨（《广记》作“风”）吹沙从南来，因手掩目，闻盘中器物蔌蔌有声，若物飞（《广记》“物飞”作“有物”）过。良久，开目，见食器微反（《广记》作“仄”）。其银酒杯与杯之舟皆狭长。时东西影壁傍有大桐树，亦拔出，投于（《广记》“投于”二字作“墙外时”三字）一里外，皆此风雨。常遥闻馆中迅雷，而馆中初不闻也。胡亦无恙。（《广记》卷三百九十五）

    Explanation

    12

    On the day of Xin You (which corresponds to the second year of the Jianlong era, 961 CE), on the fourth day of the fifth month, an envoy passed through Nankang County. The magistrate, Hu Kan, prepared a feast at the Water Pavilion of the Lotus Pavilion. Suddenly, there was a strong wind (or possibly heavy rain, according to the variant reading in "Guang Ji") that blew sand from the south. He covered his eyes and heard a rustling sound from the dishes on the table, as if something had flown past. After a while, he opened his eyes and saw that the tableware was slightly overturned. The silver wine cups and their bases were all narrow and long. There was a large梧桐 tree (梧桐 tree) by the shadow wall, which was uprooted and thrown outside the wall, about one li away. The distant sound of thunder was often heard in the pavilion, but initially, no noise was heard inside the pavilion. The magistrate was also unharmed.

    13

    ○犬吠石

    　　婺源县有大黄石，自山坠于溪侧，莹彻可爱。群犬见而竞吠之，数日，村人不堪其喧，乃相与推致水中，犬又俯水而吠。愈急取而碎之，犬乃不吠。（《广记》卷三百九十八）

    　　○瓮形石

    　　潘祚为鄱阳令，县治（《广记》“令县”作“县令”，无“治”字）后连带石城，其中隙荒数十亩。祚尝还家，望月于此，见城下草中有光，高数丈，其间荆棘蒙密，不可夜行，即取弓射其处以志之。明日，掘其地，得一瓮，大腹小口，青石塞之。祚命舁归其家，发其口，不可开，令击碎之，乃一石，如瓮之形，若冰冻之凝结者，复碎而弃之，讫无所得。（《广记》卷三百九十八）

    Explanation

    13

    Barking Stone

    In Wuyuan County, there was a large yellow stone that fell from the mountain to the side of the stream. It was clear and lovely. When the dogs saw it, they barked at it together. After several days, the villagers could not bear the noise, so they pushed it into the water together. The dogs then bent over the water and barked. They became more urgent and took it to break it, and the dogs then stopped barking. (From Guangji, Volume 398)

    Jar-Shaped Stone

    Pan Zu served as the magistrate of Poyang County. The administrative center of the county was connected to a stone wall, with several acres of vacant land in between. Once, Pan Zu returned home and looked at the moon here. He saw a light in the grass below the wall, several meters high. The area was thorny and dense, making it difficult to pass at night. He immediately took an arrow and shot at the spot to mark it. The next day, they dug up the ground and found a jar. It had a large belly and a small mouth, blocked with a green stone. Pan Zu ordered it to be carried back to his home. When they tried to open the mouth, they could not. He ordered it to be broken, and it was a stone, shaped like a jar, like ice that had frozen and solidified. It was broken again and discarded, and nothing was found. (From Guangji, Volume 398)

    14

    ○金蚕

    　　右千牛兵（毛本作“抚”）曹王文秉，丹阳人，世善刻石。其祖尝为浙西廉使裴璩采碑于积石之下，得一自然圆石，如球形。式（毛本作“试”）加砻斫，乃重叠如壳相包，斫之至尽，其大如拳。破视之（三字《广记》作“复破之”），中有一蚕，如蛴螬，蠕蠕能动，人不能识，因弃之。数年，浙西乱，王出奔，至蜀下，与乡人夜会，语及青蚨（毛本“青蚨”二字空阙）西送（《广记》无“送”字）还钱事。坐中或云“人欲求富，莫如得石中金蚕蓄之，则宝货自至（《广记》作“致”）矣。”问其形状，则石中蛴螬也。（《广记》卷三百九十八）

    Explanation

    14

    The Golden Silkworm

    The Righteous Guard of a Thousand Oxen, Cao Wang Wenbing, a native of Danyang, was skilled in carving stone for generations. His ancestor once served as a censor in the western region of Zhejiang under Pei Qu, who collected inscriptions from a rocky area. There, he discovered a naturally formed round stone, shaped like a ball. After attempting to carve it (or testing it), the stone revealed itself to be overlapping like shells embracing each other. Carving it until it was completely gone, the stone was as large as a fist. When it was broken open (or broken again, according to some versions), there was a silkworm inside, resembling a grub, slowly wriggling and able to move. People did not recognize it and discarded it. Several years later, when the western region of Zhejiang fell into chaos, Cao Wang fled to Shu, where he met with his fellow villagers at night. They discussed a certain insect (or the insect) that was sent westward (or to the west) for the purpose of returning money. One of them said, "If one wishes to seek wealth, there is nothing better than obtaining a golden silkworm from within a stone and keeping it, for then treasure will come by itself (or be brought about)." When asked about its shape, it was described as a grub in the stone. (From Volume 398 of the Guangji.)

    15

    ○濠州井

    　　戊子岁（案：戊子当唐天成三年），大旱。濠州酒肆前，有大井，堙塞积久。至是，酒家召井工陶老，有（毛本作“其”）工人父子应募者，乃子先入，倚锸而死。其父继下，亦卒。观者如堵，无敢复入。引绳出尸，竟不复凿。（《广记》卷三百九十九）

    　　○鸡井

    　　江夏有林主簿，虐而好赌。甚爱一女，好食鸡，里胥日供双鸡。一日，将杀鸡，鸡走，其女自逐之，鸡入舍北枯井中，女亦入井，遂不见。林自往，亦入井不出。俄，井中黑气腾上如炊。其家但临井而哭，无敢入者。有屠儿请入视之，但见大釜，汤涌（《广记》作“沸”）火炽，有人拒其足曰：“事不干汝。”不得入而出。久之，气稍稍而熄。井中惟鸡骨一具，人骨二具。此事（《广记》无“事”字）数闻故老言之，不知其何年也。（《广记》卷三百九十九）

    Explanation

    15

    Translation

    ○濠州井

    In the year of Wu Zi (which corresponds to the third year of Tiancheng during the Tang Dynasty), there was a severe drought. In front of a wine shop in Huaizhou, there was a large well that had been blocked up for a long time. At this point, the wine shop owner summoned an old well-digger named Tao. A worker and his son responded to the call. The son went down first and died leaning on his spade. His father followed and also died. Spectators gathered like a wall, and no one dared to go down again. They used a rope to pull out the bodies, and finally did not resume digging.

    ○鸡井

    In Jiangxia, there was a magistrate named Lin who was cruel and fond of gambling. He very much loved a daughter who liked eating chickens. The village headman daily supplied two chickens. One day, as he was about to kill a chicken, the chicken ran away, and the daughter chased after it herself. The chicken entered the dry well north of the house, and the daughter also went into the well, and then disappeared. Lin went himself and also did not come out of the well. Soon, black smoke rose from the well like cooking fumes. The family stood by the well and wept, and no one dared to go down. A butcher volunteered to go down and see. He saw only a large pot with boiling water and intense fire. Someone blocked his feet and said, "This has nothing to do with you." He could not go in and had to come out. After a while, the smoke gradually dissipated. The well contained only one chicken skeleton and two human skeletons. This story has been heard many times from old people, but it is unknown when it happened.

    16

    ○军井

    　　建州有魏使君宅，兵后焚毁，以为军营。有大井，湮（《广记》作“淀”）塞。壬子岁，军士浚之，入者二人皆卒，尸亦不获。有一人请复入，曰：“以绳缒我，我急（毛本作“亟”）引绳，即（《广记》有“亟”字）出之。”既入，久之，忽掣其（《广记》“掣其”二字作“引”字）绳甚急，即出之，色（《广记》作“已”）如痴矣，良久乃能言，云：“既入井，但见城郭、邑庐（《广记》“邑庐”作“井邑”），人物甚众。其主曰李将军，机务鞅掌府署甚盛。惧而欲（《广记》无“欲”字）遽出。”竟不获二尸。建州留后朱斥，尝奉使镇（四字《广记》作“业使填”三字）此井。（《广记》卷三百九十九）

    Explanation

    16

    ○ Military Well

    In Jianzhou, there was a residence of a high-ranking official named Wei, which was burned down after a war and turned into a military camp. There was a large well that had been blocked (or filled). In the year of Renzi (922 CE), the soldiers dredged the well. Two soldiers entered and both died, and their bodies were not found. One soldier volunteered to go in again, saying, "Tie a rope to me, and if I pull the rope urgently (or quickly), then (or urgently) pull me out." After entering, after a while, suddenly he pulled the rope very urgently, and they pulled him out. His face (or already) looked dazed, and he could speak only after a long time. He said, "After entering the well, I only saw cities, towns, and many people. The master said it was General Li, and his office was very busy and grand. He was afraid and wanted to rush out." They still did not find the two bodies. Zhu Chui, the acting governor of Jianzhou, had once been sent on a mission to fill this well. (Recorded in Volume 399 of the Guangji (Encyclopedia))

    17

    ○金华令

    　　王祝从子某，为金华令，筑私第于邑中。夏，暴雨大至，水忽奔往东南隅，如灌漏卮，顷刻而尽，其地成井，深不可测。以丝絙（《广记》作“籰”）缒石而测之，数十丈乃及底，得一新馒（《广记》作“捻”）头而出（《广记》作“上”）与人间尝（《广记》作“常”）食者，无小异也。（《广记》卷三百九十九）

    Explanation

    17

    The Magistrate of Jinhua

    Wang Zhu's nephew, serving as the magistrate of Jinhua, built a private residence in the town. In the summer, a heavy rainstorm arrived, and the water suddenly rushed to the southeast corner, draining as quickly as water poured into a leaky cup, disappearing in an instant. The area became a well, its depth unfathomable. Using a silk rope with a stone attached, they measured it, reaching the bottom after tens of feet. They retrieved a new steamed bun from the well, which was indistinguishable from those commonly eaten by people. (Volume 399 of the Guangji)

    18

    ○徐善

    　　江南伪中书舍人徐善，幼孤，家于豫章。杨吴之寇（《广记》作“克”）豫章，善之妹为一军校所虏，既定，军校求（《广记》无“求”字）得善请以礼聘之。善自以旧族，不当与戎士为婚，固（《广记》作“因”）不许。乃强纳币焉，悉掷弃之，临以白刃，亦不惧，然竟虏之而去。善即诣扬都，求见吴杨渥而诉之。时渥初嗣，藩服府庭甚严。僭拟王者、布衣游士，旬岁不得一见。而善始至白沙，渥夜梦人来言曰：“江西有秀才徐善将来见公，今在白沙逆旅矣。其人良士也，且有情事未申（《广记》无“未申”二字），公其（《广记》作“可”）厚遇之。”渥（《广记》无“渥”字）旦即遣骑迎之。既至，礼遇甚厚，（《广记》有“且”字）问所欲言，善具白其妹事。渥（《广记》无“渥”字）即命购（《广记》无“购”字）赎，归于徐氏。时歙州刺史陶雅闻而异之，因辟为从事。（《广记》卷二百七十七）

    Explanation

    18

    Xu Shan, a pseudonymous official of the Southern Tang dynasty, was an orphan from a noble family who lived in Yuzhang. During the invasion of Yuzhang by the Yang Wu regime, Xu Shan's sister was captured by a military officer. After the invasion was quelled, the military officer sought to marry Xu Shan's sister according to proper rites. Xu Shan, considering himself of a noble lineage, refused to marry his sister to a military man. The military officer then forced to accept a dowry, but Xu Shan threw it all away. Despite being threatened with a white blade, Xu Shan remained fearless. Nevertheless, the military officer eventually took Xu Shan's sister away.

    Xu Shan then traveled to Yangdu and sought an audience with Wu Yangwo, the ruler of the Yang Wu regime, to plead his sister's case. At the time, Wu Yangwo had just succeeded to the throne, and the court was very strict. Even wise kings and sage emperors required diligent study, let alone common people. It had been ten years since Wu Yangwo had last seen a commoner or wandering scholar. Xu Shan arrived at Bashi, and that night, Wu Yangwo had a dream in which someone told him, "There is a talented scholar named Xu Shan from Jiangxi who will come to see you. He is currently staying at an inn in Bashi. He is a good man and has a matter to report. You should treat him with great respect." The next morning, Wu Yangwo immediately sent a rider to fetch Xu Shan. When Xu Shan arrived, he was received with great respect, and Wu Yangwo asked what he wanted to say. Xu Shan explained the matter of his sister. Wu Yangwo then ordered her to be redeemed and returned to the Xu family. At the time, Tao Ya, the governor of Shezhou, heard of Xu Shan's story and was impressed, appointing him as an assistant.

    19

    ○何致雍

    　　何致雍者，贾人之子也，幼而英爽（《广记》作“爽俊”）好学。尝从其叔父，泊舟皖口。其叔夜梦一人，若官吏，乘马从数仆，来往岸侧，遍阅舟船人物之数。复一人自后呼曰：“何仆射在此，勿惊之。”对曰：“诺。”不敢惊。既寤，遍访邻舟之人，皆无何姓者，乃移舟入深浦中。翌日，大风涛，所泊之舟皆没，惟何氏存。叔父乃谓致雍曰：“我家世贫贱，吾复老矣，‘何仆射’必汝矣（《广记》作“也”），善自爱。”致雍后受（《广记》作“从”）知于湖南为节度判官。会楚王殷自称尊号，以致雍为户部侍郎、翰林学士。致雍自谓当作相，而居师表（《广记》作“长”）之任。后楚王希范嗣立，复去帝号，以致雍为（《广记》“为”字缺）节度判官、检校仆射。竟卒于官。（《广记》卷二百七十八，官作任）

    Explanation

    19

    He Zhiyong, the son of a merchant, was young and spirited, with a love for learning. Once, he traveled with his uncle and docked at Wuan. That night, his uncle had a dream in which he saw a figure resembling an official, riding a horse with several servants, walking along the shore, inspecting the boats and people. Another figure called out from behind, saying, "The Pushe is here, do not startle him." The first figure replied, "Yes." The uncle did not startle him. Upon waking, he searched among the people on nearby boats but found no one named He. He then moved the boat to a deeper part of the harbor. The next day, a fierce storm struck, and all the boats that had been docked were destroyed, except for He Zhiyong's. The uncle then told He Zhiyong, "Our family has always been poor and of low status, and I am old. You will surely become a Pushe, take good care of yourself." Later, He Zhiyong was recognized by the governor of Hunan and appointed as a military governor's assistant. When Prince Yin of Chu proclaimed himself emperor, He Zhiyong was appointed as the Minister of Revenue and a member of the Hanlin Academy. He Zhiyong believed he would become a chancellor and hold a position of leadership. Later, when Prince Xifan of Chu succeeded to the throne and abandoned the imperial title, He Zhiyong was appointed as a military governor's assistant and a temporary Pushe. He eventually died in office.

    20

    ○郭仁表

    　　伪吴春坊吏郭仁表，居冶（《广记》作“治”）城北。甲寅岁，因得疾沉痼，忽梦一（《广记》无“一”字）道士，衣金花紫帔，从一小童，自门入，坐其堂上。仁表初不甚敬，因问疾何时可愈，道士厉色（《广记》作“色厉”）曰：“甚则有之。”既寤，疾甚。数夜，复梦（《广记》有“前”字）道士至，因叩头逊谢。久之，道士色解，索纸笔。仁表以为将疏方，即跪奉之，道士书而授之，其辞曰：“飘风暴雨可思惟，鹤望巢门敛翅飞。吾道之宗正可依，万物之先数在兹，不能行此欲何为？”梦中不晓其义，将问之，童子摇手曰：“不可。”因拜谢。道士自西北而去，因而（《广记》作“尔”）疾愈。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    Explanation

    20

    Deputy Guo Renbiao

    Deputy Guo Renbiao, an official of the Spring Pavilion in the false Wu state, lived in the northern part of the city of Yizheng. In the year of the tiger, he fell ill with a severe and chronic condition and suddenly dreamed of a Taoist wearing a purple robe adorned with golden flowers, followed by a young boy, who entered through the door and sat on the main hall. Initially, Guo Renbiao did not show much respect to the Taoist and asked when his illness would be cured. The Taoist, with a serious expression, replied, "If so, it is possible." After waking up, his illness worsened. Several nights later, he dreamed again of the Taoist arriving. He then knelt and humbly apologized. After some time, the Taoist's expression softened, and he asked for paper and ink. Guo Renbiao thought the Taoist would write a prescription and immediately knelt to present the paper. The Taoist wrote something and gave it to him. The words read: "A stormy wind and heavy rain can be thought of, the crane looks toward the nest and tucks its wings to fly. The root of my path is indeed reliable, the first number among all things is here, if one cannot follow this, what else can be done?" In the dream, Guo Renbiao did not understand the meaning of these words and was about to ask the young boy, but the boy shook his hand, saying, "It is not appropriate." Guo Renbiao then bowed and thanked him. The Taoist left to the northwest, and Guo Renbiao's illness was cured. (From Volume 278 of the Guangji)

    21

    ○王屿

    　　伪吴鄂帅王屿，少为小将，从军围颍州。夜梦道士告之曰：“旦有流星坠地，能避之，当至将相。”明日，众军攻城，城中矢石如雨。屿仗剑，倚栅木而督战，俄有飞（《广记》作“大”）石正中其栅木，及屿，铠甲之半皆糜碎，而屿无伤。因叹曰：“流星正谓（《广记》无“谓”字）尔耶。”由是自负，卒至大官。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    　　○谢谔

    　　进士谢谔，家于南康，舍前有溪，常游戏之所也。谔为儿时，尝梦浴溪中有人以珠一器遗之，曰：“郎吞此则明悟矣。”谔度其大者不可吞，郎吞细者六十余颗。及长，善为诗。进士裴说为选其善者六十余篇，行于世。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    Explanation

    21

    ○ Wang Yu

    The general of Wu, Wang Yu, was a young officer who followed the army to besiege Yingshou. One night, he dreamed that a Taoist priest told him, "In the morning, a meteor will fall to the ground. If you can avoid it, you will become a general or a chancellor." The next day, the army attacked the city, and arrows and stones rained down from the city. Wang Yu stood with his sword, leaning against the palisade wood to oversee the battle. Suddenly, a flying stone hit his palisade wood and him, half of his armor and helmet were shattered, but Wang Yu was unharmed. He then sighed and said, "The meteor was indeed speaking to you." From then on, he became overconfident and eventually became a high-ranking official. (Volume 278 of the Guangji)

    ○ Xie E

    Xie E, a scholar-official, lived in Nankang, with a stream in front of his house, a place where he often played. When he was a child, he once dreamed of bathing in the stream and someone gave him a vessel full of pearls, saying, "If you swallow these, you will become wise and enlightened." Xie E thought the large ones could not be swallowed, so he swallowed over sixty of the smaller ones. When he grew up, he became good at writing poetry. Scholar-official Pei Shuo selected over sixty of his best poems, which circulated in the world. (Volume 278 of the Guangji)

    22

    ○崔万安

    　　江南司农少卿崔万安，分务广陵。尝病苦脾泄，困甚。其家人祷于后土祠。是夕，万安梦一妇人，珠珥珠履，衣五重，皆编贝玉（《广记》作“珠”）为之。谓万安曰：“此病（《广记》作“疾”）可治，今以一方相与。可取青木香、肉豆蔻等分，枣肉为丸米，饮下二十丸。”又云：“此药大（《广记》作“太”）热，疾平即止。”如其言服之，遂愈。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    　　○江南李令
    　　江南有李令者，累任大邑，假秩至评事，世乱年老，无复宦情，筑室于广陵法云寺之西，为终焉之计。尝梦束草加首，口衔一刀，两手各持一刀，入水而行，意甚异之。俄而，孙儒陷广陵，儒部将李琼屯兵于法云寺，恒止李令家，父事令。及儒死，宣城裨将马殷、刘建封辈率众南走，琼因强令俱行。及殷据湖南，琼为桂管观察使，用令为荔浦令，则前梦之验也。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    Explanation

    22

    Translation

    Cui Wanan

    Cui Wanan, the Deputy Director of Agriculture in the Southern Region, was stationed in Guangling. He once suffered severely from spleen diarrhea. His family prayed at the Temple of the Earth God. That night, Cui Wanan dreamed of a woman adorned with pearl earrings and pearl shoes, wearing five layers of clothing, all made of woven jade and pearls. She said to Cui Wanan, "This illness can be treated. Here is a prescription for you. Take equal parts of asafoetida and nutmeg, make pills with jujube flesh, and take twenty pills with water." She also warned, "This medicine is very hot; stop taking it once the disease is cured." Following her instructions, he took the medicine and was cured. (From The Collected Records Volume 278)

    Li Ling of the Southern Region

    In the Southern Region, there was a man named Li Ling who had held various high-ranking positions, temporarily reaching the rank of a censor. Due to the chaotic times and his old age, he had lost interest in official career. He built a house west of Fayun Temple in Guangling, planning for a final resting place. He once dreamed of having a bundle of grass on his head, holding a knife in his mouth, and two knives in each hand, walking into water. He found this dream very strange. Soon after, Sun Ru captured Guangling. Sun Ru's general Li Qiong stationed his troops at Fayun Temple and always stayed at Li Ling's home, treating him like a father. After Sun Ru died, the subordinate generals Ma Yin and Liu Jianfeng led their troops southward. Li Qiong then forced Li Ling to go with them. When Ma Yin took control of Hunan, Li Qiong became the governor of Guilin and appointed Li Ling as the magistrate of Lipu. This fulfilled the prediction of his previous dream. (From The Collected Records Volume 278)

    23

    ○毛贞辅

    　　伪吴毛贞辅，累为邑宰，应选之广陵。梦吞日，既寤，腹犹热。以问侍御史杨廷式，杨曰：“此梦至大，非君所能当。若当君而言，当得赤乌场官也。”果如其言。（《广记》卷二百七十八）

    　　○陆洎

    　　江南陆洎为常州刺史，不克之任，为淮南副使。性和雅重厚，时辈推仰之。副使李承嗣，与之尤（《广记》“尤”字在“与”字上）善。乙丑岁（案：乙丑当宋乾德三年）九月，承嗣与诸客访之，洎从容曰：“某明年此月当与诸君（《广记》作“客”）别矣。”承嗣问其故，答曰：“吾向梦人以一骑召去，（六字毛本作“一骑兵以召去”）止大明寺西可数里，至一大府，署曰阳明府。入门西序，复由东向大门下马，入一室中（《广记》无“中”字）。久之，吏引至阶下。门中有二绿衣吏，捧一案，案上有书。

    Explanation

    23

    Translation

    Mao Zhenfu

    Mao Zhenfu of the Wu regime repeatedly served as a county magistrate and was selected for a position in Guangling. He dreamed of swallowing the sun; upon waking, his abdomen was still warm. He consulted the censor Yang Tingshi, who said, "This dream is very significant, not something you can bear. If I were to interpret it for you, you will become an official at the Chìwū field." Indeed, this came to pass. (From The Complete Collection of Stories Volume 278)

    Lu Ji

    Lu Ji of Jiangnan was appointed as the governor of Changzhou but did not take up the position, instead becoming the deputy governor of Huainan. He was gentle, refined, and serious, and was respected and admired by his contemporaries. The deputy governor Li Chengsi, who was particularly close to him, visited him in September of the year 965 CE (Cànghé 三年). Lu Ji calmly said, "I will part ways with you all next month." Li Chengsi asked why, and Lu Ji replied, "I recently dreamed that someone came on horseback to take me away, stopping a few miles west of Daming Temple. I arrived at a large hall, which was named Yangming Hall. I entered through the west wing and then dismounted at the east gate, entering a room. After a while, an official led me to the steps below. There were two officials wearing green robes, holding a table with a book on it."

    24

    一紫衣秉笏取书，宣云：‘洎三世为人，皆行慈孝，功成业就，宜（毛本“就”作“宽”，“宜”作“并”）受此官。可封阳明府侍郎，判九州都监事。来年九月十七日，本府上事。’复以骑送归，奄然遂寤。灵命已定，不可改矣。”诸客皆默（《广记》作“嘻”）。然至明年九月，日使候其起居。及十六日，承嗣复与向客候之（《广记》有“客诣之”三字），谓曰：“明日君（《广记》“君”字在“明”字上）当上事，今何无恙也？”洎曰：“府中已办，明当行也。”承嗣曰：“吾尝（《广记》作‘常’）以长者重君，今无乃近妖乎？”洎曰：“惟君与我有缘，他日必当卜邻。”承嗣默然而去。明日遂卒，葬于茱萸湾。承嗣后为楚州刺史，卒，葬于洎墓之北云。（《广记》卷二百七十九）

    　　○周延翰

    Explanation

    24

    A purple-robed official took a tablet and read out: "Since three generations, the family has practiced kindness and filial piety. Upon completing their tasks, they should be granted this position. They shall be appointed as the Deputy of Yangming Prefecture and the Inspector of the Nine Provinces. The appointment will take effect next year on the seventeenth day of September." The official then sent a rider to escort the person back home, and suddenly, the person awakened. Fate has been decided and cannot be changed. All the guests were silent (or perhaps sighed). The following year, on September sixteenth, Cengshi and the former guest visited him again. The guest said, "Tomorrow you will take office, why do you seem so well?" Jiu replied, "The office has been prepared, I will leave tomorrow." Cengshi said, "I always respected you as a senior, but now you seem to be near something ominous." Jiu said, "Only you and I have a connection, we will surely become neighbors in the future." Cengshi left in silence. The next day, Jiu died and was buried in Zhuyu Bay. Cengshi later became the Prefect of Chu Prefecture and died, being buried to the north of Jiu's tomb.

    25

    江南太子校书周延翰，性好道，颇修服饵之事。尝梦神人以一卷书示（《广记》作“授”）之，若道家之经，其文皆七字为句，惟记其末句云“紫髯之伴（《广记》作“畔”）有丹砂”。延翰寤而自喜，以为必得丹砂之效。后（《广记》无“后”字）从事建业，卒，葬于吴大帝陵侧，无妻子，惟一婢名丹砂。（《广记》卷二百七十九。按：据李剑国考证，《广记》明钞本引作（稽神录》，谈本讹作《广异记》）

    　　○王瞻

    　　处（《广记》作“虔”）化县令王瞻，罢任归建业，泊舟秦淮。病甚，梦朱衣吏执牒至曰：“君命已尽，今奉召。”瞻曰：“命不敢辞，但舟中隘狭，欲宽假之，使得登岸卜居，无所惮也。”吏许诺，以五日为期，曰：（《广记》无“曰”字）“至期，平旦（《广记》作“明”）当来也。”既寤，便能下床，自出僦舍，营办凶具。教其子哭踊之节，召六亲为别。至期，登榻安卧，向曙乃卒。（《广记》卷二百七十九）

    Explanation

    25

    Translation

    The royal scholar Zhou Yanhan from the southern region, fond of Daoism, often practiced the use of elixirs and potions. Once, he dreamed of a divine being presenting (or giving) him a scroll of text, which was like a Daoist scripture. The text was composed of seven-character lines, and he only remembered the last sentence which said, "The companion of the purple beard has cinnabar" (or "the purple beard's side has cinnabar"). Upon waking, Yanhan was pleased with himself, believing that he would surely achieve the effects of cinnabar. Later, he served as an official in Jianye and died, being buried beside the tomb of Wu's Great Emperor. He had no wife or children, only a maid named Dan Sha.

    Translation

    The magistrate of Chuchuan (or Qianchuan) County, Wang Zhan, resigned from his post and returned to Jianye, docking his boat on the Qinhuai River. He was very ill and dreamed of a red-clad official holding a document and saying, "Your life has come to an end, and now you are summoned." Zhan replied, "I dare not refuse my fate, but the boat is cramped. I wish to be given some respite so that I can go ashore and find a place to live, without any fear." The official agreed, setting a period of five days, and said, "On the appointed day, at dawn (or early morning), you will come." After waking up, Zhan was able to get out of bed, went out to rent a room, and arranged for funeral preparations. He taught his son the rituals of mourning and called his relatives to bid farewell. On the appointed day, he climbed onto his bed and lay down peacefully, dying just before dawn.

    26

    ○邢陶

    　　江南大理司直邢陶，癸卯岁（按，癸卯当南唐保大元年），梦人告云：“君当为泾州刺史。”既而，为宣州泾县令。考满，复梦其人告云：“宣州诸县官人，来春皆替，而君官诰不到。”邢甚恶之。至明年春，罢归。有荐陶（《广记》作“邢”）为水部员外郎，牒下，而所司失去，复请二十余日，竟未拜而卒。（《广记》卷二百七十九）

    　　●卷二

    　　○紫石

    　　晋安有东山，樵人陈某（《广记》作“氏”），恒见山中有紫光烛天。伺之久，乃见一大鹿，光自口出。设置捕而获之，刳其腹，得一紫石，圆莹如珠。因宝藏之，家自是富。至其孙，奢纵好酒，醉而玩其珠，以为石何能神，因击碎之，家自是贫矣。（《广记》卷四百四十三）

    Explanation

    26

    Translation

    Xing Tao

    In the year Gui Mao (which corresponds to the first year of the Bao Da era during the Southern Tang dynasty), Jiangnan's Judicial Censor Xing Tao had a dream in which someone told him, "You will become the Governor of Jingzhou." Soon after, he was appointed as the County Magistrate of Jing County in Xuanchou Prefecture. After completing his term, he dreamed again that the same person told him, "All officials in the various counties of Xuanchou will be replaced next spring, but your official decree will not arrive." Xing Tao was greatly distressed by this. By the following spring, he was dismissed and returned home. Someone recommended Xing Tao (as recorded in the Guang Ji) to be appointed as Assistant Minister of Water Affairs. The official document was issued, but the office lost it. After waiting for more than twenty days, he never took office and died.

    Purple Stone

    In Jin'an, there is Dongshan Mountain. A woodcutter named Chen (as recorded in the Guang Ji) often saw a purple light illuminating the sky from the mountain. After watching for a long time, he finally saw a large deer with the light emanating from its mouth. He set up a trap and caught it. Upon opening its stomach, he found a purple stone, round and lustrous like a pearl. He kept it as a treasure, and his family became wealthy as a result. By the time it came to his grandson, who was extravagant and loved drinking, he played with the stone while drunk, thinking that a stone could not be so powerful. He smashed it, and his family became poor as a result.

    27

    ○杨迈

    　　司农卿杨迈，少好畋猎。自云：在长安时，放鹰于野，遥见草中一兔跳跃，鹰亦自见，即奋往搏之。既至，无有。收鹰上鞲，行数十步，回顾其处，复见其兔（《广记》无“其”字，“兔下”有“走”字）。又搏之，亦不获，如是者三。即命芟草以求之，得兔骨一具，盖兔之鬼也。（《广记》卷四百四十三，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    　　○舒州人

    　　舒州有人入灊山，见大蛇，击杀之。视之有足，甚以为异，因负之而（《广记》无“而”字）出，将以示人。遇县吏数人于路，因告之曰：“我杀此蛇而有四足。”吏皆不见，曰：“蛇何在？”曰：“在尔前，何故不见？”即弃蛇于地，乃见之。于是负此蛇者，皆不见，人以为怪，乃弃之。按，此蛇生（《广记》作“至”）不能自隐其形，死乃能隐人之形，此理有不可穷者。（《广记》卷四百五十九）

    Explanation

    27

    Translation:

    Yang Mai

    The Minister of Agriculture, Yang Mai, enjoyed hunting in his youth. He once recounted that while in Chang'an, he released an eagle into the wild. From afar, he saw a rabbit jumping in the grass, and the eagle also saw it, then rushed forward to attack it. Upon arrival, there was nothing there. He retrieved the eagle onto his wrist, walked dozens of steps, looked back at the place, and saw the rabbit again (in the Guangji, the character "其" is omitted, and "走" follows "兔"). He attacked it again, but still did not catch it, repeating this three times. He then ordered the grass to be cleared in search of it, and found a set of rabbit bones, which were believed to be the ghost of the rabbit. (Guangji vol. 413, also cited in Zeng Zao's Leishuo)

    A Man from Shuzhou

    A man from Shuzhou entered Qianshan and saw a large snake, which he killed. Upon examination, he found it had feet, which he considered very strange. He carried it out (in the Guangji, the character "而" is omitted), intending to show it to others. On the road, he encountered several county officials, to whom he said, "I killed this snake, and it had four feet." The officials all claimed not to see it, asking, "Where is the snake?" He replied, "It is right in front of you, why can't you see it?" Immediately, he threw the snake to the ground, and they saw it. Those who carried the snake could no longer see it, and people found this strange, so they abandoned it. According to the record, this snake could not hide its own form while alive, but could hide others' forms when dead. This principle is beyond comprehension. (Guangji vol. 459)

    28

    ○贾潭

    　　伪吴兵部尚书贾潭，言其所知为岭南节度（《广记》有使字），获一橘，其大如升，将表献之，监军中使以为非常物，不可轻进。因取针，微刺其带下，乃有蠕蠕（四字《广记》作乃“蝡”二字）而动者。因（《广记》作“命”）破之，中有一小赤蛇，长数寸。（《广记》卷四百五十九）

    　　○姚景

    　　伪吴寿州节度使姚景，为儿时，事濠州节度使刘金，给使厩中。金尝卒行至内（《广记》作“厩”），见景方寝，有二小赤蛇戏于景面，出入两鼻中，良久，景寤，蛇乃不见。金由是骤加宠擢，妻之以女，卒至大官。（《广记》卷四百五十九）

    　　○王稔

    　　伪吴寿州节度使王稔，罢归扬都，为统军，坐厅事，与客语。忽有小赤蛇，自屋坠地，向稔而蟠。稔令以器覆之，良久，发视，惟一蝙蝠飞去。其年，稔加（毛本作“升”）平章事。（《广记》卷四百五十九）

    Explanation

    28

    ○贾潭

    Pseudo Wu Ministry of War Secretary General Jia Tan reported that the person he knew was the Governor of Lingnan. He obtained an orange, as large as a winnowing basket, and intended to present it as a gift. The imperial censor's envoy considered it an extraordinary object and deemed it inappropriate to present it lightly. He then took a needle, slightly pricked under the band, and there was something wriggling. He then broke it open, and inside there was a small red snake, several inches long. (Volume 459 of the Guangji)

    ○姚景

    Pseudo Wu Governor of Shouzhou Yao Jing, when he was a child, served under the Governor of Haozhou Liu Jin in the stables. Once, Liu Jin suddenly entered the stable and saw Jing sleeping. Two small red snakes were playing on his face, entering and exiting his nostrils. After a while, Jing woke up, and the snakes were gone. Liu Jin, impressed by this, quickly promoted him, married him to his daughter, and eventually appointed him to a high office. (Volume 459 of the Guangji)

    ○王稔

    Pseudo Wu Governor of Shouzhou Wang Ren, after being dismissed and returning to Yangdu, became a general and sat in the hall, talking with guests. Suddenly, a small red snake fell from the roof, coiling towards Ren. Ren ordered a container to cover it. After a while, when he lifted the container, only a bat flew away. That year, Ren was promoted to Chancellor. (Volume 459 of the Guangji)

    29

    ○安陆人

    　　安陆人姓毛，善食毒蛇，以酒吞之。尝游齐安，遂至豫章，恒弄蛇于市，以乞丐为生（《广记》作“事”），积年十余。有卖薪者，自鄱阳来，宿黄培（《广记》作“倍”）山下，梦老父云：“为我寄一蛇与江西弄蛇毛生也。”乃至豫章观步门，卖薪，将尽，有一蛇，苍白色，蟠于船舷，触之不动。薪者方省向梦，即携之至市，访得毛生，因以与之。毛始欲展拨，应手啮其指（《广记》作“乳”），毛失声颠（《广记》作“顿”）仆，遂卒。良久即腐坏，蛇亦不知所在。（《广记》卷四百五十九）

    　　○食虎

    　　建安（《广记》作“中”）山中人（《广记》“人”字在“山”字上）种粟者，皆构棚于高树，以防虎。尝有一人，方升棚，见一虎，垂头榻尾，过去甚速。俄有一兽，如虎而稍小，蹑前虎而去。遂闻竹林中哮吼震地，久之乃寂。明日往视，其虎被食略尽，但存少骨。（《广记》卷四百三十二）

    Explanation

    29

    A Man from Anlu

    A man from Anlu, whose surname was Mao, was skilled in eating venomous snakes, swallowing them with wine. He once traveled to Qi'an and then went to Yuzhang, where he often performed snake tricks in the market and made a living by begging (as recorded in The Collected Tales as "engaging in such activities"). He had been doing this for over ten years. There was a wood seller who came from Poyang, stayed overnight at the foot of Huangpei Mountain (as recorded in The Collected Tales as "Huangbei"), and in his dream, an old man said, "Please deliver a snake to Mao Sheng, the snake handler from Jiangxi, on my behalf." The wood seller then went to the Viewing Gate in Yuzhang, sold his wood, and was nearly finished when he saw a snake, pale and greenish-white, coiled around the side of a boat. When he touched it, it did not move. The wood seller then remembered his dream, took the snake to the market, found Mao, and gave it to him. Mao was just about to handle it when the snake suddenly bit his finger (as recorded in The Collected Tales as "his nipple"), causing Mao to lose his voice and fall over, and he died. After a long time, his body rotted away, and the snake also disappeared (as recorded in The Collected Tales, Volume 459).

    A Man Who Ate a Tiger

    In Jian'an (as recorded in The Collected Tales as "Jian'an Mountain"), there were people who grew millet in the mountains. They all built platforms on tall trees to protect themselves from tigers. Once, a man was just climbing onto the platform when he saw a tiger, its head and tail drooping, pass by very quickly. Soon after, another creature, resembling a tiger but slightly smaller, followed the tiger and left. Then, he heard roaring and ground-shaking sounds coming from the bamboo forest, which lasted for a long time before becoming silent. The next day, when he went to check, the tiger had been mostly eaten, leaving only a few bones (as recorded in The Collected Tales, Volume 432).

    30

    ○鞭牛（《广记》作青牛）

    　　京口居人晚出，见（《广记》“见”在“上”下）江上石公山下，有二青牛，腹青背赤（《广记》作“腹嘴皆红”），戏于水滨。一白衣老翁，长可三丈，执鞭于其旁。久之，翁回顾见人，即鞭二牛入水，翁即跳跃而上，倏忽渐长，一举足径上石公山顶，遂不复见。（《广记》卷四百三十四）

    　　○王姥

    　　广陵有王（《广记》有“氏老”二字）姥，病数日，忽谓其子曰：“我死必生西溪浩氏为牛子，当寻而赎我，腹下有王字是也。”顷之，遂卒。（其）（《广记》无“其”字）西溪者，海（《广记》作“广”）陵之西地名也。其民浩氏，生牛，腹有白毛成王字。其子寻而得之，以束帛赎之以归。（《广记》卷四百三十四，以归作而去）

    Explanation

    30

    Whip the Ox (《广记》作青牛)

    A resident of Jingkou went out late at night and saw, on the river below Shigong Mountain, two blue oxen with blue bellies and red backs, playing by the water. A white-clad old man, about three zhang tall, was holding a whip beside them. After a while, the old man turned around and saw the resident, immediately whipping the two oxen into the water. The old man then leaped into the water and suddenly began to grow, taking one step to the top of Shigong Mountain with a single stride, and then disappeared. (From 《广记》 volume 434)

    Madam Wang

    In Guangling, there was a woman named Wang who had been sick for several days. Suddenly, she told her son, "After I die, I will be reborn as a calf to the Hao family in Xixi. You should look for me and redeem me; there will be a 'Wang' character on my belly." Soon after, she died. Xixi is a place in the west of Haixing (present-day Yangzhou, Jiangsu Province). The Hao family gave birth to a calf with white hair forming the character 'Wang' on its belly. Her son found it and redeemed it with bundles of silk, bringing it back home. (From 《广记》 volume 434)

    31

    ○陈璋

    　　淮南统军陈璋，加平章事，拜命于朝。李昪时执政，谓璋曰：“吾将诣公贺，且求一女婿于公家，公其先归，吾将至。”璋驰一赤骥而去，中路马蹶而坠。顷之，昪至，璋扶疾而出。昪坐少选即去。璋召马数之曰：“吾以今日拜官，又议亲事，尔乃以是而坠我。畜生！不忍杀汝，使牵去，勿与刍秣，饿死之。”是夕圉人窃秣之（《广记》“秣之”作“具刍粟”三字），马视之而已，达旦不食刍（《广记》无“刍”字）。如是累日，圉人以告。璋复召数之曰：“尔既知罪，吾赦尔。”马跳跃而去，是夕乃饮食如故。璋后出镇宣城，罢归而薨，旬月之中，马亦悲鸣而死。（《广记》卷四百三十五）

    Explanation

    31

    Commander of Huainan, Chen Zhang, was promoted to Pingzhangshi and received his appointment in the court. When Li Bian, the founder of the Southern Tang dynasty, was informed of this promotion, he said to Chen Zhang, "I will come to congratulate you and ask for a son-in-law from your family. You should return first, and I will come." Chen Zhang returned on a red horse, but in the middle of the road, the horse stumbled and fell. Shortly after, Li Bian arrived, and Chen Zhang came out with a slight illness. Li Bian sat for a short time and then left. Chen Zhang called the horse and scolded it, saying, "You caused me to fall. Beast! I cannot kill you, but take it away and do not give it any feed. Starve it to death." That night, the stable boy secretly fed the horse. The horse looked at it but did nothing and did not eat feed until dawn. Like this for several days, the stable boy reported this to Chen Zhang. Chen Zhang called the horse and scolded it again, saying, "You have already recognized your fault. I forgive you." The horse jumped away and that night ate and drank as usual. Chen Zhang later went out to govern Xuancheng, retired, and died. Within a month, the horse mourned and died.

    32

    ○吴宗嗣

    　　军使吴宗嗣者，尝有某府吏（《广记》作“父吏某”）从之贷钱二十万，月计利息。一年后不复肯还，求索不可得。宗嗣怒，召而责之曰：“我前世负尔钱，我今还矣。尔负我，当作驴马还我。”因焚券而遣之。逾年，宗嗣独坐厅事，忽见吏白衣而入曰：“某来还债。”宗嗣曰：“已焚券，何用（《广记》作“为”）复偿？”（《广记》作“来”）吏不答，径入厩中，俄而，厩人报马生白驹。使诣吏舍诘之，云：“死已翌日矣。”驹长，卖之，正得所负钱数。（《广记》卷四百三十六）

    　　○孙汉威

    　　江南神武军使孙汉威，厩中有马，遇夜辄尾上放光，状若散火，群马惊嘶（《广记》“惊”作“皆”，“嘶”下有“鸣”字）汉威以为妖，拔剑斩之，数月除卢州刺吏。（《广记》卷四百三十六）

    Explanation

    32

    Gao Zong

    The military official Gao Zong once lent twenty thousand strings of cash to a clerk from a government office. The clerk calculated the interest monthly. After a year, he refused to repay the loan, and Gao could not obtain it. Gao Zong became angry and summoned the clerk, rebuking him: "I owed you money in a past life, and I have repaid it now. You owe me, so you should repay me with a donkey or a horse." He then burned the bond and dismissed him. A year later, Gao Zong sat alone in the hall when suddenly the clerk appeared in white clothing and said, "I have come to repay my debt." Gao Zong replied, "I have already burned the bond, so why should you repay it again?" (According to Guangji, it reads "why should you come?") The clerk did not answer and went directly into the stable. Soon, the stable-hand reported that a white foal had been born. Gao sent someone to inquire at the clerk's house, and they said, "He died the next day." When the foal grew up, it was sold, and the amount received was exactly the same as the debt owed. (From Guangji Volume 436)

    Sun Hanwei

    The military official Sun Hanwei of the Southern Army had a horse in his stable that would emit light from its tail at night, appearing like scattered fire. All the horses were frightened and neighed. (According to Guangji, it reads "all neighed.") Sun Hanwei thought this was an omen and drew his sword to cut off the horse's tail. A few months later, he was appointed as the governor of Luzhou. (From Guangji Volume 436)

    33

    ○唐道袭

    　　王建称尊于洛（《广记》作“蜀”），其嬖臣唐道袭为枢密使，夏日在家，会大雨，其所蓄猫戏水于檐溜下。道袭视之，稍稍而长，俄而前足及檐，忽（《广记》有“尔”字）雷雹（《广记》作“电”）大至，化为龙而去。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    　　○鬻醯者（《广记》作“卖醋人”）

    　　建康（曾慥《类说》作“昌”）有鬻醯者（《广记》作“卖醋人”）某，蓄一猫，甚俊健，爱之甚。辛亥岁（案：辛亥当南唐保大九年）六月，猫死，某不忍弃，犹置坐侧。数日，腐且臭，不得已，携弃秦淮中。既入水，猫乃活，某（《广记》有“自”字）下救之，遂溺死，而猫登岸走。金乌铺吏（曾慥《类说》作“金吾吏”）获之，绠而鐍之（四字《广记》作“缚置”二字）铺中，缫其户。出白官司，将以其猫为证。既还，则已断索啮壁而去，竟不复见。（《广记》卷四百四十，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    33

    Final Translation

    ○唐道袭

    　　王建在洛阳（《广记》作“蜀”）称帝，其宠臣唐道袭担任枢密使。夏日里，唐道袭在家，正赶上大雨，他所养的猫在屋檐下戏水。唐道袭看见猫，渐渐地变长，不久前爪触及屋檐，忽然（《广记》有“尔”字）雷电大作，猫化为龙飞去。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    　　○鬻醯者（《广记》作“卖醋人”）

    　　建康（曾慥《类说》作“昌”）有一位卖醋的人（《广记》作“卖醋人”），名叫某，养了一只非常敏捷强壮的猫，非常喜爱它。辛亥年（案：辛亥当南唐保大九年）六月，猫死了，某不忍心丢弃，仍放在身边。几天后，猫腐烂发臭，不得已，某将其带至秦淮河中丢弃。猫刚入水，却突然复活，某（《广记》有“自”字）下水去救它，结果自己溺水而死，而猫则爬到岸上跑了。金乌铺的官吏（曾慥《类说》作“金吾吏”）抓住了猫，将其用绳子绑住并锁在铺中，封住门。某向官府报告，打算用猫作为证据。官吏返回后，猫已经咬断绳子，啃破墙壁逃走了，最终再也没有出现。（《广记》卷四百四十，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    34

    ○建康人

    　　建康人方食鱼，弃鱼头于地。俄而，壁下地穴中，有人乘马，铠甲分明，大不盈尺，手执长槊，径刺鱼头，驰入穴去。如是数四。即掘地求之，见数大鼠，鱼头在焉。惟有箸一只，了不见甲马之状，无何其人卒。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    　　○卢嵩

    　　太庙斋廊卢嵩，所居釜鸣，灶下有鼠，如人哭声。因祀灶，灶下有五大鼠，各如方色，尽食所祀之物，复入灶中。其年嵩选（《广记》无“选”字）补兴化尉，竟无（《广记》“怪上”有“他”字）怪。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    Explanation

    34

    Translation

    ○建康人

    A person from Jiankang was eating fish and discarded the fish head on the ground. Soon afterward, from a hole in the wall, there appeared a figure riding a horse, clearly visible in armor, no more than a foot tall, holding a long spear. The figure directly pierced the fish head and galloped into the hole, leaving. This happened several times. They immediately dug the ground to find it and discovered several large rats, with the fish head among them. Only a chopstick remained, and no trace of the armored horse was seen. Soon after, the person died.

    ○卢嵩

    In the corridor of the Imperial Ancestral Temple, Lu Sheng lived, and his pot in the home made a noise. There were mice under the stove, making sounds like a person crying. Because of the stove worship, five large rats, each a different color, ate all the offerings and returned to the stove. That year, Lu Sheng was selected to serve as the magistrate of Xinghua, and there were no further strange occurrences.

    35

    ○柴再用

    　　龙武统军柴再用，尝在厅事，凭几独坐，忽有（《广记》有“一”字）鼠走至庭下，向再用拱（《广记》有“手而”二字）立，如欲拜揖之状。再用怒，呼左右，左右皆不至。即自起逐之，鼠乃去，而厅屋梁折，所坐床几尽压糜碎。再用后为卢鄂宣三镇节度使卒。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    　　○苏长史

    　　苏长史者将卜居京口，此宅素凶，妻子谏止之。苏曰：“尔恶此宅，吾必独住。”始宿之（毛本“之”作“一”）夕，有三十余人，皆长尺余，道士冠，衣（《广记》“衣”字在“道”字上）褐来谒苏曰：“此吾等所居也，君必速去，不然祸及。”（《广记》作“及祸”）苏怒持杖逐之，皆走入宅后竹林中而没。即掘其处，获白鼠三十余头，皆杀之（三字《广记》无）。宅不复凶矣。（《广记》卷四百四十）

    35

    Final Translation

    Dragon Warrior Commander Chai Zaiyong

    Dragon Warrior Commander Chai Zaiyong, while in his office, was leaning on a desk and sitting alone. Suddenly, a mouse ran to the courtyard and faced him, bowing as if it wanted to pay respects. Chai Zaiyong became angry and called his attendants, but none came. He then got up to chase the mouse, and the mouse ran away. As a result, the beam in the hall broke, and the bed and desk he was sitting on were completely crushed. Later, Chai Zaiyong served as the military governor of three regions and died.

    Magistrate Su

    Magistrate Su was about to settle in Jingkou, but this house had always been considered ominous. His wife and children advised him against it. Su said, "If you dislike this house, I will live alone here." On the first night he stayed there, more than thirty people, all about a foot long, wearing Taoist hats and coarse cloth, came to pay respects to him. They said, "This is our home, you must leave quickly, otherwise disaster will befall you." Su became angry and chased them with a stick. They all ran into the bamboo forest behind the house and disappeared. He then dug at the spot and found over thirty white mice, all of which he killed. The house no longer had an ominous aura.

    36

    ○卢枢

    　　侍御史卢枢言其亲为建州刺史，尝（《广记》无“尝”字）暑夜独居（《广记》作“出”）寝室，望月于中（《广记》无“中”字）庭，既（《广记》作“始”）出户，忽闻堂西阶下，若有人语笑声。蹑足窥之，见七八白衣人，长不盈尺，男女杂坐饮酒，几席什（《广记》作“食”）器皆具而微，献酬久之，席中一人曰：“今夕甚乐，但白老将至，奈何？”因叹叱（《广记》无“叱”字）。须臾，坐中皆突（《广记》作“哭”）入阴沟中，遂不见。后数日（《广记》无“数日”二字），罢郡新政家有猫名白老，既至，白老自（《广记》作“穴”）堂西阶地中获（《广记》有“白”字，“七八”下有“枚”字）鼠七八，皆杀之。（《广记》卷四百四十，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    36

    Lu Chu

    The Censor Lu Chu recounted that his relative was the governor of Jianzhou. Once, during a hot summer night, he was alone in his bedroom, gazing at the moon in the courtyard. After stepping out of the door, he suddenly heard what sounded like people talking and laughing at the western steps of the hall. Tiptoeing to peek, he saw several white-clad figures, no more than a foot tall, men and women sitting together drinking. The tables, seats, and utensils were all present but small, and they drank and exchanged toasts for a long time. One of them said, "Tonight is very enjoyable, but the white old one is coming; what shall we do?" They then sighed and exclaimed. Soon, all of them rushed into the sewer and disappeared. A few days later, the new official's family had a cat named White Old. After arriving, White Old dug into the western steps of the hall and caught seven or eight rats, all of which it killed.

    37

    ○豫章中官

    　　天福（《广记》作“复”。案：晋天福五年系庚子。广记作天复者，是唐天复祗三年，四年甲子四月改元为天祐元年）甲子岁，豫章居人近市者，夜恒闻街（毛本作“阶”）中若数十人语声，向市而去，就（《广记》作“视”）则无人，如是累夜。人皆惴恐，夜不能寐。顷之，诏尽诛阉官，豫章所杀凡五十余，驱之向市，聚（《广记》作“骤”）语喧う（《广记》作“噪”），如前所闻。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    Explanation

    37

    Translation:

    In the year Tianfu (甲子), which corresponds to 936 CE, residents of Yuzhang (Nanchang) who lived near the market often heard voices at night as if dozens of people were talking in the street (or on the stairs, according to the Mao edition). The voices seemed to be heading toward the market, but when they approached, no one was there. This phenomenon occurred for many consecutive nights, causing the people to feel fearful and unable to sleep. Soon after, an imperial edict was issued to completely eliminate the eunuchs. In Yuzhang, more than fifty eunuchs were killed and driven to the market, where they gathered and made a commotion, similar to what had been heard before. (From Guangji, Volume 353)

    38

    ○青州客

    　　朱梁时青州有贾客，泛海遇风，漂至一处，远望有山川城郭，海师曰：“自顷遭风者，未尝至此。吾闻鬼国在是，得非此耶？”顷之，舟至岸，因登之（《广记》作“岸”），向城而去。其庐舍田亩，皆如（《广记》皆如“作不殊”）中国，见人皆揖之，而人皆不应（《广记》作见）。已至城，有守门者，揖之亦不应。入城，屋（毛本无“屋”字）室人物殷富（《广记》无“富”字），遂至其（《广记》无“其”字）王宫，正值大宴，群臣侍宴者数十，其衣冠器用、丝竹陈设之类，多如（《广记》作“类”）中国。客因升殿，俯逼王座以窥之。

    Explanation

    38

    青州客

    During the Later Liang dynasty, a merchant from Qingzhou was sailing across the sea when he encountered a storm. The wind carried him to a place far away, where he saw mountains, rivers, and cities. The sailor said, "In recent times, no one who has been caught in a storm has come here. I have heard that the Ghost Country is located here; could this be it?" Soon after, the boat reached the shore, and the merchant disembarked and headed towards the city. The houses and fields there were all like those in the central region of China. They saw people who all bowed to them, but the people did not respond. Upon entering the city, the houses, people, and goods were plentiful. They eventually arrived at the king's palace, just as a grand feast was taking place. There were dozens of officials attending the feast, dressed in fine clothes and using elegant utensils, with music and decorations arranged beautifully. The merchant then approached the king's throne closely to observe it.

    39

    俄而，王（《广记》有“有”字）疾，左右扶还，亟召巫者示之，巫云：“有阳地使（《广记》无“使”字）人至此，阳气逼人，故王病。其人偶来尔，无心为祟，以饮食车马谢遣之，可矣。”即具酒食，设坐于别室，王（《广记》作“巫”）及其群臣（《广记》有皆字）来祀祝，客据案而食，俄有仆夫驭马而至，客亦乘马而归。至岸登舟，国人竟不见（《广记》有“已”字）。复遇便风得归。时贺德俭为青州节度，与魏博节度杨思厚有亲，因遣此客使魏，具为思厚言之。魏人范宣古亲闻其事，至（《广记》无“至”字）为余言。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    Explanation

    39

    Shortly after, the king fell ill and was carried back by his attendants. They quickly summoned a witch to show him the situation. The witch said, "There is an envoy from the Yang region here, and his yang energy is oppressive, which is why the king is sick. He has come by chance and does not intend to cause harm. Dismiss him with food, drink, and vehicles, and that will suffice." They immediately prepared food and drink and set up seats in a separate room. The king and his ministers came to offer sacrifices and prayers. The guest sat at the table and ate. Soon, a servant arrived driving a horse, and the guest also rode away on a horse. He reached the shore and boarded a boat, and the people of the country did not see him. He encountered favorable winds and returned. At that time, He Dejian was the military governor of Qingzhou and had a close relationship with the military governor of Weibo, Yang Sihou. He sent this guest to Wei and explained the entire event in detail to Yang Sihou. A person from Wei, Fan Xuan, personally heard about the event and told me about it.

    ○周元枢

    　　周元枢者，睢阳人，为平卢掌书记。（《广记》有“寄”字）居临淄官舍，一夕将寝，忽有车马辎重甚众，扣门，吏（《广记》作“使”）报曰：“李司空候谒。”元枢念亲知辈皆无此人，因自思必乡曲之旧，吾不及知矣，因出见之。延坐请问其所从来，曰：“吾新移家至此（《广记》作“吾亦新家至此”），未有所止，求君（《广记》作“居”）此宅可矣。”（《广记》无“可矣”二字）元枢惊曰：“何至是。”对曰：“此吾之旧宅也。”元枢曰：“吾从官至此，相传云书记之公署也。君何时居此。”曰：“隋开皇中尝居之。

    Explanation

    40

    Zhou Yuanshu, a man from Suizhou, served as the chief secretary (掌书记) of Pinglu. One night, while residing in an official residence in Linzi, he was about to go to sleep when a large number of vehicles and people suddenly arrived at his door. A messenger reported, "The Sikong is waiting to pay respects." Zhou Yuanshu thought that none of his close acquaintances were Sikongs, so he reasoned that it must be an old acquaintance from his hometown, whom he had not met before. He then went out to see the visitor, invited him to sit down, and asked where he had come from. The visitor replied, "I have recently moved here (《广记》作“吾亦新家至此”) and have not yet found a place to stay. I would like to ask if you could allow me to stay in this house." Zhou Yuanshu was surprised and said, "Why would you want to do that?" The visitor responded, "This is my old house." Zhou Yuanshu said, "I have been serving in this position since I came here, and it is said that this is the office of the secretary. When did you live here?" The visitor replied, "I once lived here during the Kaihuang era of the Sui Dynasty."

    ”（《广记》有“元”字）枢曰：“若尔，君定是鬼耶？”曰：“然”地府许我立庙于此，故请君移去尔。”元枢不可，曰：“人不当与鬼相接，岂吾将死，故君得临吾（《广记》“临吾”作“凌我”）耶？虽然，理不当以此宅授君，吾虽死必与君讼。”因召妻子曰：“我死，必多置纸笔于棺中，将与李君对讼。”即具酒与之饮相酬数百杯，词色愈厉。客将去，复留之，良久，一苍头来云：“（《广记》有“夫人传语”四字）司空周书记，木石人也，安可与之论难，自取困哉？”客于是辞谢而去，送之出门，倏忽不见。元枢竟无恙。（《广记》卷三百五十三）
