    41

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    This translation captures the essence of the original text, including the supernatural elements and the protagonist's reaction to the ghost. The translation aims to be faithful to the original while ensuring it reads naturally in English.

    42

    ○朱延寿

    　　寿州刺史朱延寿，末年，浴于室中，窥见窗外有二人，皆青面朱发青衣，手执文书。一人曰：“我受命来取。”一人曰：“我亦受命来取。”一人又曰：“我受命在前。”延寿因呼侍者，二人即灭。侍者至，问外有何人，皆云无人。俄而被杀。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    　　○秦进忠

    　　天祐丙子岁（案：天祐为吴之年号，铉生于是，年曾仕吴为校书郎），浙西军士周交作乱，杀大将秦进忠、张胤凡十余人。进忠少时，尝怒一小奴，刃贯心，杀而并埋之。末年恒见此奴捧心而立，始于百步之外，稍稍而近。其日将出，乃在马前，左右皆见之，（《广记》有“而”字）入府（《广记》有“又”字）遇乱兵伤胸而卒。张胤前月余每闻呼其姓名者（《广记》无“者”字），声甚清越，亦稍稍而近。其日若在对面，入府而毙。（《广记》卷三百五十三，而“毙”作“皆毙矣”）

    Explanation

    42

    ○Zhu Yanshou

    The governor of Shouzhou, Zhu Yanshou, in his later years, bathed in his room and saw two figures outside his window. They were all blue-faced, red-haired, and wore blue clothing, holding documents in their hands. One said, "I was sent here by command to take something." Another said, "I was also sent here by command to take something." A third said, "I was sent here before the others." Zhu Yanshou then called for a servant, and the figures disappeared. When the servant arrived, he asked if there were anyone outside, and everyone said there was no one. Shortly after, Zhu Yanshou was killed.

    ○Qin Jinzhong

    In the year 906 AD (the Tianyou era of the Wu state), a military officer named Zhou Jiao from the western Zhejiang region rebelled, killing major generals Qin Jinzhong and Zhang Yin, among others. Qin Jinzhong, in his youth, once became angry at a small servant and stabbed him through the heart, killing him and burying him together. In his later years, he often saw this servant standing with his heart in his hand, starting from a hundred steps away and gradually coming closer. On the day he entered the government office, he was killed by rebels, wounded in the chest.

    Zhang Yin, about a month earlier, often heard someone calling his name, the voice being very clear and resonant, and it also gradually came closer. On the day he entered the government office, he was killed. All were killed.

    43

    ○望江李令

    　　望江李令者，罢秩居舒州，有二子，甚聪慧。令尝饮酒暮归，去家数百步，见二子来迎，即共擒而殴之，令惊（《广记》有“大”字）怒大呼，而远方人绝，竟无知者。且行且殴，将至家，二子皆却走而去。及入门，二子复迎于堂下，问之皆云“未尝出门”。后月余，令复饮酒于所亲家，因具白其事，请留宿不敢归。而其子恐其父（《广记》作“及”）暮归复为所殴，即俱往迎之，及至（《广记》无“至”字）中途，见其父怒曰：“何故暮出？”即使从者击之，困（毛本作“因”）而获免。明日令归，益骇其事。不数月，父子皆卒。郡人云：“吾（《广记》无“吾”字）舒有山鬼，善为此厉，盖黎邱之徒也。”（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    Explanation

    43

    The County Magistrate of Wangjiang

    The County Magistrate of Wangjiang, after being dismissed from his post, resided in Shuzhou. He had two sons who were very intelligent. One day, the magistrate drank wine late into the evening and returned home. When he was still several hundred steps away from his house, he saw his two sons coming to greet him. They immediately seized and beat him. The magistrate was shocked and shouted loudly, but no one from afar came to help, and no one knew about it. As he continued walking and being beaten, they were about to reach home when his sons all retreated and left. Upon entering the house, his sons greeted him again at the hall entrance. When asked, they all said, "We never left the house." After more than a month, the magistrate again drank wine at a friend's house and reported the incident in detail, asking to stay overnight and not daring to return home. His sons feared that their father would be beaten again if he returned late at night, so they went to meet him. On the way, they saw their father angrily say, "Why did you go out late?" He then ordered his attendants to hit him, and he managed to escape after being in a difficult situation. The next day, when the magistrate returned home, he was increasingly shocked by the incident. Not long after, both the father and son died. People in the county said, "Our region (Wushu) has mountain spirits who are good at causing such harm, probably similar to those from Liqi." (From Volume 353 of Guangji)

    44

    ○建康乐人

    　　建康有乐人，日晚如市，见二仆夫云“陆判官召”，随之而去。至一（《广记》无“一”字）大宅，陈设甚严，宾客十余人，皆善酒。惟饮酒而不设食，酒亦不及乐人，向曙而散，乐人困甚，因卧门外床上。及（《广记》作“既”）寤，乃在草间，旁有大冢，问其里人，云相传陆判官之冢，不知何时人也。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    　　○黄廷让

    　　建康吏黄廷让，尝饮酒于亲家，迨夜而散。不甚醉而（《广记》“而”字在“然”字下）怳然身浮，飘飘而行，不能自致（《广记》作“制”）行可十数里，至一大宅，寂然无人，堂前有小房，房中有床，廷让困甚，因寝床上。及寤，乃在蒋山前草间，逾重城复堑矣。因恍惚得疾，岁余乃愈。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    Explanation

    44

    Translation

    The Leisure People of Jiankang

    In Jiankang, there were leisure people who, as dusk approached, gathered like a market. They saw two servants who said, "Judge Lu has summoned you," and followed them away. They arrived at a grand mansion, where the setup was very formal, with over ten guests, all skilled in drinking. Only wine was served without food, and the wine was not even served to the leisure people. They scattered as dawn approached, and the leisure people were very tired, so they lay down on a bed outside the gate. Upon waking, they found themselves in the grass, beside a large tomb. They asked the locals, who told them that it was said to be Judge Lu's tomb, but they did not know when he lived. (From The Collection of Strange Stories Volume 353)

    Huang Tingrang

    Huang Tingrang, an official from Jiankang, once drank with his in-laws until night and then dispersed. He was not very drunk but suddenly felt floating and drifting along, unable to control his movements for about ten miles. He arrived at a grand mansion, which was deserted, with a small room in front of the hall and a bed inside the room. Huang Tingrang was very tired and lay down on the bed. Upon waking, he found himself in the grass before Mount Jiangshan, having crossed multiple walls and moats. He suffered from a sudden illness and recovered after more than a year. (From The Collection of Strange Stories Volume 353)

    45

    ○张瑗

    　　江南内臣张瑗，日暮过建康新桥，忽见一美妇（《广记》无“妇”字）人，袒衣猖獗而走。瑗甚讶，谛视之，妇人忽尔回顾，（《广记》作“头”）化为旋风扑瑗，瑗马倒伤面，月余乃复。初马既起，乃提（毛本作“是”）一足跛行而归，自是每过此桥，马辄提一足而行，竟亦无他怪祸。（《广记》卷三百五十三，无“亦”字“祸”字）

    　　○婺源军人妻

    　　丁酉岁（案：丁酉当南唐升元元年），婺源建威军人（曾慥《类说》引作“建安有人”），妻死更娶。其后妻虐遇前妻之子过甚，夫不能制。一日，忽见亡妻自门而入，大怒后妻曰：“人谁无死？孰无母子之情？乃虐我女儿如是耶？吾此诉于（《广记》作“与”）地下所司，今与我假十日，使我诲汝，汝遂不改，必能杀君。”夫妻皆恐惧，再拜，即为具酒食。便（广记作“遍”）召亲党邻里问讯，叙语（《广记》作“话”）如常。

    Explanation

    45

    Final Translation

    Zhang Yuan

    In the late afternoon, Zhang Yuan, an official of the Southern Tang court, passed over the new bridge of Jiankang. Suddenly, he saw a beautiful person (some versions omit the character for "woman") running naked and wildly. Zhang Yuan was very surprised and looked at her carefully. The woman suddenly turned her head (some versions say "head") and transformed into a whirlwind that attacked Zhang Yuan. Zhang Yuan's horse fell, and he was injured on his face. He took more than a month to recover. At first, when the horse stood up, it limped on one leg and returned home. From then on, every time they passed this bridge, the horse would limp on one leg, and there were no other strange misfortunes.

    Wife of a Soldier from Wuyuan

    In the year Ding You (which corresponds to 937 AD, the first year of the Southern Tang dynasty), a soldier from Jiànwei, Wuyuan, remarried after his first wife died. His new wife excessively mistreated his children from his previous marriage, and the husband could not control her. One day, he suddenly saw his deceased wife enter through the door. She angrily told his new wife, "Who among people does not die? Who has no maternal love for their children? Why did you treat my daughter so badly? I will report this to the officials in the underworld. Now give me ten days to teach you. If you do not change, I will definitely kill you." Both husband and wife were terrified and bowed twice. They immediately prepared food and drink and invited relatives, neighbors, and acquaintances to visit. They talked as usual.

    46

    他人但闻其声，惟夫妻（《广记》无“妻”字）见之。及夜，为设榻别室，夫欲从之宿，不可。满十日，将去，复责詈（《广记》作“励”）其后妻，言甚切至。举家亲族共送至墓（《广记》有“去墓”二字）百余步，曰：“诸人可止矣。”复殷勤辞诀而去。将及柏林中，遂入，（《广记》无“遂入”二字，有“诸”字）人皆见之，衣服容色如平生，及墓乃没。建威军使汪延昌言如是。（《广记》卷三百五十三，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    46

    A Man with a Strange Voice

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a man from Luoyang had a voice so peculiar that others only heard it, while only his wife and husband saw him. At night, he was given a bed in a separate room. The husband wanted to stay with him overnight, but he refused. After ten days, he was about to leave, and he again scolded his second wife, his words being very severe and heartfelt. The entire family and relatives accompanied him to the tomb, a hundred steps away, and he said, "Everyone can stop here." He then politely bid farewell and left. As he was about to enter the pine forest, he went in. Everyone saw him, and his clothes and appearance were as they were in life, until he reached the tomb, where he disappeared. Jianwei Army Commander Wang Yanchang recounted it as such. (From the "Guangji," Volume 353; also cited in Zeng Zao's "Leishuo.")

    47

    ○陈德遇

    　　辛亥岁（案：辛亥当南唐保大九年），江南伪右藏库官陈居让，字德遇，直宿库中。其妻在家，五更初忽梦二吏，手把文书，自门而入，问：“此陈德遇家耶？”曰：“然。”德遇何在？”曰：“在库中。”吏将去，妻追呼之曰：“家夫字德遇耳，有主衣库官陈德遇者，家近在东曲。”二吏相视而嘻曰：“几误。”（《广记》有“矣”字）遂去。尔（毛本作“弥”）日德遇晨起如厕，乃自云有疾，还卧，良久遂卒。二人并居冶（《广记》作“治”）城之西。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    　　○广陵吏人

    Explanation

    47

    In the year of the Black Pig (941 AD), Chen Ju Rang, an official in charge of the right treasury in the southern region, was on duty in the warehouse. His wife was at home when, at the first watch of the night (around 3 AM), she suddenly had a dream. Two officials, carrying documents, entered from the door and asked, "Is this the home of Chen De Yu?" She replied, "Yes." They then asked, "Where is Chen De Yu?" She answered, "He is in the warehouse." As the officials were about to leave, the wife called out to them, saying, "My husband's name is De Yu. There is another official named Chen De Yu who works in the clothing treasury, and his home is near the east bend." The two officials looked at each other and laughed, saying, "We nearly made a mistake." They then left. That day, Chen Ju Rang got up early to use the toilet, claimed he was ill, returned to bed, and after a long time, he died. The two officials lived west of the Iron City.

    In Guangling, an official was involved in a similar incident, but the details are not provided in this excerpt.

    48

    广陵吏姓赵，当暑独寝一室中。夜忽见大黄衣人自门而入，从小黄衣七八（《广记》作“人”），谓己曰：“处处寻不得，乃在此耶！”叱起之，曰：“可以行矣！”一黄衣前白（《广记》无“白”字）曰：“天年未尽，未可遽行，宜有以记之可也。”大人即探怀出（《广记》有“一”字）印，印其左臂而去。及明视之，印文著肉，字若古篆，识其下，右若先字，左若记之，其上不可识。赵后不知所终。（《广记》卷三百五十三）

    　　○田达诚

    　　庐陵有贾人田达诚，富于财业，（《广记》无“业”字）颇以周给为务。治第新城，有夜扣门者，就视无人，如是再三。因呵（《广记》作“呼”）问之“为人耶鬼耶”，良久答曰：“实非人也。比居龙泉舍，为暴水所漂，（《广记》作“毁”）求寄君家，治舍毕乃去耳。”达诚不许曰：“人岂可与鬼同居耶？”对曰：“暂寄居耳，无害于君，且以君义气闻于乡里，故告耳。”达诚许之。

    Explanation

    48

    A Clerk Named Zhao in Guangling

    During the hot summer, a clerk named Zhao slept alone in a room. At night, he suddenly saw a large person in yellow clothes entering from the door, followed by several smaller yellow-clad figures. The large person said to him, "We searched everywhere and could not find you, but here you are!" He shouted at Zhao, "It is time to go!" One of the smaller yellow-clad figures stepped forward and said, "Your days are not yet complete, you cannot go yet. It is appropriate to mark it somehow." The large person then probed his chest to take out a seal and sealed Zhao's left arm before departing. When morning came, the seal text was visible on the flesh, the characters were like ancient seal script. Reading below, the right side seemed like "先" (first), and the left side like "记" (record), but the top part could not be recognized. Zhao later disappeared without a trace. (From Volume 353 of the Guangji)

    Tian Dacheng, a Merchant in Luzhou

    In Luzhou, there was a merchant named Tian Dacheng, wealthy in wealth and business, who often engaged in charitable acts. He built a new residence and one night, someone knocked at the door. Upon looking, no one was there, and this happened several times. He then shouted, "Are you a person or a ghost?" After a long while, the figure replied, "I am not a person. I previously lived in a house in Longquan, which was destroyed by a flood. I am seeking to stay at your home until the new house is completed and then leave." Tian Dacheng refused, saying, "Can a person live with a ghost?" The figure replied, "It is only a temporary stay, it will not harm you. Moreover, your reputation for righteousness is known in the village, so I am telling you." Tian Dacheng agreed.

    49

    因曰：“当止我何所？”达诚曰：“惟有厅事耳？”即（《广记》有“拜”字）辞谢而去。数日复来，曰：“吾家已至厅中，亦无妨君宾客，然可严整，家中人慎火，万一不虞（《广记》作“意”），或当云吾等所为也。”达诚亦虚其厅以付（《广记》作“奉”）之。达诚尝为诗，鬼忽空中言曰：“君乃能诗耶？吾亦尝好之，可唱和耳。”（《广记》作“乎”）达诚即具酒，置纸笔于前，谈论无所不至，众目视之，酒与纸笔俨然不动，试暂回顾，则酒已尽，字已著纸矣。前后数十（《广记》无“十”字）篇，皆有意趣（《广记》作“义”），笔迹劲健作柳体。

    Explanation

    49

    A Ghost Visits Dacheng's Hall

    Dacheng then said, "Where should I stop?" Dacheng replied, "There is only the hall." He then bowed and left. After several days, he returned and said, "Our family has arrived at the hall. It does not interfere with your guests, but you can be strict, and be careful with fire in the house. In case of unforeseen circumstances, perhaps it will be said that it was done by us." Dacheng also vacated the hall and handed it over to them. Dacheng once composed poetry, and a ghost suddenly spoke from the air, "Can I really compose poetry? I too have enjoyed it; we can exchange verses." Dacheng immediately prepared wine, placed paper and ink on the table, and they discussed everything without limit. All watched it, but the wine and paper and ink remained unmoved. When they tried to glance back, the wine was already gone, and the words had already been written on the paper. They composed dozens of poems, all full of interest and charm, with handwriting that was strong and vigorous in the style of Liu Gongquan.

    50

    或问其姓字，曰：“吾傥言之，将不益于主人，可诗以寄言也。”（《广记》作“之”）乃赋诗云：“天然与我亦（《广记》作“一”）灵通，还与人间事不同。要识吾家真姓字，大字（《广记》“大”字作“天地”）南头一段红。”众（《广记》有“亦”字）不喻也。一日，复告曰：“吾有少子，婚樟树神女，以某日成礼，复欲借君后堂三日，以终君大惠，可乎？”达诚亦虚其堂，以幕帷（《广记》作“图”）之。三日，复谢曰：“吾事讫矣，还君此堂。主人之恩，可谓至矣。然君家老婢某可笞一百也。

    Explanation

    50

    Someone asked about his name. He replied, "If I were to say it, it would not benefit the host. It can be expressed through poetry." (In the Guangji, it is written as "it.") He then recited a poem: "Naturally connected to me, different from human affairs. To know the true name of my family, a significant mark at the southern end." The others did not understand. One day, he said again, "I have a young son who married the spirit of the camphor tree. On a certain day, the wedding was held, and I wish to borrow your back hall for three days to complete your great kindness. Is that acceptable?" The host, named Da Cheng, also prepared his hall, using curtains and screens to make it ready. After three days, he thanked him, saying, "My affairs are completed, and I return this hall to you. The host's kindness can be considered great. However, your old servant girl can be beaten a hundred times."

    51

    ”达诚辞谢，即（《广记》无“即”字）召婢笞数下，鬼曰：“使之知过，可止矣。”达诚徐问其婢，云（《广记》作“言”）曾穴幕窃视，见宾客男女，厨膳花烛，与人间不殊。后岁余，乃辞谢而去。达诚以事至广陵，久之不归，其家尤之，鬼复至曰：“君家尤主人耶？吾将省之。”翌（《广记》作“明”）日乃还，曰：“主政（《广记》作“人”）在扬州（《广记》作子），甚无恙，行当归矣。新纳一妾，与之同寝，吾烧其帐后幅以戏之耳。”大笑而去。达诚归，问其事皆同。后至龙泉访其居，亦竟不获。（《广记》卷三百五十四）

    Explanation

    51

    A Man Named Da Cheng

    Da Cheng politely declined, but immediately called his servant girl and lashed her several times. The ghost said, "To make her understand her mistake, that's enough." Da Cheng then asked the servant girl in a calm manner, and she said (as recorded in the Guangji) that she had once peeped through a hole in the curtain and saw guests, both men and women, along with food and candles, all no different from the human world. After more than a year, the ghost finally bid farewell and left. Da Cheng went to Guangling for official business and did not return for a long time. His family blamed him, and the ghost came again, saying, "Is your family blaming the master? I will go to check on him." The next day, the ghost returned and said, "The master is in Yangzhou, very well, and will return soon. He has recently taken a concubine and shares a bed with her. I burned the back part of her screen to play a prank on her." The ghost laughed loudly and left. When Da Cheng returned home, he asked about the matter, and everything was the same as what the ghost had said. Later, he went to Longquan to search for the ghost's residence but did not find it. (From the Guangji, Volume 354)

    ●卷三

    　　○徐彦成

    　　军吏徐彦成，恒业市木。丁亥岁（案：丁亥当唐天成二年），往信州汭口场，无木可市，泊舟久之。一日晚，有少年从二仆往来岸侧，状若访人而不遇者。彦成因延入舟中，为设酒席，宾礼（《广记》作“敬”）之。少年甚愧焉，将去，谢曰：“吾家近此数里别业中，君今肯辱枉（四字《广记》作“旦日能辱”）顾乎？”彦成许诺。明日乃往，行里余，有仆马来迎，奄至一大宅，门馆甚盛。少年出延客，酒膳丰备，从容久之。彦成因言住此久无木可市，少年云：（《广记》作“曰”）“吾有木在山中，明当令出也。

    Explanation

    52

    Chapter Three

    ○ Xu Yancheng

    The military official Xu Yancheng, whose constant occupation was trading wood, traveled to the market at Xinzhou's Rui Kou in the year Ding Hai (which corresponds to the second year of the Tiancheng era during the Tang Dynasty). Finding no wood to trade, he anchored his boat for a long time. One evening, a young man accompanied by two servants came and went along the shore, appearing as if he were visiting but not meeting anyone. Xu Yancheng invited him into his boat, prepared a feast, and treated him with courtesy. The young man was greatly moved and, as he was leaving, thanked Xu Yancheng, saying, "My family home is a few miles away in a separate estate. Would you be so kind as to visit us?" Xu Yancheng agreed. The next day, he went there, and after traveling a few miles, he was met by servants and horses, and soon arrived at a grand mansion with splendid gates and halls. The young man came out to greet him, and the feast was abundant. They spent a long time together in leisurely conversation. Xu Yancheng then mentioned that he had been staying there for a long time without any wood to trade. The young man replied, "I have some wood in the mountains. I will have it brought out tomorrow."

    53

    ”居一二日，果有杉（《广记》作“材”）木大至，良而价廉，市易既毕，往辞，少年复出大杉板四枚，曰：“向之木吾所卖，今以此赠君，至吴当获善价。”（二字《广记》作“菩提”）彦成回，始至秦淮，会吴帅殂，纳杉板为棺，以求（《广记》作“为”）材之尤异者，获钱数十万。彦成广（《广记》作“大”）市珍玩，复往汭口以酬少年，（《广记》有“少年复”三字）更与交易于市，三往返（三字《广记》作“如是三往”四字，下有“颇”字）获其（《广记》无“其”字）厚利。间一岁，复往，但见（《广记》“往但见”三字作“诣之”二字）村落如故，了无所见。询（《广记》作访）其里中，竟无能知（《广记》无“之”字）之者。（《广记》卷三百五十四）

    Explanation

    53

    After one or two days, indeed there was a large quantity of pine wood that arrived, of good quality and cheap. After completing all the transactions, Yan Cheng went to bid farewell, and the youth brought out four large pieces of pine wood, saying, "The wood mentioned before was what I sold, and now I am giving this to you. When you reach Wu, you will get a good price."

    Yan Cheng returned and just reached the Qinhuai River, coinciding with the death of the Wu commander. He accepted the pine wood as a coffin and sought the most extraordinary wood, receiving tens of thousands of coins. Yan Cheng widely bought precious and exquisite items and returned to the market to repay the youth, further engaging in transactions in the market. After three round trips, he gained substantial profits.

    After a year, he returned, but only saw the village as it was, with nothing more. He inquired in the village, but no one could identify it.

    54

    ○周洁

    　　霍邱令周洁，甲辰岁罢任，客游淮上。时民大饥，逆旅殆绝，投宿无所。升高而望，遥见村落烟火，趋而诣之，得一村舍，扣门久之，一女子出应门，告以求宿，女子曰：“家中饥饿，老幼皆病，愧（《广记》无“愧”字）无以延客，止（《广记》作“至”）中堂一榻可矣。”遂入之，女子侍立于前。少顷，其妹复出，映妇（《广记》作“姊”）而立，不见其面。洁自具食，取饼二枚以与二女，持之入室，闭关而听（《广记》作“寝”），悄无人声。洁方竦（《广记》“方”作“亦”）然而惧，向晓将去，使（《广记》作“更”）呼二女告别（《广记》作“之”），了无声应者。因坏户而入，乃见积尸满屋，皆将枯朽，惟女子死未（《广记》作“可”）旬日，其妹面目已枯矣，二饼犹置胸上。洁后皆为瘗之。（《广记》卷三百五十四，“之”字下有“云”字，毛本同）

    Explanation

    54

    A Tale of Zhou Jie

    In the year of Jia Chen, Zhou Jie, the magistrate of Huoqiu, was dismissed from his post and traveled as a guest to the north of the Huai River. At that time, the people were suffering from a severe famine, and inns were nearly nonexistent, leaving him without a place to stay. He climbed to a high place and looked afar, seeing smoke rising from a distant village. He hurried towards it and found a rural cottage. After knocking on the door for a long time, a woman came out to answer it. Zhou Jie asked for a place to stay for the night. The woman said, "Our family is starving, and both the old and the young are ill. I am ashamed (as noted in Guangji, the word '愧' is omitted) and have nothing to offer as a guest, but there is only one bed in the central hall, and you can stay there." Zhou Jie then entered, and the woman stood in front of him. After a short while, her sister came out and stood beside her, but Zhou Jie could not see her face. Zhou Jie prepared food himself and took two pieces of bread to give to the two women. He took them into the room, closed the door, and listened, but there was no sound of anyone. Zhou Jie was startled and afraid, and at dawn, he was about to leave. He tried to call out to the two women to say goodbye, but there was no response. He then broke down the door and entered, only to find the room filled with decaying corpses. All of them were nearly rotten, except for the woman who had died no more than ten days ago, and her sister's face was already withered. The two pieces of bread were still placed on the woman's chest. Zhou Jie later buried all of them. (Guangji, Volume 354, the word "云" is added after "之" in the Mao edition.)

    55

    ○杨副使

    　　壬午岁（案：壬午为梁龙德二年，吴顺义二年），广陵瓜州市中有人市果实甚亟（《广记》作“急”），或问所用，云：“吾长官明日上事。”又（《广记》作“有”）问长官为谁，云：“杨副使也。”又问官署何在，（《广记》无“又”字）云金山之东。遂去不可复问。时浙西有杨（《广记》无“杨”字）副使，被召之扬都，（《广记》有“明日”二字）船至金山，无故而没。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    55

    In the year of Renwu (壬午岁, 922 AD), during the Longde era of the Later Liang dynasty and the Shunyi era of the Wu kingdom, there was a person in the melon market of Guangling (广陵瓜州市中) who was buying fruit very urgently (市果实甚亟). Someone asked him what he was buying the fruit for, and he replied, "My superior will take office tomorrow." When asked who the superior was, he said, "Yang Deputy." When asked where the official residence was, he said, "East of Jinshan." He then left, and it was no longer possible to ask him further. At that time, there was a Yang Deputy in Zhe West (时浙西有杨副使) who was summoned to Yangzhou (被召之扬都). His boat arrived at Jinshan (船至金山), and he died without any apparent reason (无故而没).

    56

    ○僧珉楚

    　　广陵法云寺僧珉楚，尝（《广记》作“常”）与中山贾人章某者亲熟，章死珉楚为设斋诵经。数月，忽遇章于市中，楚未食，章即延入食店，为置胡饼，既食，楚问：“君已死，那得在此？”章曰：“然吾以小罪，（《广记》有“而”字）未得辞脱（《广记》“脱”作“免”），今死（《广记》作“配”）为扬州掠剩儿。”（《广记》作“鬼”）复问何谓掠剩，曰：“凡市）人卖（《广记》作“贾”）贩利息，皆有常（《广记》无“常”字）数，过数得之（《广记》有“即”字）为掠（《广记》作“余”）剩，吾得而掠有之。今人间如吾辈甚多。”因指路人男女曰，某人某人皆是也。顷之有一僧过于前，又曰：“此僧亦是也。”因召至，与语良久，僧亦不见楚也。

    Explanation

    56

    ○僧珉楚

    　　广陵法云寺僧珉楚，尝（《广记》作“常”）与中山贾人章某者亲熟，章死珉楚为设斋诵经。数月，忽遇章于市中，楚未食，章即延入食店，为置胡饼，既食，楚问：“君已死，那得在此？”章曰：“然吾以小罪，（《广记》有“而”字）未得辞脱（《广记》“脱”作“免”），今死（《广记》作“配”）为扬州掠剩儿。”（《广记》作“鬼”）复问何谓掠剩，曰：“凡市）人卖（《广记》作“贾”）贩利息，皆有常（《广记》无“常”字）数，过数得之（《广记》有“即”字）为掠（《广记》作“余”）剩，吾得而掠有之。今人间如吾辈甚多。”因指路人男女曰，某人某人皆是也。顷之有一僧过于前，又曰：“此僧亦是也。”因召至，与语良久，僧亦不见楚也。

    Final Translation:

    ○ Monk Mingchu

    　　Monk Mingchu of the Fayun Temple in Guangling had once been acquainted with a merchant named Zhang from Zhongshan. After Zhang died, Mingchu set up a meal and recited scriptures for him. Several months later, Mingchu unexpectedly met Zhang in the market. Mingchu had not yet eaten, so Zhang invited him into a food shop and prepared some flatbread for him. After eating, Mingchu asked, "You have already died, how can you be here?" Zhang replied, "Indeed, I have committed a minor offense and have not been able to escape (《广记》作“免”). Now, I am (《广记》作“配”) a leftover child in Yangzhou." (《广记》作“鬼”) Mingchu then asked what was meant by "leftover." Zhang explained, "All merchants who sell goods and make profits have a fixed amount (《广记》无“常”字). If they exceed the fixed amount, it is considered leftover (《广记》作“余”), and I get to take it. There are many like me in the world today." He then pointed to passersby and said, "Those people are all like me." Soon after, a monk passed by, and Zhang said, "This monk is also one of us." He then called the monk over, and they talked for a long time, but the monk did not see Mingchu either.

    57

    顷之，相与南行，遇一妇人卖花，章曰：“此妇人之花（《广记》无“之花”二字）亦鬼所买（《广记》作“卖”），花亦鬼用之，人间无所用（《广记》作“见”）也。”章即（《广记》作“则”）出数钱买之，以赠楚曰：“凡见此花而笑者，皆鬼也。”即告辞而去。其花红色（《广记》作“芳”）可爱，而甚重，楚亦昏然而归。路人见花颇有笑者，至寺北门，自念我与鬼同游，复持鬼物，（《广记》作“花”，下有“亦”字）不可，即将花掷溅水中（七字《广记》作“即掷花沟中溅水有声”）。既归有（《广记》无“有”字）同院人觉其面（《广记》无“面”字）色甚异，以为中恶，竞持汤药以救之，良久乃复，且（《广记》作“具”）言其故。因相与覆视其花，乃一死人手也。楚亦无恙。（《广记》卷三百五十五，曾慥《类说》同）

    Explanation

    57

    After a while, they went together south and met a woman selling flowers. Zhang said, "These flowers are also bought by ghosts, and the flowers are also used by ghosts, of no use in the human world." Zhang then took out some money to buy them and gave them to Chu, saying, "Whenever you see this flower and laugh, it is a ghost." He then bade farewell and left. The flowers were red and lovely but very heavy. Chu dazedly returned. Passersby saw the flowers and many laughed. Upon reaching the north gate of the temple, he thought to himself, "I have traveled with ghosts, and I now hold ghostly objects." He then threw the flowers into the water, splashing. After returning, his fellow residents noticed that his face looked very strange, thinking he had been afflicted by evil spirits and held herbs to treat him. After a long time, he recovered and explained the reason. They then looked at the flowers together, and they were a dead person's hand. Chu was unharmed.

    58

    ○陈守规

    　　军将陈守规者，尝坐法流信州，寓止公馆，馆素凶，守规始至，即鬼物书见，奇形怪状，变化倏忽。守规素刚猛，亲持弓矢刀仗与之斗。久之，乃空中语曰：“吾鬼神不欲与人杂处（《广记》作“居”），君既坚贞（《广记》作“正”），愿以兄事可乎？”守规许之。自是尝（《广记》作“常”）与交言，有吉凶辄先报，或求饮食，与之辄得钱物。既久，颇为厌倦，因求方士手书章疏奏之上帝。翌日，鬼乃大骂曰：“吾与君为兄弟，奈何上章疏（《广记》作“诉”）我？大丈夫结交当如是耶？”守规曰：“安得（《广记》有“有”字）此事？”即于空中掷下章疏，纸墨（《广记》作“笔”）宛然。鬼（《广记》无“鬼”字）又曰：“君图我居处，谓我无所止也，吾今往蜀川，亦不下于此矣。”由是遂绝。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    58

    ○ Chen Shougui

    A military officer named Chen Shougui, once exiled to Xinzhou for a legal offense, stayed in a public guesthouse. The guesthouse was known to be haunted. As soon as Chen arrived, ghosts wrote to see him, appearing in strange shapes and bizarre forms, changing suddenly and swiftly. Chen, known for his bravery, personally wielded bows, arrows, swords, and weapons to fight against them. After a long time, one of the ghosts spoke from the air, saying, "I, a spirit, do not wish to live among humans. Since you are steadfast, would you be willing to treat me as a brother?" Chen agreed to this. From then on, they often communicated, and any good or bad news was reported beforehand. Sometimes the ghosts asked for food and drink, and giving them resulted in money and goods. After a long time, Chen became quite tired of this and therefore sought a Taoist priest to write a petition to the Jade Emperor. The next day, the ghost shouted angrily, saying, "You planned my dwelling, thinking I had no place to stay. Now I am going to Shu region, and it is not inferior to this place." And thus, the relationship ended. (From Guangji Volume 355)

    59

    ○广陵买人

    　　广陵有贾人以柏木造床，凡什物百余事，制作甚精，其费已二十万，载之建康，卖以求利。晚至瓜步，微有风起，因泊山下。顷之，有巨舟，其中空，惟篙工三人乘之，亦泊于其侧。买人疑之，相与议此必群盗也，将伺夜而劫我。前浦既远，风又益急，逃避无地（《广记》作“所”），夜即相与登岸，深（《广记》有“林中以”三字）避之。俄而，风雨雷电蒙覆舟所，岸上则星月皎（《广记》作“了”）然。食顷，雨止云散，见巨艘（《广记》作“舟”）稍稍前去，乃敢归舟中，所载柏床（《广记》作“木”）什器都不复见，余物皆在。巨舟犹在东岸，有人呼曰：“尔无恨，当还尔价直。”（《广记》无“直”字）贾人所载既失，复归广陵。至家已有人送钱三十万，置之而去，问其人，即泊瓜步之明日也。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    59

    A Merchant from Guangling

    In Guangling, there was a merchant who crafted a bed and over a hundred other household items from cypress wood. The craftsmanship was exquisite, and the total cost amounted to twenty thousand. He loaded these items onto a boat and sailed to Jiankang to sell them for profit. Late in the day, as they reached Guabu, a slight wind began to blow, so they anchored near a mountain. Soon after, a large ship appeared, which was mostly empty and carried only three boatmen. It also anchored nearby. The merchant suspected the large ship and discussed with his companions that it must be a group of bandits planning to rob them. The harbor was far ahead, and the wind was becoming stronger, leaving them with no place to escape. That night, they all disembarked and hid deeply in the forest. Shortly thereafter, a storm of wind, rain, thunder, and lightning enveloped the area where the ships were anchored, while the shore was bathed in a clear sky with bright stars and moon. After a short while, the rain stopped, and the clouds dispersed. They saw the large ship gradually move away, and then they dared to return to their boat. However, the cypress bed and other items were gone, though the remaining items were still there. The large ship remained on the eastern shore, and someone called out to them, saying, "Do not be angry; we will compensate you for the value of your lost items." The merchant, having lost his goods, returned to Guangling. Upon arriving home, he found that someone had left thirty thousand coins for him, which was placed and then departed. When he asked about the person, it turned out that this happened the day after they had anchored at Guabu. (From Volume 355 of the Yan's Record of the Strange)

    60

    ○浦城人

    　　浦城人，少死于路，家有金一斤，其妇匿之，不闻于其姑。逾年，忽夜扣门，号哭而归。其母惊骇，相与哀恸，曰：“汝真死耶？”曰：“儿实已死，有不平事，是以暂归。”因坐母膝，言语如（《广记》有“平”字）生，但手足冷如水耳。因起握刀，责其妻曰：“我死有金尔，何以（《广记》无“以”字）不供（《广记》有“老”字）母乃（《广记》作“而”）自藏耶？”即往（《广记》作“欲”）杀之，其母曰：“汝已死矣，傥杀尔妻（《广记》“尔妻”作“是人”），必谓我（《广记》作“吾”）所杀也。”于是哭辞母而去，复自提刀送其妻归母（《广记》“归母”作“还父”）家。迨晓及门数十步，忽然不见。（《广记》卷三百五十五，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    60

    A Man from Pucheng

    A man from Pucheng died young on the road, leaving behind one pound of gold at home. His wife concealed it and did not inform his mother-in-law. After a year, he suddenly knocked on the door at night, crying and returning home. His mother was shocked and they both wept together, saying, "Are you truly dead?" He replied, "I am indeed dead, but there are unjust matters, so I have come back temporarily." He sat on his mother's lap, speaking as if alive, but only his hands and feet were cold like water. He then stood up, took a knife, and scolded his wife, saying, "When I died, I had gold, why didn't you provide for your mother and instead hid it for yourself?" He immediately went to kill her, but his mother said, "You are already dead, if you kill your wife, people will surely say that I killed her." He then cried and said goodbye to his mother before leaving, taking the knife and escorting his wife back to his mother's house. Until dawn, when he reached the gate several dozen steps away, he suddenly disappeared. (From Tales of the Taiping Era, Volume 355, also cited in Zeng Zhao's Classical Sayings)

    61

    ○刘道士

    　　庐山道士刘某，将游南岳，路出宜春，宿一村家。其主（《广记》作“家”）至贫，复丧一（《广记》作“其”）子，未有以殓。既夕，忽有一男子行哭而来，但抚膺而号（《广记》作“呼”）曰：“可惜，可惜。”刘出视之，见面白如雪，梳两髻者（《广记》“梳”作“作”，“髻”作“结”，下无“者”字），径入其家，负尸而去（《广记》作“负其尸去”）。莫知所之。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    61

    A Taoist priest named Liu from Mount Lu planned to visit Mount Heng, passing through Yichun City, and stayed overnight at a village household. The host family was extremely poor and had recently lost a son, but they lacked the means to bury him properly. After dusk, a young girl, pale as snow and with two braids, appeared, walking while crying. She entered the house and carried the body away, and no one knew where she went.

    62

    ○清源都将

    　　清源（《广记》有“郡”字）人杨某，为本郡防遏营副将。有大（毛本作空）第在西郭，侵（《广记》作“某”）晨趋府未归，家人方食，忽有一鹅负纸钱自门而入，径诣西郭（《广记》作“廊”）房中，家人云：“此鹅自神祠中来耶？”令其（《广记》“令其”作“乃令”）奴逐之，奴入房，但见一双髻白髯老翁，家人莫不惊走。某归闻之，怒持杖击之，鬼出没四隅，变化倏忽，杖莫能中。某益怒，曰：“食讫当复来击杀（《广记》作“杖”）之。”鬼乃折腰而前口诺。

    Explanation

    62

    A Deputy Commander of Qingyuan

    Yang, a person from Qingyuan (with the word "prefecture" included in the Tales of the Taiping Era), served as the deputy commander of the defensive camp of the prefecture. He had a large mansion in the western suburb (with the Mao Edition omitting the word "large"). Early in the morning (with the Tales of the Taiping Era using the word "dawn"), he went to the government office and had not returned, while his family was just eating. Suddenly, a goose carrying paper money entered through the gate and headed directly to the room in the western suburb (with the Tales of the Taiping Era using the word "hall"). The family said, "Is this goose from the shrine?" They ordered their servant to chase it. The servant entered the room and only saw an elderly man with two braids and a long white beard. The family fled in terror. Upon returning home and hearing about it, Yang became angry and grabbed a stick to hit it. The ghost appeared and disappeared in all four corners, changing suddenly and swiftly, making it impossible for the stick to hit it. Yang became even angrier and said, "After eating, I will come back to kill it with the stick." The ghost then bowed its waist forward and nodded with its mouth.

    63

    杨有女二（《广记》“女二”作“二女”），长女入厨切肉具（《广记》作“且”）食，肉落砧，辄失去。女执刀白父（《广记》“白父”作“向空”）曰：“砧下（《广记》“曰砧下”作“四斫乃”）露一大黑毛手，曰：“请斫。”女走，气殆绝，因而成疾。次女于大瓮中取盐，有一猴自瓮突出，上女之背，女走至堂前，复失之，亦成疾。乃召巫立坛治之，鬼亦立坛作法，愈盛于巫，巫不能制，亦惧而去。顷之，二女及妻皆卒。后有善作魔法者，名曰明教，请为持经。一宿，鬼乃唾骂某而去，因而遂绝。某其年亦卒。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    63

    Yang had two daughters. The eldest daughter entered the kitchen to cut meat and was about to eat it. When the meat fell onto the chopping board, it was immediately lost. The daughter held the knife and said to her father, "A large black hairy hand appeared under the chopping board, saying, 'Please cut.'" The daughter ran away, nearly fainting, and thus fell ill. The younger daughter took salt from a large jar, and a monkey suddenly jumped out of the jar and climbed onto the daughter's back. The daughter ran to the front of the hall, and the monkey was again lost, and she also fell ill. He then summoned a witch to set up a ritual to deal with the situation. The ghost also set up a ritual and performed magic, becoming more powerful than the witch. The witch could not control the ghost and was also afraid to leave. Soon after, the two daughters and his wife all died. Later, a skilled magician named Mingjiao was invited to hold a scripture. After one night, the ghost spat and cursed at him and left. And thus the problem was resolved. He also died that year.

    64

    ○王■〈讠利〉妻

    　　王■〈讠利〉者，南安县大盆（《广记》作“盈”）村人也。妻林氏忽病，有鬼凭之，言：“我陈九娘也，以香花祠我，当有益于主人。”■〈讠利〉许之，乃呼林为阿姐，为人言祸福多中。半岁余（《广记》作“余岁”）乃见形，自腰已下见为（《广记》“见”上有“可”字，无“为”字）人。未尝来者，亦不见也，但以言语相接。乡人有召者，不择远近，与林偕往。

    Explanation

    64

    Wife of Wang Li

    Wang Li, a man from the village of Dapeng (or Ying, according to the Guangji), suddenly fell ill, and a ghost possessed his wife Lin. The ghost said, "I am Chen Jiuniang. Offer incense and flowers to me, and it will be beneficial to the owner." Wang Li agreed, and then called Lin "sister." The ghost often spoke of good and bad fortune, often hitting the mark. After half a year (or more than a year, according to the Guangji), the ghost appeared in physical form, looking like a person below the waist (or could appear as a person, according to the Guangji). Those who had never come also did not appear, but the ghost only communicated through words. When villagers called, the ghost went regardless of distance, accompanying Lin.

    65

    人有祭祀，但具酒食，陈氏自召神名，祝词明惠，听者亡（《广记》作“忘”）倦，林拱坐而已。二年间获利甚溥（《广记》作“博”），一旦忽悲泣，谓林曰：“我累生为人女，年未及笄而夭，问（《广记》作“闻”）于地府，乃前生隐瞒（《广记》作“没”）阿姐钱一（《广记》作“二”）十万，故主者令我为神以偿此钱讫，即生为男子而获寿，今酬已足，请置酒为别。”乃尽见其形，容质端媚，言词婉转，殷勤致谢，呜咽云：“珍重珍重。”遂不复（《广记》无“复”字）见。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    65

    A man performed a ritual sacrifice, preparing only food and drink. Chen summoned the names of the gods, and his blessings were sincere and kind. The listeners did not grow tired, and Lin sat upright and did nothing else. In two years, he gained a great deal of wealth. One day, he suddenly wept and told Lin, "I have been a woman for many lives, and before reaching adulthood, I died young. I asked in the underworld and learned that in my previous life, I hid my elder sister's money of ten thousand (or twenty thousand). So the master ordered me to become a spirit to repay this money. After that, I will be reborn as a man and gain longevity. Now the repayment is complete. Please prepare wine for a farewell." She then fully revealed her form, her appearance graceful and charming, her words gentle and persuasive. She expressed her gratitude earnestly and sobbed, saying, "Take care, take care." She then disappeared. (From Guangji, Volume 355)

    66

    ○林昌业

    　　林昌业者（《广记》无“者”字），漳浦人也。博览典籍，精究术数，性高雅，人不可干。尝为泉州军事衙推，年七十余，退居本郡龙溪县羊额山之阳，乡里宗敬之。有良田数顷，尝欲舂谷为米，载诣州货之。工力未集，忽有一（《广记》“一字”作“双髻”二字）男子，年可三十，髭（《广记》作“须”）髯甚长，来诣林。林问何人，但微笑，唯唯不对。林知其鬼物，令家人食之致饱而去。翌日，忽闻仓下有（《广记》无“有”字）砻谷声，视之乃昨日男子，取谷砻之。（《广记》有“而”字）林问无故辛苦，而（《广记》作“耶”）鬼亦笑不言，复置丰馔饭蔬而已。凡月余砻谷不辍。鬼复自斗量，得米五十余石，拜辞而去，卒无一言，不复再（《广记》无“再”字）来矣。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    66

    Lin Changye

    Lin Changye, a man from Zhangpu, extensively studied classical texts and was an expert in divination. He was of refined character and difficult to approach. He once held the position of military office in Quanzhou. At the age of seventy, he retired to the south side of Yang'e Mountain in Longxi County. The local community respected him. He owned several hectares of good farmland. Once, he intended to grind grain into rice and transport it to the prefecture to sell it. However, the labor force had not yet gathered. Suddenly, a man with twin braids, about thirty years old, with long whiskers, came to visit Lin. Lin asked who he was, but the man only smiled and did not respond. Lin knew he was a ghost and ordered his family to feed him until he was full and then send him away. The next day, Lin suddenly heard the sound of grinding grain in the granary. Looking down, he saw the man from the previous day grinding the grain. Lin asked why he was working so hard, and the ghost only smiled without speaking. Lin provided him with a meal and then left. For over a month, the ghost continued to grind grain without stopping. The ghost then measured the grain himself and obtained over fifty dan of rice. He bowed, bid farewell, and left, finally without a word, and did not return again.

    67

    ○潘袭

    　　潘袭为建安令（曾慥《类说》作“晋安令”），遣一手力，赍牒下乡，有所追摄。手力新受事，未尝行此路。至夕，道左有草舍，扣门求宿。其家惟一妇人应门云：“主人不在，又将移居，无暇延客也。”手力以道远多虎苦（《广记》叠“苦”字）求之，妇人即召入，门侧席地而寝。妇人结束箱箧什器（六字曾慥《类说》作“结草束箱箧”五字）之类，达旦不寐。手力向晓辞去，行数里乃觉失所赍牒，复返求之宿处，乃（《广记》有“是”字）一坟。方见其家人改葬，及开棺，席下得一书，即所失公（《广记》作“之”）牒也。（《广记》卷三百五十五，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    67

    Pān Xí, the Governor of Jian'an (as recorded in Zēng Zào's Lèishuō as "Governor of Jìn'àn"), sent a low-ranking official to deliver a warrant to the countryside. The official was new to the task and had never traveled this route. By evening, he came upon a thatched cottage along the way and knocked on the door to ask for lodging. The woman who answered said, "The owner is not here, and we are about to move, so we have no time to host guests." The official, fearing the long journey and the presence of many tigers, pleaded with her. The woman then let him in, and they slept on the ground. The woman packed boxes and household items and did not sleep until dawn. The official left at dawn and, after walking several miles, realized the document was lost. He returned to the place where he had stayed and found it was a grave. He saw the family performing a secondary burial and, when they opened the coffin, found a document under the mat, which was the lost official warrant. (From Guangji Volume 355, also cited in Zēng Zào's Lèishuō.)

    68

    ○胡澄

    　　池阳人胡澄，佣耕以自给，妻卒，官给棺以葬，其平生服饰悉附棺中。后数年，澄偶至市，见列肆卖首饰者，熟视之乃妻送葬物也，问其人云：“一妇人寄于此，约某日来取。”澄如期复往，果见其妻取直而去。澄因蹑其后，至郊外及之，妻曰：“我昔葬时官给口具（《广记》作“秘器”，曾慥《类说》作“凶器”），虽免暴骨，然至今为所司督责，其直计无所出，卖此以偿之耳。”言讫不见，澄遂为僧焉。（《广记》卷三百五十五，无“焉”字曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    68

    Tru, a man from Chi Yang, worked as a hired farmer to support himself. After his wife's death, the government provided a coffin for her burial, and all her clothing from her lifetime was placed in the coffin. Several years later, Tru stumbled into the market and saw a stall selling jewelry. Upon closer inspection, he realized they were his wife's funeral items. He asked the seller, who said, "A woman left these here and agreed to come back on a certain day to retrieve them." Tru returned on the agreed day and saw his wife take the payment and leave. He then followed her and caught up with her in the outskirts. His wife explained, "When I was buried, the government provided a coffin (the Guangji records it as 'secret coffin,' and Zeng Zao's Leishuo records it as 'funeral coffin'). Although it prevented my bones from being exposed, they are still holding me responsible, and I have no way to pay them back. I'm selling these to repay them." She disappeared after speaking, and Tru then became a monk. (Recorded in Guangji, Volume 355, without the character "焉"; Zeng Zao's Leishuo also records it.)

    69

    ○王攀

    　　高邮县医士（《广记》作“工”）王攀，乡里推其长者。恒往来广陵城东，每数月辄一直县。自念明日当赴县，今夕即欲出东水门，夜泛小舟，及明可至。既而，乃（《广记》无“乃”字）与亲友饮于酒家，不觉大醉，误出参佐门，投一村舍宿。向晓稍醒，东壁有灯而不甚明，仰视屋室知非常宿处。因独叹曰：“吾明日须至县，今在何处（《广记》作“所”）也？”久之，乃闻其内蹑履声。有妇人隔壁问曰：“客将何之？”因起辞谢曰：“欲之高邮，醉中误至于是。

    Explanation

    69

    Mr. Wang Pan, a medical officer of Gaoyou County (or "worker" according to The Record of the Supernatural), was respected by the villagers as a senior figure. He frequently traveled to the east of Guangling City and would go directly to the county every few months. Thinking to himself that he would go to the county tomorrow, he intended to leave through the east water gate that night, sailing a small boat, and by morning he could arrive. Afterward, he drank with friends at a tavern, not realizing he was very drunk, and mistakenly left through the gate of the officials, staying at a village hut. As dawn approached, he began to wake up, noticing a lamp on the east wall that wasn’t very bright. Looking up at the room, he realized it wasn’t his usual place to stay. He sighed to himself, "I must go to the county tomorrow, but where am I now?" After a while, he heard footsteps from inside. A woman from the next room asked, "Where are you going?" He got up and apologized, saying, "I wanted to go to Gaoyou, but I got here by mistake while drunk."

    70

    ”妇曰：“此非高邮道也，吾（《广记》作“将”）使人奉送至城东，无忧也。”乃有一村竖至，随之而行，每历艰险，竖辄以手捧其足而过。既曙，（《广记》作“随”）至城东常宿之店（《广记》作“尝所宿店”），告辞而去，攀解其襦以赠之，竖不受，固与之乃持去。既而入店易衣，又（《广记》作“乃”）见其襦放（《广记》作“故”）在腰下。即复诣宿处寻之，但一（《广记》无“一”字）古冢（《广记》有“耳”字），并无人家。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    　　○郑守澄

    　　广陵裨将郑守澄，新买一小婢。旬日，有夜扣门者，曰：“君家纳（《广记》作“买”）婢，其名籍在此。”（《广记》有“不可留也，开门视之无所见，方怪之。数日广陵大疫此。”二十一字）婢忽（《广记》作“亦”）病，遂卒死（《广记》无“死”字）。既而，守澄亦病卒。而吊客数人转相染著，皆卒，甲寅岁春也。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    70

    A woman said, "This is not the road to Gaoyou. I (or I will) send someone to escort you to the eastern part of the city; there is no need to worry." Then a village boy arrived, and they followed him. Whenever they encountered difficult and dangerous terrain, the boy would lift her feet with his hands to help her pass. As soon as it was dawn, they reached the eastern part of the city, where they stayed at the usual inn (or the inn where they had stayed before). She bade farewell and departed, removing her short-sleeved jacket to give it to the boy, but he refused it. She insisted on giving it to him, and he finally took it away. Shortly after, she entered the inn to change clothes and saw that her jacket was still lying at her waist. She then returned to her lodging to look for it, but found only an ancient tomb (or nothing but an ancient tomb), with no one else around.

    ○ Zheng Shoucheng

    Zheng Shoucheng, a subordinate general from Guangling, had recently bought a young maid. After ten days, someone knocked on the door at night and said, "The maid you purchased is here, and her name is recorded in this register." (The Guangji adds, "She cannot be kept. When the door was opened, no one was seen, and it was only then that they became suspicious. A few days later, a great epidemic broke out in Guangling.") The maid suddenly fell ill and died. Shortly after, Zheng Shoucheng also fell ill and died. Several mourners who came to pay their respects were subsequently infected and also died, all in the spring of the year of the Water Tiger. (From the Guangji, Volume 355)

    71

    ○刘骘

    　　洪州高安人刘骘，少遇乱，有姊曰粪扫，为军将孙金所虏。有妹曰乌头，生十七年而卒。卒后三岁，孙金为常州团练副使，粪扫从其女君会宴于大将陈氏，乃见乌头在焉。问其所从来，云：“顷为人所虏至岳州，与刘翁媪为女，嫁得北来军士任某，任即陈所将卒也，从陈至此尔。”因通信至其家。骘时为县手力，后数年因事至都，遂往毗陵省之。晚止逆旅，翌日先谒孙金，即诣任营中。先遣小仆觇之，方见洒扫庭内，曰：“吾阿兄（《广记》“阿兄”作“兄弟”）将至矣。”仆良久扣门，问为谁，曰：“高安刘家使来。”乃曰：“非（《广记》有“二”字）兄名骘多髯者乎？昨日晚当至，何为迟也？”即自（毛本作“日”）出营门迎之。容貌如故，相见悲泣，了无小异。顷之，孙金遣其诸甥持酒食至任之居，抚（《广记》作“燕”）叙良久。

    Explanation

    71

    ○ Liu Zhi

    Liu Zhi, a native of Gao'an in Hongzhou, was young when he encountered chaos. He had an elder sister named Fensao, who was captured by the military commander Sun Jin. He also had a younger sister named Wutou, who lived for seventeen years and then died. Three years after her death, Sun Jin became the deputy military governor of Changzhou. Fensao attended a banquet hosted by the general Chen with his daughter, where she saw Wutou present. She asked Wutou where she came from, and Wutou replied, "Recently, I was captured and brought to Yue Prefecture, where I became the daughter of Liu (the elder sister's) parents. I married a northern soldier named Ren, who was one of General Chen's soldiers, and came here with Chen." Fensao then sent a message to her family. At the time, Liu Zhi was a county official. A few years later, he went to the capital for official business and then went to Pi Ling to visit her. He stayed at an inn in the evening and the next day first visited Sun Jin, then went to Ren's camp. He sent a small servant to spy on them, and saw that the courtyard was being cleaned. Someone said, "My elder brother (《广记》“阿兄”作“兄弟”) is coming." The servant knocked on the door for a long time and asked who it was. They replied, "It is a messenger from the Liu family of Gao'an." Then they said, "Is it not my elder brother Zhi with many whiskers? He was supposed to arrive last night, why is he late?" Ren then came out of the camp to meet him. They looked the same as before, met and cried, with no small difference. Soon, Sun Jin sent his nephews with wine and food to Ren's residence, and they talked and drank for a long time.

    Translation complete.

    72

    乌头曰：“今日乃得二兄来证我为人，向来（《广记》作“者”）恒为诸兄（《广记》作“儿”）辈呼我为鬼也。”任亦言其举止轻健（《广记》作“捷”），女工敏速，恒夜作至旦，若有人为同作者，饮食必待冷而后食。骘因密问：“汝昔已死，那得至是？”对曰：“兄无为如此问我，将不得相见矣。”骘乃不敢言。久之，任卒，再适军。（《广记》作“隶”）江州陈承昭为高安制置使，召骘问其事，令发墓视之。墓在米岭，无人省视，数十年矣。

    Explanation

    72

    乌头说：“今天终于有两位兄长来证明我的身份，过去他们总是叫我鬼。”任也说她举止轻健，女工敏捷迅速，常常从夜晚工作到天亮，如果有人和她一起工作，食物一定要等凉了才吃。骘于是悄悄地问：“你以前已经死了，怎么会到现在呢？”回答说：“哥哥不要这样问我，否则我们再也不能相见了。”骘于是不敢再问。过了很久，任去世了，她再次嫁给军人。（《广记》作“隶”）江州的陈承昭担任高安制置使，召见骘询问此事，命令打开坟墓查看。坟墓位于米岭，多年来无人照料。

    73

    伐木开路而至，见墓上有穴，大如碗，测其甚深（四字《广记》作“其深不测”）。众惧不敢发，相与退坐大树下，笔疏其事，以白承昭。是岁乌头病，骘往省之，乃曰：“顷为乡人百（《广记》无“百”字）十余辈，持刀仗剑（二字《广记》作“杖劫我”三字），几中我面，故（《广记》无“故”字）我大责骂，力拒之乃退，坐大树下作文书而去，今至举身犹痛。”骘乃知恒出入墓中也。因是亦惧而疏之。罗后移隶晋王城戍。显德五年，周有淮南之地，罗陷没不知所在，时年六十二岁矣。（《广记》卷三百五十五）

    Explanation

    73

    They cut down trees and opened a path to reach the tomb, where they saw a hole as big as a bowl and measured how deep it was (in the Guangji, it reads "its depth is unfathomable"). The crowd was afraid and dared not open it; they all retreated and sat under a big tree, writing down the incident and reporting it to Cheng Zhao. This year, Wutou was ill, and Zhi went to visit him. He said, "Recently, a hundred or so villagers with swords and knives (or 'robbing me with a stick' according to the Guangji), almost hit my face. So, I scolded them severely and resisted them, forcing them to retreat. They sat under a big tree and wrote down their words before leaving. Now, my whole body still hurts." Zhi then knew that he always went in and out of the tomb. Because of this, they were also afraid and recorded it. Afterwards, Luo was transferred to guard the city of Jin Wang. In the fifth year of Xiande, the Zhou dynasty had the land south of the Huai River. Luo was lost, and his whereabouts are unknown. He was sixty-two years old at that time. (From the Guangji, Volume 355)

    74

    ○舒州军吏

    　　王琪为舒州刺史，有军吏方某者，其家忽有鬼降（《广记》作“怪”），自言：“姓杜，年二十，广陵富家子，居通津（《广记》作“肆”）桥之西。前生因（《广记》无“因”字）欠君钱十万，今地府使我为神，偿君此债尔。”因为人占候祸福，其言多中，方以家贫，告琪（《广记》有“求”字）为一镇将，因问鬼：“吾所求可得否？”鬼曰：“诺，吾将问之。”良久乃至曰：“必得之，其镇名一字正方，他不能识矣。”既而得双港镇将，以为其言无验，未及之任，琪忽谓方曰：“适得军牒，军中令一人来为双港镇将，吾今以尔为口镇。”（《广记》有“将”字）竟如其言。比岁余，鬼忽言曰：“吾还君债足。”告别而去，遂寂然。方后至广陵，访得杜氏，问其子弟（《广记》作“弟子”），云：“吾第二子顷忽病如痴人，岁余，今愈矣。”（《广记》卷三百五十八）

    Explanation

    74

    ○舒州军吏

    　　Wang Qi, the governor of Shuzhou, had a military official named Fang. Suddenly, a ghost appeared in his household (in the "Guangji" it is referred to as "a strange occurrence"), and the ghost said, "My name is Du, I am twenty years old, from a wealthy family in Guangling, living west of Tongjin Bridge. In my past life, I owed you ten thousand coins, and now the underworld has made me a god to repay this debt to you." The ghost began to predict good and bad fortune for people, and his predictions often came true. Fang, due to his poverty, asked Qi for the position of a military commander, and then asked the ghost, "Is my request possible?" The ghost replied, "Yes, I will ask about it." After a long time, he returned and said, "You will definitely get it, the name of the town is a single character that is square, others cannot recognize it." Eventually, Fang became the commander of Shuanggang Town, and thinking the ghost's words were not true, he did not take up the position. Suddenly, Qi told Fang, "I just received a military order, the army has ordered someone to come as the commander of Shuanggang Town, I will now appoint you as the commander of a town named Jiankou." (In the "Guangji," there is a "将" character.) It turned out just as he said. After a few years, the ghost suddenly said, "I have repaid your debt." He bid farewell and left, and then there was silence. Later, Fang went to Guangling and found the Du family, asking about their children, and they said, "My second son suddenly fell ill like a madman, after a year, he is now recovered." (From the "Guangji" volume 358)

    75

    ○田頵

    　　宣州节度田頵，将作乱。一日向暮，有鸟赤（毛本作“出”）色，如雉而大，尾有火光如散星之状，自外飞入，止戟门而不见。翌日，府中大火，曹局皆尽，惟甲兵存焉。頵资以起事，明年遂败。（《广记》卷一百四十五，毛本脱“遂败”二字）

    　　○钟传

    　　南平王钟传，在江西，有衙门吏孔知让新治第，昼有一星陨于庭中，知让方（《广记》无“方”字）甚恶之，求典外戎以空其第（《广记》作“地”）。岁余御史中丞薛昭纬贬官至豫章，传取此第以居之，后遂卒于是。（《广记》卷一百四十五，无后字，是作此）

    　　○顿金

    　　袁州刺史顿金，罢郡还都，有人以紫袱包一物诣门遗之。开视则白襽（《广记》误作“栏”）衫也，遽追其人则亡矣。其年金卒。（《广记》一百四十五）

    Explanation

    75

    ○田頵

    The military governor of Xuanzhou, Tian Yuan, was planning to rebel. One evening, a bird with a reddish color, resembling a pheasant but larger, with a tail that had a flame-like appearance, resembling scattered stars, flew in from outside and stopped at the gate, then disappeared. The next day, a major fire broke out in the government office, destroying all departments and offices, leaving only the military equipment intact. Tian Yuan used this as a pretext to start a rebellion, which ultimately failed the following year.

    ○钟传

    The Prince of Nanping, Zhong Chuan, in Jiangxi, had a government office clerk named Kong Zhilang who had newly built a residence. During the day, a star fell in the courtyard. Kong Zhilang was very displeased by this and sought to transfer to an external military post to vacate the residence. More than a year later, the Inspector of Justice Xue Zhaowei was demoted and sent to Yuzhang (present-day Nanchang). Zhong Chuan took up residence in this house and died there.

    ○顿金

    The governor of Yuanzhou, Dun Jin, resigned from his post and returned to the capital. Someone sent a gift wrapped in a purple cloth to his door. When opened, it was a white robe. He immediately tried to find the person, but they had disappeared. That year, Dun Jin died.

    76

    ○宋氏

    　　江西军吏宋氏，尝市木至星子江，见水滨人物喧聚，乃渔人得大鼋，鼋见宋屡顾，宋即以钱一千赎之，放于江中。后数年泊舟龙沙，忽有一仆夫至云：“某长史奉召。”宋恍然不知何长史也，既往，欻至，一府官出迎与坐曰：“君尚相识耶？”宋思之实未尝识，又曰：“君亦记星子江中放鼋耶？”曰：“然。”“我（《广记》作“身”）即鼋也，顷尝有罪，帝命谪为水族，见困于渔人，微君之惠已骨朽矣。今已得为九江长，予将（二字《广记》作“相召者”三字）有以奉报。君之儿某者，命当溺死，名籍在是，后数日乌山神将朝庐山，使者行必以疾风雨，君儿当以此时死。今有一人名姓正同，亦当溺死，但先期岁月间耳，吾取以代之，君儿宜速登岸避匿，不然不免。”宋陈谢而出，不觉已在舟次矣。数日，果有风涛之害，死者甚众，宋氏之子竟免。（《广记》卷四百七十一）

    Explanation

    76

    The Song Family

    A military official named Song from Jiangxi once bought wood and arrived at the Xingzi River. He saw a gathering of people by the water, and it turned out to be a fisherman who had caught a large turtle. The turtle looked at Song repeatedly, so Song redeemed it with a thousand coins and released it into the river. Several years later, Song anchored his boat at Longsha. Suddenly, a servant came and said, "A certain Censor-in-Chief has summoned you." Song was suddenly unsure which Censor-in-Chief it was. He went, and the official appeared abruptly. A government official came out to welcome and sit with him, saying, "Do you still recognize me?" Song thought for a moment and realized he had never met this official before. The official then said, "Do you also remember when I was released from the Xingzi River?" Song replied, "Yes." "I am the turtle," the official said, "I once committed a sin, and the emperor ordered me to be exiled to the water creatures. I was trapped by fishermen. Without your kindness, I would have turned to bones. Now I have become the ruler of the Nine Rivers. I will have something to repay you. Your son, whose name is [name], is destined to drown. His name is recorded here. In a few days, the Black Mountain deity will pay homage to Mount Lu. The envoy will travel with strong winds and heavy rain. Your son will die at this time. Now there is a person with the same name and surname, who is also destined to drown. But it will happen a few years earlier. I will take his place. Your son should quickly go ashore and hide. Otherwise, he cannot escape." Song thanked the official and left, not realizing he was already back on the boat. A few days later, there was indeed a storm, and many people died. Song's son was saved.

    77

    ○史氏女

    　　溧水五坛村人史氏女，莳田困（毛本“莳田”作“因莳”）倦，偃息树下，见一物鳞角爪距可畏，来据其上。已而有娠，生一鲤鱼，养于盆中，数日益长，乃置投金濑中。顷之，有（《广记》“有”字作“村中”二字）人刈草，误断其尾，鱼即奋跃而去，风雨随之，入太湖而止。家亦渐富，其后女卒，每寒食其鱼辄从群鱼一至墓前，至今每闰年一至尔。有渔人李黑獭，恒张网于江，忽获一婴儿，长可三尺，为网乱纟延所萦，浃旬不解。有道士见之曰：“可取铁汁灌之。”如其言遂解。视婴儿口鼻眉发如画，而无肩，（《广记》作“目”）口犹有酒气，众惧，复投于江（毛本“江”下有“而去矣”三字）。（《广记》卷四百七十一）

    Explanation

    77

    A Woman from the Shi Family

    A woman from the Shi family in Wutan Village, Lizhui, was tired from weeding the fields and lay down to rest under a tree. She saw a creature with scales, horns, claws, and spurs that was frightening, which came and sat on her. Soon after, she became pregnant and gave birth to a carp, which she raised in a basin. The carp gradually grew larger, and she then released it into the Jin River. Shortly after, someone from the village was cutting grass and accidentally cut off the carp's tail. The carp struggled and swam away, accompanied by wind and rain, and entered the Taihu Lake. The family gradually became wealthy. After the woman died, every Tomb-Sweeping Day, the carp would come with other fish to her grave. This continues to happen every leap year. There was a fisherman named Li Heita who often set a net in the river. One day, he suddenly caught a baby about three feet long, which was caught in the tangled net for ten days without being freed. A Taoist priest saw the baby and said, "You can pour molten iron over it." Following his advice, the entanglement was resolved. The baby's eyes, nose, eyebrows, and hair were as beautiful as a painting, but it had no shoulders (or eyes, according to the "Guangji"). Its mouth still had the look of drunkenness. The people were afraid and threw the baby back into the river and left. (From the "Guangji," Volume 471)

    78

    ○渔人

    　　近有渔人泊舟马当山下，月明风细（《广记》作“恬”），见一大鼋出水直上山顶，引首四望。顷之，江水中涌出一彩舟，有十余人会饮酒，妓乐陈设甚盛，献寿（《广记》作“酬”）久之。上流有巨舰来下，橹声振于坐中，彩舟乃没，前之鼋亦下，未及（《广记》有“水”字）死于岸侧。意者水神使此鼋为候望，而不知巨舰之来，故殛之。（《广记》卷四百七十一）

    Explanation

    78

    The Fisherman

    Recently, a fisherman anchored his boat at the foot of Mount Madang. Under the bright moon and gentle breeze, he saw a large turtle emerge from the water and ascend directly to the top of the mountain, lifting its head to look around. Soon after, a brightly decorated boat emerged from the river, with more than ten people gathered for drinking. Music and entertainment were set up in great abundance, and they celebrated for a long time. Upstream, a large ship approached, and the sound of oars was heard among the guests. The brightly decorated boat then submerged, and the turtle also descended, not reaching the shore in time to die there. It seems that the water god had sent this turtle as a lookout, but it was unaware of the large ship's approach, and thus was punished. (From Volume 411 of the Guangji)

    79

    ○阎居敬

    　　新安人阎居敬，所居为山水所侵（《广记》作“浸”），恐屋壤，移榻于户外而寝。梦一乌衣人曰：“君避水在此，我亦避水至此，于君何害？而迫逐我如是，不快甚矣。”居敬寤，不测其故，尔夕三梦，居敬曰：“岂吾不当止此耶？”因命移床，乃床脚压一龟，于户限外放之而去。（《广记》卷四百七十二）

    　　○池州民

    　　池州民杨氏以卖鮓为业。尝烹鲤鱼十枚（《广记》作“头”），令儿守之，将熟，忽闻釜中乞命者数四，儿惊惧，走告其亲，往视之，釜中无复一鱼，求之不得。期年所蓄犬恒窥户限下而吠，数日，其家人曰：“去年鲤鱼得非在此耶？”即撤视之，得龟十头，送之水中，家亦无恙。（《广记》卷四百七十二）

    Explanation

    79

    ○阎居敬

    A man from Xian'an named Yan Jujing lived in a house that was being threatened by water. Fearing that the house would be damaged, he moved his bed outside to sleep. One night, he dreamed of a person dressed in black clothes who said, "You are avoiding the water here, and I am also avoiding the water here. What harm have I done to you? Yet you treat me as if I were a threat, which is very unpleasant." Upon waking, Yan Jujing did not understand the reason for the dream. That same evening, he had the same dream three times. He thought, "Perhaps I should not stay here?" So he ordered his bed to be moved. When the bed was moved, he discovered that the bed leg was pressing down on a turtle, which he then released outside the threshold.

    ○池州民

    A family from Chizhou named Yang sold pickled fish as their livelihood. One day, they cooked ten heads of carp and had a child watch over them. As the fish were cooking, the child suddenly heard the fish begging for their lives four times. The child was frightened and ran to tell his parents. Upon checking, they found that there was no fish left in the pot, and they could not find any. After a year, the family's dog would constantly bark at the threshold. One day, the family said, "Could the carp we cooked last year not be here?" They removed the floorboards to look underneath and found ten turtles. They released the turtles into the water, and the family remained unharmed.

    80

    ○李宗

    　　李宗为楚州刺史，郡中有尼，方行于市，忽踞地而坐，不可推动，不食不语者累日。所有司以告，宗命武士扶起，掘其地得大龟，长数尺，送之江中，其尼乃愈。（《广记》卷四百七十二）

    　　○渔人妻

    　　瓜村有渔人妻，得劳瘦（《广记》无“瘦”字）疾，转相传染（《广记》“传染”作“染著”），死者数人。或云取病者生钉棺中，弃之，其病可绝。顷之，其女病，即生钉棺中，流之于江，至金山有渔人见而异之，引之至岸，开视之见女子犹活，因取置渔舍中（《广记》无“中”字），多得鳗鮓鱼以食之。久之病愈，遂为渔人之妻，至今尚无恙。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    Explanation

    80

    Final Translation

    李宗

    Li Zong, the governor of Chuzhou, reported that in his jurisdiction, there was a nun who was walking in the market when she suddenly sat cross-legged on the ground, unable to be moved, and did not eat or speak for several days. Upon hearing this, Li Zong ordered soldiers to lift her up. They dug the ground and found a large turtle, several feet long, which they sent into the river. The nun then recovered. (From Taiping Guangji, Volume 472)

    渔人妻

Someone suggested that the sick person be nailed alive into a coffin and thrown into the river, which would cure the disease. Soon after, the woman's daughter fell ill, so they n

    81

    ○陈寨

    　　陈寨者，泉州晋江巫也。善禁咒之术，为人治疾多效（《广记》作“愈”）者。澶（《广记》作“漳”，漳上有“有”字）州逆旅苏猛，其子病狂，人莫能疗，乃往请陈。陈至，苏氏子见之，戟手大骂。寨曰：“此疾入心矣。”乃立坛于堂中，戒人无得窃视，至夜乃取苏氏子劈为两片，悬堂之东壁，其心悬北檐下。寨方在堂中作法，所悬之心遂为犬食，寨求之不得，惊惧，乃持刀宛转于地，出门而去。主人弗知，谓其作法耳。食顷，乃持心而入，内于病者之腹，被发连叱，其腹遂合。苏氏子既寤（《广记》作“悟”），但连呼递铺递铺，家人莫之测。乃其日去家十（《广记》作“数”）里，有驿吏手持官文书死于道傍。初，南中驿路二十里置一递铺，吏持符牒以次传授，欲近前铺，辄连呼以警之。乃寨取驿吏之心而活苏氏，苏遂愈如故。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    81

    Translation:

    Tanchai

    Tanchai was a sorcerer from Jinjiang, Quanzhou. He was skilled in the art of exorcism and magical spells, and he often successfully treated many illnesses. In Changzhou, Su Meng, an innkeeper, had a son who was suffering from madness, and no one could cure him. Su then went to invite Tanchai. When Tanchai arrived, the son of Su saw him and gestured with his hand like a spear while shouting abuse. Tanchai said, "This illness has entered his heart." Then he set up an altar in the hall and warned people not to peek. At night, he took the son of Su, cut him into two pieces, and hung him on the eastern wall of the hall, with his heart hanging under the northern eaves. While Tanchai was performing his rituals in the hall, the heart that was hanging was eaten by a dog. Tanchai searched for it but could not find it, and he was filled with fear. He then held a knife, twisted and turned on the ground, and left the house. The host did not know what had happened and thought it was part of Tanchai's ritual. After a short while, Tanchai returned with the heart, placed it inside the patient's abdomen, and shouted while disheveled. The patient's abdomen then closed. The son of Su then woke up and kept calling out, "Post station, post station," which puzzled the family. That day, several miles away from home, a postal official was found dead by the roadside, holding official documents. Initially, in the southern regions, a post station was set up every twenty li along the postal route. The official held the documents and passed them on in sequence. To alert the next post station, he would repeatedly shout. It turned out that Tanchai had taken the heart of the postal official to heal the son of Su, and Su then recovered as before. (From The Strange Tales of Liaozhai, Volume 202)

    82

    ●卷四

    　　○陶俊

    　　江南吉州刺史张曜卿有傔力曰（《广记》作“者”）陶俊，性谨直。尝从军征江西，为飞石所中，因有腰足之疾，恒扶杖而行。张命守舟于广陵之江口，因至白沙市中（《广记》无“中”字），避雨于酒肆。同立者甚众，有二书生过于前，独顾俊相与言曰：“此人好心，宜为疗其疾。”即呼俊，与药二丸曰：“服此即愈。”乃去，后归舟吞之。良久，觉腹中痛楚甚，顷之痛止，疾亦都（《广记》作“多”）瘥。操篙理缆，尤觉轻捷（《广记》作“健”），白沙去城八十里，一日复还（《广记》复还“作往复”），不以为劳。后访二书生，竟不复见。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    Explanation

    82

    Volume 4

    Tao Jun

    Zhang Yaoying, the Prefect of Jizhou in Jiangnan, had a personal attendant named Tao Jun, who was diligent and straightforward. Once, he served in the military in Jiangxi and was struck by a flying stone, resulting in a leg or foot ailment. He always walked with a cane. Zhang ordered him to guard the boat at the river mouth of Guangling. One day, he sheltered from the rain in a wine shop. There were many people standing together, and two scholars passed by. They looked at Jun alone and spoke to him, saying, "This person has a good heart. He should treat his illness." They immediately called Jun and gave him two pills, then left. Later, back at the boat, he swallowed them. After a while, he felt severe pain in his abdomen, but soon the pain stopped, and his illness also completely healed. He especially felt agile when handling the oar and managing the rope. Baisha is eighty li away from the city, and one day he returned, not considering it tiring. Later, he sought out the two scholars, but never saw them again. (From Yingyai Shenglan, Volume 220)

    83

    ○延陵村人妻

    　　延陵灵宝观道人谢及（《广记》作“又”，下同）损，近县村人。有丧妇者，请及损为斋。妇死已半月矣，忽闻摧（《广记》作“推”）棺而呼，众皆惊走，其夫开棺视之，乃起坐。顷之，能言，云：“为舅姑所召去，云‘我此无人，使之执爨。’其居处甚闲洁，但苦无水，一日见沟中水甚清，因取以酿（《广记》作“漉”）馈，姑见之大怒曰：‘我不知尔不洁如是，用尔何为？’”乃（《广记》作“因”）逐之使回，走出门遂苏。今尚无恙。（《广记》卷三百八十六）

    Explanation

    83

    The Wife of a Villager in Yanling

    Xie Ji, a Taoist priest at the Lingbao Temple in Yanling, was asked by the villagers to perform a ritual. A woman who had died half a month ago suddenly called out from her coffin, startling everyone. Her husband opened the coffin and saw her sitting up. Soon, she was able to speak, saying that her mother-in-law and father-in-law had summoned her to their home, telling her, "We have no one here, so we need you to cook." Her living conditions in the afterlife were very clean and orderly, but she was troubled by the lack of water. One day, she saw clear water in a ditch and tried to pour it. Her mother-in-law saw this and became very angry, saying, "I didn't know you were so unclean. What use are you?" She then sent her back, and as soon as she stepped out of the door, she revived. She is still alive and well today.

    (From the Guangji 卷三百八十六)

    84

    ○赵某妻

    　　丁亥岁（案：丁亥当唐天成二年），浙西有典客吏赵某，妻死未及旬将葬（三字《广记》作“大殓”二字），忽大叫而活，云：“为一（《广记》无“一”字）吏所录，至鹤林门，内有府署，侍卫严整，官吏谘（《广记》有“事”字）及领囚集（《广记》作“禁”）者甚众。吏持已入（毛本“已入”作“几人”），至庭下，堂上一绿衣、一白衣偶坐，绿衣谓吏曰：‘汝误，非此人也，急遣之。’白衣曰：‘已迫至此，何用遣之？’（《广记》作“禁”）绿衣不从，相质食顷，绿衣怒叱吏遣之。吏持（毛本作“时”）己疾趋，出路经一桥，数十人（“数十人”毛本作“数日”）方修桥，其（《广记》作“无”）板有钉，吏持之走过，钉伤足。因痛失声，遂活。”视足果伤。俄而邻妇遂（《广记》作暴）卒，不复苏矣。（《广记》卷三百八十六）

    Explanation

    84

    Translation:

    The Wife of Zhao

    In the year Dinghai (which corresponds to the second year of the Tiancheng era during the Later Tang dynasty), there was a guest official named Zhao in Zhejiang West. His wife had died less than ten days ago and was about to be buried. Suddenly, she cried out and came back to life, saying, "I was summoned by an official and taken to the Gate of the Crane Forest. Inside, there was an office with strictly organized guards, and many officials and prisoners were gathered, with officials consulting and managing the prisoners. The official who took me had already entered the courtyard and led me to the hall below. Two officials, one wearing green and the other white, were sitting together. The green-clad official said to the clerk, 'You made a mistake; this is not the right person. Release him quickly.' The white-clad official said, 'He has already been brought this far; why release him?' The green-clad official did not agree and, after discussing for a mealtime duration, angrily ordered the clerk to release me. The clerk, holding me, hurriedly fled. On the way out, we passed a bridge where many people were repairing it. The planks of the bridge had nails, and as the clerk carried me across, the nails injured my foot. I cried out in pain and came back to life." Upon inspection, it was found that my foot was indeed injured. Soon after, the neighbor's wife suddenly died and did not revive.

    85

    ○建业妇人

    　　近岁建业有妇人，背生一瘤，大如数斗，囊中有物，如茧粟甚众，行即有声。恒乞于市，自言村妇也，尝与娣（毛本作“姊”）姒辈分养蚕，已独频年损耗，因窃（毛本“因窃”作“窃以”）其姒囊茧焚之，顷之背患此疮，渐成此瘤。以衣覆之，即气闭闷，常露之乃可，而重如负囊矣（《广记》卷一百三十三引作《搜神记》。按：今人李剑国考证，此条当为《稽神录》佚文，《广记》误）。

    Explanation

    85

    A Woman from Jianye

    In recent years, a woman in Jianye had a tumor growing on her back, as large as several dou (a unit of volume). Inside the tumor were numerous items resembling cocoons and millet grains, and it made a sound when she walked. She constantly begged in the market, claiming to be a village woman. She used to raise silkworms with her sisters-in-law, but she alone suffered frequent losses. One day, she stole and burned her sister-in-law's silkworm cocoons. Soon after, she developed this sore, which gradually became this tumor. If she covered it with clothing, she became suffocated; she must keep it exposed, but it was as heavy as carrying a bag. (This story is referenced in the Guangji (Encyclopedia of the Supernatural) as part of the Soushenji (Records of the Supernatural). According to modern scholar Li Jian Guo, this entry is likely from the Jishenlu (Record of Supernatural Events), and the Guangji mistakenly attributed it to the Soushenji.)

    86

    ○广陵男子

    　　广陵有男子行乞于市，每见马矢，即取食。自云：“常为人饲马，慵不能夜起，其主恒自检视，见槽中无草，督责之，乃取乌梅饼以饲马，马齿酸楚，不能食，竟致死。”已（毛本作“亡”）后因患病，见马矢辄流涎欲食，食之与乌梅味正同，了无秽气。（《广记》卷一百三十三）

    　　○施汴

    　　庐州营田吏施汴，尝恃势夺民田数十顷，其主遂为其耕夫，不能自理。数年汴卒，其田主家生一牛，腹下有白毛，方数寸，既长稍斑驳，不逾年成施汴字，点画无缺。道士邵修默亲见之。（《广记》卷一百三十四）

    Explanation

    86

    A Man from Guangling

    There was a man from Guangling who begged in the market. Whenever he saw horse droppings, he would take and eat them. He said, "I used to feed horses for others, but I was too lazy to get up at night. My master would always check himself, and seeing no grass in the manger, he would scold me. Then I would take plum cakes to feed the horse, but the horse's teeth were sore, it couldn't eat, and eventually died." Afterwards, he fell ill, and whenever he saw horse droppings, he would drool and want to eat them. Eating them tasted exactly like plum cakes, with no foul smell. (From The Strange Tales Volume 133)

    Shi Bian

    Shi Bian, a land steward in Luyang, once used his power to seize dozens of acres of farmland from the people. The landowners then became his laborers and could not manage their own affairs. Several years later, when Shi Bian died, a cow was born in the family of one of the landowners. The cow had a patch of white hair on its belly, measuring several inches square. As the cow grew, the white hair became slightly speckled, and within a year, it formed the characters of Shi Bian's name, with no missing strokes. The Taoist priest Shao Xiemo personally saw this. (From The Strange Tales Volume 134)

    87

    ○朱庆源

    　　婺源尉朱庆源，罢任方还家，在豫章之丰城，庭中地甚爽垲，忽生莲一枝。其家骇惧，多方以禳之，莲生不已，乃筑堤堰（《广记》作“汲”）水以沼（《广记》作“回”）之，遂成大池，芡荷甚茂。其年庆源（《广记》有“选”字）授南奉令，后三岁入为大理评事。（《广记》卷一百三十八）

    　　○僧十朋

    　　刘建封寇豫章，僧十朋与其徒奔分宁，宿澄心僧院。初夜见窗外有光，视之见团火高广数尺，中有金车子，与火俱行，呕轧有声。十朋始惧，其主人云：“见之数年矣。每夜必出于西（《广记》作“东”）堂西北隅地中，绕堂（《广记》作“屋”）数周，复没于此。以其不为祸福，故无掘视之者。”（《广记》卷三百六十六）

    Explanation

    87

    Final Translation

    朱庆源

    The magistrate of Wuyuan, Zhu Qingyuan, had just been dismissed from his post and was returning home. He was in Fengcheng, within the jurisdiction of Yuzhang. The ground in his courtyard was very dry and cool, but suddenly a lotus sprouted. His family was terrified and tried various methods to ward it off, but the lotus continued to grow. They then built a dike to channel water and create a pond, which eventually became a large pond filled with lush lotus and water chestnut. That year, Zhu Qingyuan was selected and appointed as the magistrate of Nanfeng, and three years later, he was promoted to the position of a judge in the Dali Temple. (From Volume 138 of The Book of Swindles)

    僧十朋

    Liu Jianfeng invaded Yuzhang, and the monk Shi Peng and his disciples fled to Fenning, where they stayed at the Clear Mind Monastery. Early in the night, he saw light outside the window. Looking out, he saw a ball of fire several feet high and wide, with a golden carriage in the middle. It moved with the fire, making a rumbling sound. Shi Peng was initially afraid. The owner said, "I have seen it for several years now. Every night it appears in the northwest corner of the west hall, circles around the hall several times, and then disappears there. Because it does not bring disaster or benefit, no one has dug to see it." (From Volume 366 of The Book of Swindles)

    88

    ○宜春人

    　　天祐初，有人游宜春之（《广记》作“止”）空宅中。兵革之后，井邑芜没，堂西屋（《广记》作“至”）梁上有小窗，外隙荒数十亩。日暮窗外，有一物正方，自下而上，顷之全蔽其窗。其人引弓射之，应弦而落。时已夕，不能仰（《广记》作“即”）视，明旦寻之，西百余步，有方杉木板，带一矢，即昨所射也。（《广记》卷三百六十六）

    　　○朱从本

    　　李遇为宣武节度使，军政委大将朱从本。其（《广记》作“本”）家究中畜猴，圉人夜起秣马，见一物如驴，黑而毛，手足皆如人，据地而食此猴，见人乃弃（《广记》作“去”）猴，已食其半。明年遇族诛。宣城故老云：“郡中常有此怪，每军城有变，此物辄出，出则满城皆臭。田頵将败，出于街中，巡夜者见之不敢逼，旬月祸及。”（《广记》卷三百三十六）

    Explanation

    88

    Translation

    The Man from Yichun

    At the beginning of the Tianyou era, there was a man who wandered into an abandoned house in Yichun. After the turmoil of war, the villages and towns were overgrown and deserted. In the western part of the house, there was a small window on the beam, with a gap leading to a wasteland of several acres outside. As dusk fell, a square object appeared outside the window, moving from below upwards, and soon completely obscured the window. The man drew his bow and shot at it, and it fell upon the string. By then, it was already evening, and he could not look up to see it clearly. The next morning, he searched for it and found a square piece of fir wood, with an arrow embedded in it, exactly what he had shot the previous day. (From Guangji, Volume 366)

    Zhu Congben

    Li Yu served as the military governor of the Xuanwu region, and military affairs were entrusted to the general Zhu Congben. In Zhu's household, there were monkeys kept in the stables. One night, a stable boy got up to feed the horses and saw an object like a donkey, black and covered in hair, with hands and feet like a human. It sat on the ground eating the monkey, and when it saw a person, it abandoned the monkey, having eaten half of it. The following year, Li Yu was exterminated along with his entire family. An old man from Xuancheng said: "There is often such a strange creature in the county. Every time there is a change in the military city, this creature appears. When it appears, the whole city smells. Tian Jun was about to be defeated, and this creature appeared in the street. The night patrol saw it but dared not approach. Within a month, disaster befell them." (From Guangji, Volume 336)

    89

    ○周本

    　　信州刺史周本，入觐扬都，舍于邸第，遇私讳日，独宿外斋，张灯而寐。未熟，闻室中有声划然，视之见火炉冉冉而上，直抵（《广记》作“博”）于屋，良久乃下，飞灰勃然。明日满室浮埃覆物，亦无他怪。（《广记》卷三百六十六）

    　　○薛老峰

    　　福州城中有乌石山，山（《广记》“山”在“峰”字下）有大峰，凿三字曰薛老峰。癸卯岁，一夕间（《广记》“间”在“雨”字下）大风雨，山上如数千人喧噪之声。及旦，则薛老峰倒立，峰字返向上，城中石碑皆自转侧，其年闽亡。（《广记》卷三百三十六）

    Explanation

    89

    ○ Zhou Ben

    Governor Zhou Ben of Xinzhou paid a formal visit to Yangzhou, staying at an official residence. On a day of personal taboo, he slept alone in an outer study, lighting a lamp to sleep. Before falling asleep, he heard a sudden, clear sound in the room. Looking, he saw a fire stove slowly rising, reaching directly to the ceiling (or spreading, according to the note). After a long time, it descended, and flying ash appeared suddenly. The next day, the entire room was covered with floating dust, but there were no other strange occurrences.

    ○ Xue Lao Peak

    In the city of Fuzhou, there is Wusi Mountain, on which there is a large peak, carved with three characters called Xue Lao Peak. In the year of Gui Mao, a heavy rainstorm occurred overnight, and the mountain sounded like thousands of people making loud noises. By dawn, Xue Lao Peak was standing on its head, the characters on the peak turned upward, and all the stone tablets in the city turned over. That year, the region of Fujian fell.

    90

    ○王慎辞

    　　江南通事舍人王慎辞，有别墅在广陵城西，慎辞尝与亲友宴（《广记》无“宴”字）游于其上。一日忽自爱其冈（《广记》作“岗”）阜之势，叹曰：“我死必葬于此。”是夜村中闻犬吠，或起视之，见慎辞独骑徘徊于此，逼而视（《广记》无“而视”二字）之，遂不见。自是夜夜恒至，月余慎辞卒，竟葬其地。（《广记》卷一百四十五）

    　　○姚氏

    　　东州静海军姚氏，率其徒捕海鱼以充岁贡。时已将晚，而得鱼殊少，方忧之，忽网中获（毛本“获”在“网”字上）一人，黑色，举身长毛，拱手而立，问之不应。海师曰：“此所谓海人，见必有灾，请杀之以塞其咎。”姚曰：“此神物也，杀之不祥。”乃释而祝之曰：“尔能为我致群鱼以免阙职之罪，信为神矣。”毛人却行水上，数十步而没。明日，鱼乃大获，倍于常岁矣。（《广记》卷四百七十一）

    Explanation

    90

    Translation

    ○ Wang Shendici

    Wang Shendici, an official of the Southern Region known as the Tongshi She Ren, had a villa in the western part of Guangling City. Shendici once feasted and played with relatives and friends there. One day, he suddenly admired the beauty of the hills and exclaimed, "When I die, I will surely be buried here." That night, the villagers heard dogs barking. Some got up to investigate and saw Shendici riding alone, wandering around the area. They approached him closely, but he disappeared. From then on, every night he would come, and after a month, Shendici passed away and was indeed buried there. (From Volume 145 of the Guangji)

    ○ Yao Shi

    Yao Shi of the Eastern State Navy led his disciples to catch sea fish to fulfill the annual tribute. By evening, they had caught very few fish, and they were worried. Suddenly, they caught one person in the net, who was black, covered in long hair, and stood with hands clasped. When they asked him, he did not respond. The sea captain said, "This is what is called a sea person. Seeing him will bring disaster. Please kill him to avert the calamity." Yao Shi replied, "This is a divine being. It is inauspicious to kill him." So, he released the person and said, "If you can bring me a school of fish to avoid the fault of failing in my duties, truly you are a god." The person walked on the water and disappeared after several dozen steps. The next day, they caught a large number of fish, double the usual amount. (From Volume 471 of the Guangji)

    ○彭顒

    　　宣州盐铁院官彭顒，常病数月，恍惚不乐，每出外厅，辄见俳优乐工数十人，长皆（《广记》作“皆长”）数寸，合（毛本作“金”）奏百戏，并作朱紫炫目。顒视之移（《广记》作“或”）时，欣笑或愤懑，然无如之何，他人不见也。顒后病愈，亦不复见，后十余年乃卒。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    　　○吕师造

    　　吕师造为池州刺史，颇聚敛。常嫁女于扬都，资送甚厚，使家人送之。晚泊竹筱江，岸上忽有一道士，状若狂人，来去奔走，忽跃入舟，直穿舟中过，随其所经，火即大发，复登后船，火亦随之。凡所载之舟（《广记》作“物”），皆为煨烬。一老婢发（《广记》“发”下有“亦尽”二字，无“尺”字）尺余，人与船了无所损失（《广记》，“失”字作火灭二字）。道士亦不复见。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    Explanation

    91

    Translation:

    Peng Ying

    Peng Ying, an official in charge of salt and iron affairs in Xuanzhou, suffered from illness for several months, feeling restless and unhappy. Whenever he stepped out of the outer hall, he would see dozens of actors and musicians, all a few inches tall, performing various entertainments and dressed in brightly colored attire. Peng Ying would watch them for a time, sometimes laughing joyfully or feeling frustrated, but he could do nothing about it. Others could not see them. After his illness healed, he no longer saw the apparitions, and he passed away ten years later.

    Lü Shizao

    Lü Shizao served as the governor of Chizhou and was known for his accumulation of wealth. He once married off his daughter to Yangzhou, with generous gifts, and sent his family to accompany her. One evening, they anchored at Zhuxiao River. Suddenly, a Taoist priest appeared on the shore, looking like a madman, running back and forth. He suddenly leaped onto the boat, passing through the middle of it, and wherever he went, fire immediately broke out. He then jumped onto the next boat, and fire followed him as well. All the boats (or items) they were carrying were reduced to ashes. An elderly maid had her hair burned more than a foot long, but no one was harmed, and no boats were lost. The Taoist priest disappeared after the incident.

    ○崔彦章

    　　饶州刺（《广记》脱“刺”字）史崔彦章，送客于城东，方燕，忽有一（《广记》无“一”字）小车，其色如金，高尺余，巡席而行，若有求觅，至彦章（《广记》有“前”字）遂止不行。彦章（六字《广记》无）因即绝倒，携（《广记》无“携”字）舆（“舆”字毛本作“与”）归州而卒。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    　　○润州气

    　　戊子（案：戊子当唐天成三年）岁，润州有气如虹，五彩夺目，有首如驴，长数十丈，环厅事而立（《广记》无“立”字），行三周而灭。占者曰：“厅中将有哭声，然非州府之咎也。”顷之，其国太后殂，发丧（《广记》作“哀”）于此堂。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    92

    Translation

    Cui Yan Zhang

    The Governor of Raozhou, Cui Yan Zhang, was sending guests off to the east of the city and was just having a banquet. Suddenly, there appeared a small carriage, golden in color, about a foot tall, circling the table as if seeking something. When it reached Cui Yan Zhang, it stopped and would not move. Cui Yan Zhang then collapsed in shock and was carried back to the state and died.

    The Qi of Runzhou

    In the year 928 AD (the third year of the Tiancheng era), there was a qi in Runzhou like a rainbow, multicolored and dazzling, with a head like a donkey, several dozen feet long. It circled the hall, going around three times before vanishing. The diviner said, "There will be crying sounds in the hall, but it is not the fault of the state or the governor." Soon after, the太后 of the country died, and the funeral was held in this hall.

    ○黄极

    　　甲午岁（案：甲午当唐应顺元年），江西馆驿巡官黄极子妇生男（《广记》无“子”字），一首两身相背，四手四足。建昌民家生牛，每一足更附出一足，投之江中。翌日，浮于水上。南昌新义里地陷长数十步，广者数丈，狭者七八尺，其年节度使徐知询卒。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    　　○熊勋

    　　军吏熊勋，家于建康长乐坡（《广记》作“漫”）之东。尝（《广记》作“常”）日晚见屋上有二物，大如卵，赤而有光，往来相驰逐。家人骇惧，有亲客壮勇，登（毛本作“开”）屋捕之，得其（毛本无“其”字）一，乃被（《广记》作“辟”）缯彩，包一鸡卵壳也。锉而焚之，臭闻数里。其一走去不复来矣，家亦无恙。（《广记》卷三百六十七引不注出处。按：明钞本《广记》引作《稽神录》）
