    Translation

    ○黄极

    In the year Jia Wu (which corresponds to the first year of the Yingshun era during the Tang Dynasty), the wife of a son of Huang Ji, an official overseeing inns in Jiangxi Province, gave birth to a boy with one head but two bodies facing opposite directions, each with four arms and four legs. A household in Jianchang gave birth to a cow with an extra foot attached to each of its feet. The cow was thrown into the river, but the next day, it floated on the water. In Xinyi of Nanchang, a section of land sank, measuring several zhang in width and several chi in narrowness. That same year, the Jiedushi Xu Zhiqun died. (From the Guangji Volume 367)

    ○熊勋

    The military official Xiong Xun lived east of Changle Slope in Jiankang. One evening, he saw two objects on the roof of his house, each as large as an egg, red and glowing, moving back and forth and chasing each other. The family was terrified. A brave and strong relative climbed onto the roof to catch them and managed to catch one. It turned out to be wrapped in brocade, containing the shell of a chicken egg. He cut it up and burned it, and the smell spread for several li. The other one ran away and did not return, and the family was also unharmed. (From the Guangji Volume 367, cited without specific source. According to the Ming edition of the Guangji, this is from the Ji Shen Lu.)

    ○王建封

    　　江南军使王建封，骄恣奢攒。筑大第于淮之南，暇日临街坐窗下，见一老妪携少女过于前，衣服缢缕而姿色绝世。建封呼问之，云：“孤贫无依，乞食至此。”建封曰：“吾纳尔女，而给养以（《广记》作“尔”）终身可乎？”妪欣然。建封即召入，命取新衣二袭以衣之，妪及女始脱故衣，皆化（《广记》无“化”字）为凝血（《广记》有“聚”字）于地。旬月建封被诛。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    　　○广陵士人

    　　广陵有士人，尝（《广记》作“常”）张灯独寝。一夕中夜而坐（《广记》作“寐”），忽有双髻青衣女子，姿（《广记》作“资”）质甚丽，熟寐于其足。某知其妖物也，惧不敢近，复寝如故，向晓乃失，门户犹（《广记》有故“字”）扃鐍（《广记》作“闭”）。后（《广记》无“后”字）自是夜夜恒至。

    94

    王建封

    江南军使王建封，骄恣奢攒。筑大第于淮之南，暇日临街坐窗下，见一老妪携少女过于前，衣服缢缕而姿色绝世。建封呼问之，云：“孤贫无依，乞食至此。”建封曰：“吾纳尔女，而给养以（《广记》作“尔”）终身可乎？”妪欣然。建封即召入，命取新衣二袭以衣之，妪及女始脱故衣，皆化（《广记》无“化”字）为凝血（《广记》有“聚”字）于地。旬月建封被诛。（《广记》卷三百六十七）

    Translation:

    The military official Wang Jianfeng of the south was arrogant, unrestrained, and extravagant. He built a grand mansion in the south of the Huai River. One leisure day, while sitting by the window facing the street, he saw an old woman carrying a young girl who passed by. The girl was dressed in fine silk and had a beauty that was unparalleled in the world. Wang Jianfeng called out to ask her, and she replied, "I am poor and have no one to rely on, begging for food up to this point." Wang Jianfeng said, "I will take your daughter in and provide for her lifetime, is that acceptable?" The old woman was pleased. Wang Jianfeng immediately summoned her inside and ordered to bring two sets of new clothes to dress her. The old woman and the girl began to remove their old clothes, and all turned into clotted blood on the ground. After a few months, Wang Jianfeng was executed. (From The Record of the Strange Volume 367)

    广陵士人

    广陵有士人，尝（《广记》作“常”）张灯独寝。一夕中夜而坐（《广记》作“寐”），忽有双髻青衣女子，姿（《广记》作“资”）质甚丽，熟寐于其足。某知其妖物也，惧不敢近，复寝如故，向晓乃失，门户犹（《广记》有故“字”）扃鐍（《广记》作“闭”）。后（《广记》无“后”字）自是夜夜恒至。

    Translation:

    In Guangling, there was a scholar who often lit a lamp and slept alone. One night, in the middle of the night, he was sitting (or sleeping), and suddenly a young woman with twin braids and wearing green clothes appeared. She was very beautiful and was sleeping soundly at his feet. The scholar knew she was a supernatural being and was afraid to approach her. He returned to sleep as before, and in the morning, she had disappeared. The doors and windows were still locked. From then on, every night she would come.

    95

    有术士为书符，施其髻中，（《广记》有“其”字）夜半（《广记》作“佯”）寝以阅（《广记》作“伺”）之，果见自门而入，径诣髻中解取符，灯下视之微笑，讫复为（《广记》作“入”）置髻中，升床而寝，无（《广记》作“甚”）惧。后闻玉笥山有道士，符禁神妙，乃往访之。至暮（《广记》“至暮”二字作“既”字）登舟，遂长往（《广记》“长往”作“不至”），途次豫章，暑夜乘月行舟，时甚热，（《广记》有“乃”字）尽开船窗而寝，中夜忽复见寐于床后，某即潜起，急提（《广记》作“捉”）其手足，投之江中，ヨ然有声，因尔遂绝。（《广记》卷三百六十七，绝作“灭”）

    Explanation

    95

    A magician wrote a talisman and placed it in his hair bun. At midnight, he pretended to sleep to observe it. Indeed, the talisman entered through the door and went directly to his hair bun to remove itself. He looked at it by the lamp and smiled, then put it back in his hair bun. He climbed into bed and slept, without fear. Later, he heard that there was a Taoist priest on Yushisi Mountain whose talismanic spells were wondrous, so he went to visit him. At dusk, he boarded a boat and traveled far away. On the road to Yuzhang, on a hot summer night, he sailed by the moonlight, with the weather very hot, and opened all the ship windows to sleep. In the middle of the night, he suddenly saw the talisman sleeping behind the bed. He quickly got up, grabbed its hands and feet, and threw it into the river, where it made a splash and disappeared.

    96

    ○黄仁浚

    　　舒州司士参军黄仁浚，自言五十（《广记》作“壬子”）岁罢陇州阳主簿，至凤翔，有文殊寺，寺中有（《广记》无“有”字）土偶数十躯，忽自然摇动，如醉人状（《广记》无“状”字）。食顷不止，傍（《广记》无“傍”字）观者如堵，官司禁止之，至今未得（《广记》作“知”）其应验。（《广记》卷三百六十七，无“验”字）

    　　○孙德遵

    　　舒州都虞候孙德遵，其家寝室（《广记》作“堂”）中铁灯擎（《广记》作“檠”，下同）忽自摇动，如人撼之。至明日，有（《广记》有“一”字）婢偶至灯擎所，忽尔仆地，遂卒。（《广记》卷同上）

    Explanation

    96

    Huang Renjun

    Huang Renjun, a county magistrate in Shuzhou, reported that when he was fifty (or "Rensub" according to Guangji), he left his position as the county clerk of Yanyang in Longzhou and arrived in Fengxiang. There, he encountered Wenshu Temple, which housed dozens of clay figurines. These figurines suddenly began to shake on their own, as if they were drunk. The shaking continued for a while, and the crowd watching was so dense that it resembled a wall. The authorities tried to stop the phenomenon, but its cause remains unexplained to this day.

    Sun Dezun

    Sun Dezun, a military officer in Shuzhou, experienced a strange event at home. One of the metal lamp stands in his bedroom (or "hall" according to Guangji) began to shake on its own, as if someone were shaking it. The next day, one of his maidservants happened to be near the lamp stand and suddenly fell to the ground, dying as a result.

    97

    ○木成（毛本木作朱，成作盛）文

    　　梁开平二年，使其将李思安攻潞州，营于壶口（《广记》有“关”字），伐木为栅，破一大木，木中隶（《广记》作“朱”）书六字曰“天十四载石进”，思安表上之，其群臣皆贺，以为十四年必有远夷入（《广记》无“入”字）贡。（《广记》有“珍宝者其”四字）司天少监徐鸿独（《广记》无“独”字）谓其（《广记》无“其”字）所亲曰：“自古无一字为年号者，上天符命岂阙文乎？吾以为（《广记》无“为”字）丙申之年当有石氏王此地者。移四字中两竖书（《广记》作“画”），置天字左右即丙字也；移四之外围以十字贯之，即申字也。”后至丙申岁，晋高祖以石信（《广记》作“姓”）起并州，如鸿之言。（《广记》卷一百六十三）

    Explanation

    97

    Translation

    The Wooden Inscription (Wooden Edition reads "Red" instead of "Wood," and "Prosperous" instead of "Complete")

    In the second year of the Kai Ping era of the Later Liang dynasty, the general Li Sian was sent to attack Lushui Prefecture, setting up camp at Hukou Pass (as recorded in the Guangji). They cut down trees to build a fence, and while breaking apart a large piece of wood, they found six characters carved or written on it: "天十四载石进" (as recorded in the Guangji as "Red"). General Li Sian presented this discovery to the court, and all his ministers congratulated him, believing that in the fourteenth year there would surely be distant barbarians offering tribute (as recorded in the Guangji without the word "入"). The astrologer Xu Hong, the deputy director of the Office of Astronomy, spoke privately to someone close to him (as recorded in the Guangji without the word "独"): "Since ancient times, there has never been a single character used as a year name. Could the mandate of heaven leave it incomplete? I believe that in the year Bingshen (丙申), a person surnamed Shi will rule this place. By moving the two vertical strokes in the character '四' (four) and placing them on either side of the character '天' (heaven), you get the character '丙' (Bing); by moving the outer part of the character '四' and connecting it with the character '申' (Shen), you get the character '申'. After the year Bingshen, Emperor Shizong of Later Jin, surnamed Shi, rose to power in Bingzhou, just as Xu Hong had predicted (as recorded in volume 163 of the Guangji).

    98

    ○柳翁

    　　天祐中，饶州有柳翁，常乘小舟钓鄱阳江中，不知其居处妻子，亦不见其饮食。凡水族之类与山川之深远者，无不周知之；凡鄱（《广记》无“凡”字，“鄱”下有“阳”字）人渔钓者，咸谘访而后行。吕师造为刺史，修城掘濠，至城北则雨止，役则晴，或问柳翁，翁曰：“此下龙穴也，震动其土（《广记》作“上”）则龙不安而出穴，龙出则雨矣。掘之不已，必得其穴，则霖雨方将为患矣。

    Explanation

    98

    During the Tianyou period, there was a man named Liu in Raoyang who often fished in the Poyang River by boat. His residence, wife, and children were unknown, and it was also unclear what he ate. He had extensive knowledge of all aquatic creatures and the deep and distant mountains and rivers. All the fishermen and anglers in Poyang would consult and visit him before setting out. When Lü Shizao became the prefect and began repairing the city walls and digging moats, the rain would stop when they reached the north of the city, and it would be clear when they worked. Someone asked Mr. Liu about this, and he replied, "This is a dragon's lair. If the earth is disturbed, the dragon becomes restless and leaves its lair, and when the dragon comes out, it rains. If digging continues, it will surely find the lair, and a long rain will soon become a disaster."

    99

    ”既深数丈，果得大（《广记》作“方”）木，长数丈（《广记》“丈”作“十尺”），交加（《广记》无“加”字）构叠之，累积（毛本作“之”）数十重，其下雾气冲人，不可入；而其上（《广记》“而”下有“止”字，“其”下无“上”字）木皆腥涎萦之，刻削平正，非人力所致（《广记》作“及”）。自是果霖雨为患。吕氏诸子将网鱼于鄱阳江，召问柳翁，翁指南岸一处，“今日惟此处有鱼，然有一小龙在焉。”诸子不信，网之，果大获。舟中以瓦（《广记》作“巨”）盆贮之，中有一单鱼长一二尺，双目精明，有二长须，绕盆而行，群鱼皆翼从之。将至北岸，遂失所在。柳翁竟不知所终。（《广记》卷四百二十三）

    Explanation

    99

    After they had dug several meters deep, they indeed found a large piece of wood, about ten meters long, intricately interwoven and layered, with dozens of layers accumulated on top of each other. Below, the mist was oppressive and difficult to breathe; above, the wood was covered with a slimy, fishy substance, carved and polished smoothly, not the work of human hands. From then on, heavy rain caused a disaster. The sons of the Lu family planned to catch fish in the Poyang River and consulted the old man, who pointed to a place on the south bank, saying, "Today there are fish only at this place, but there is also a little dragon there." The young men did not believe him, but they caught a large amount of fish. On the boat, they stored the fish in a pottery basin, and among them was a 单 fish about one to two feet long, with bright, clear eyes and two long whiskers, swimming around the basin, with the other fish following like wings. As they approached the north bank, the lead fish suddenly disappeared. The old man, however, was never seen again.

    100

    ○李禅

    　　李禅，楚州刺史承嗣少子也。居广陵宣平里大第，昼日寝庭前，忽有白蝙蝠绕庭而飞，家僮辈竟以帚扑，皆不能中，久之飞出院门，扑之亦不中，及飞出至外门之外，遂不见。其年禅妻卒，而车出入之路，即白蝙蝠飞翔之所也。（《广记》卷四百七十九）

    Explanation

    100

    Li Chan, the younger son of Governor Chengsi of Chu Prefecture, lived in a grand residence in Xuanping Lane, Guangling. One day, while he was sleeping in front of his courtyard during the day, a white bat suddenly flew around the courtyard. The servants tried to beat it with brooms, but none of them could hit it. After a long time, the bat flew out of the gate, and even when they tried to beat it again, they still couldn't catch it. Eventually, the bat flew beyond the outer gate and disappeared. That same year, Li Chan's wife died, and the road used for the funeral procession was the very place where the white bat had flown. (From The Collection of Strange Stories, Volume 479)

    101

    ○蚓疮

    　　天祐中，浙西重建慈和寺，画地既毕，每为蚯蚓穿穴，执事者患之。有一僧教以石灰覆之，由是得定，而杀蚯蚓无数。顷之其僧病，举身皆痒，日须得长指爪者搔之，以至成疮。疮中辄得死蚯蚓一条，殆数百千条，肉尽至骨而死。（《广记》卷四百七十九）

    　　○蜂余

    　　庐陵有人应举行，遇夜诣一村舍求宿，有老翁出见客曰：“吾舍窄人多，容一榻可矣。”因止其家，屋室百余间，但窄小甚。久之，告饥，翁曰：“吾家贫，所食惟野菜耳。”即以设客，食之甚甘美，与常菜殊。及就寝惟闻讧讧之声，既晓而寤，身卧田中，旁有大蜂窠。客常患风，因而遂愈，盖食蜂之余尔。（《广记》卷四百七十九）

    Explanation

    101

    ○蚓疮

    During the Tianyou era, the Cihu Temple in Zhejiang West was being rebuilt. After the planning of the ground was completed, earthworms would dig holes, troubling the person in charge. There was a monk who taught to cover the area with lime, which stabilized the situation but resulted in the death of countless earthworms. Soon after, the monk fell ill, his entire body itching, requiring someone with long fingernails to scratch him every day, until sores formed. From the sores, dead earthworms were found one after another, almost hundreds of thousands, until the flesh was completely gone and down to the bones, and he died. (From the Guangji Volume 479)

    ○蜂余

    In Luling, there was a man who was traveling and one night went to a village house to ask for lodging. An old man came out to greet the guest, saying, "My house is small and crowded with people, but it can accommodate one mat." The guest stayed at his home, which had over a hundred rooms, but they were very narrow and small. After some time, the guest asked for food. The old man said, "My family is poor, and we only eat wild vegetables." He served the guest, and the food tasted very sweet and delicious, different from usual vegetables. When the guest went to sleep, he only heard a loud noise. In the morning when he woke up, he was lying in the field, with a large beehive nearby. The guest often suffered from wind, and thus he was cured, it was because he ate the remains of the bees. (From the Guangji Volume 479)

    102

    ○熊乃

    　　信州有板山，川谷深远，采板之所，因以名之。州人熊乃，尝与其徒入山伐木，其弟从西（《广记》作“而”）追之，日暮不及其兄。忽见甲士清道自东来，传呼甚厉，乃弟恐惧，伏于草间。俄而旗帜戈甲，络绎而至，道旁亦有行人，其犯清道者辄为所戮，至军中，有一人若大将者，西驰至（《广记》“至”字作“而去”二字）。度其尚（《广记》无“尚”字）远，乃敢起行，迨晓方见其兄，具道所见。众皆曰：“非巡逻之所，而西去溪滩险绝，往无所诣，安得有此人？”即共寻之，可十余里，隔溪犹见旌旗纷若布围畋猎之状。其徒有勇者遥叱之，忽无所见。就视之，人皆树叶，马皆大蚁，取而碎之，皆有血云。贮在庭中，以火烧之，少时荡尽，众口所哭。乃亦寻患足肿，粗于瓮，其酸不可忍，旬月而终。（《广记》卷四百七十九，无“贮在庭中”以下三十四字）

    Explanation

    102

    ○熊乃

    Xinzhou has a mountain called Ban Mountain, with deep and far-reaching valleys and rivers, named after the practice of cutting boards. A man from Xinzhou named Xiong Nai once went into the mountain with his followers to cut wood. His younger brother followed him from the west but did not catch up with him by evening. Suddenly, he saw armored soldiers clearing a path from the east, their calls very loud. Xiong Nai's younger brother was afraid and hid in the grass. Soon after, flags and weapons followed one after another, and there were also people on the road. Those who violated the cleared path were killed. Reaching the army, one man resembling a general galloped westward. Thinking he was still far away, Xiong Nai's younger brother dared to get up and walk. Until dawn, he finally saw his elder brother and told him everything he had seen. Everyone said, "It was not a place for patrols, and the western stream and rapids were extremely dangerous. There was nowhere to go, so how could there be such a person?" They immediately searched for it, about ten miles away, and across the stream, they still saw flags scattered as if in a hunting encampment. One of Xiong Nai's followers shouted at it from a distance, and suddenly, nothing was seen. Upon closer inspection, the people were leaves and the horses were large ants. They took them and crushed them, and they all had blood clouds. They stored them in the courtyard and burned them with fire, and in a short time, they were completely destroyed. They all cried out. Xiong Nai also soon developed a swollen foot, as thick as a jar. The pain was unbearable, and he died after a month or two.

    103

    ○刘威

    　　丁卯岁（案：丁卯当宋乾德五年），卢（《广记》作“庐”，下同）州刺史刘威移镇江西，既去任，而郡中大火，虞候申（《广记》作“吏”）巡，火甚急而往往有持火夜行（《广记》有“者”字），捕之不获，或射之殪，就视之，乃棺材板、腐木、败帚之类。郡人愈恐，数月除张宗为卢州刺史，火灾乃止。（《广记》卷三百七十三）

    Explanation

    103

    In the year Dingmao (967 AD during the reign of Emperor Taizu of Song), Liu Wei, the Governor of Luhu State (also referred to as "Luling" in the Guangji), was transferred to govern Jiangxi. After he left his post, a major fire broke out in the county. The military officer Shen (referred to as a "yuhou" in the Guangji) patrolled the area and found that the fires were burning intensely, and there were often people carrying fire at night. Despite efforts to catch them, they could not be captured. Sometimes, they were shot and killed, and upon examination, it was discovered that the objects they were carrying were pieces of coffin boards, rotten wood, and broken brooms. The people of the county became even more frightened. After several months, Zhang Zong was appointed as the Governor of Luhu State, and the fires finally ceased.

    104

    ○马希范

    　　楚王马希范修长沙城，开濠毕，忽有一物（“有一物”三字毛本脱），长十丈余，无头尾手足，状若土山，自北岸出，游泳水上，久之入南岸而没，出入俱无踪迹。或谓之土龙，无几何，而马氏遂（《广记》无“遂”字）亡。（《广记》卷三百七十三）

    　　●卷五

    　　○桂从义

    　　池阳建德县吏桂从义，家人入山伐木（《广记》作“薪”），常于（《广记》无“于”字）所行山路，（《广记》有“忽”字）有一石崩倒。就视之，有一室，内（《广记》作“室”）有金漆柏床六张，茭荐芒簟皆新，金银积叠。其人坐床上，良久，因揭簟下，见一角柄小刀，取内怀中而出。恐（《广记》“恐”字作“扶起”二字）崩石塞之，以物为记，归呼家人共取，及至则石壁如故，了无所睹。（《广记》卷三百七十四，睹作见）

    Explanation

    104

    ○马希范

    King Ma Xifan of Chu repaired the city of Changsha. After digging the moat, suddenly there was a creature over ten zhang long, without head, tail, hands, or feet, shaped like a mound of earth, emerging from the north bank, swimming on the water, and after a while, entering the south bank and disappearing. Both entering and leaving, it left no trace. Some called it a mud dragon. Not long after, the Ma clan perished.

    ●卷五

    ○桂从义

    Guizongyi, an official from Jiande County in Chiyang, had family members who went into the mountains to cut wood. Often on the road they were traveling, a stone collapsed. They went to look at it, and inside, there was a room with six beds painted with gold and lacquer, all the straw mats and rush mats were new, and accumulated silver and gold. The person sat on the bed for a long time, then lifted the rush mat, found a small knife with a curved handle, picked it up and put it in their chest. Afraid the collapsed stone would block it, they marked the spot with an object, returned and called the family to come together to retrieve it. When they arrived, the stone wall was as it had been, and nothing could be seen.

    105

    ○金精山木鹤

    　　处（《广记》作“虔”）州处（《广记》作“虔”）化县金精山，昔长沙王吴芮时女张丽英飞升之所，道馆在焉。岩高数百尺，有二木鹤，二女仙乘之，铁缫悬于岩下，非傍道所至（《广记》作“及”），不知其所从。其二鹤嘴随四时而转，初不差忒。顺义道中百胜军小将陈师粲者，能卷簟为牛，跃而出入，尝与乡里女子遇于岩下，求娶焉，女子曰：“君能射中此鹤，姻即成。”（《广记》“姻”作“目”，“成”作“可”，“即”在“粲”字下）师粲一发而中，臂即无力，归而病卧如梦。（《广记》有“非”字）梦见二女道士绕床而行，每过辄以手拂师粲之目，数四而去，竟致（《广记》无“致”字）失明而卒。所射之鹤，自尔不复转，其一犹转如故。辛酉岁（案：辛酉当宋建隆二年），其女子犹在。师粲之子孙，至今犹（《广记》作“亦”）为军士。（《广记》卷二百七十四）

    Explanation

    105

    Gold Essence Mountain Wood Crane

    In the Chuzhou (or Qianzhou) region, there is a place called Chuhua County, and within it lies the Gold Essence Mountain. This is the site where Lady Zhang Liying, a daughter of King Wu Rui of Changsha, ascended to immortality, and a Daoist temple stands there. The mountain rises several hundred feet high, and there are two wooden cranes, upon which two female immortals ride. A metal chain hangs from the cliff below, inaccessible to anyone who does not follow the path. The beaks of the two cranes rotate with the four seasons, without any deviation.

    During the Shunyi era, a minor officer named Chen Shican from the Baisheng Army, who could roll up mats into cows and leap in and out, once met a local woman at the foot of the mountain and asked to marry her. The woman said, "If you can shoot one of these cranes, your marriage will be accomplished." Chen Shican shot and hit one of the cranes, but his arm immediately became powerless. He returned home and fell ill, as if in a dream. In his dream, he saw two female Daoists walking around his bed, and each time they passed, they would gently touch his eyes several times before leaving. Eventually, he lost his sight and died. The crane he shot no longer turned, while the other continued to turn as usual.

    In the Xinyou year (961 CE), the woman was still alive. Chen Shican's descendants continued to serve as military officers.

    106

    ○卖饼王老（毛本作“广陵人卖饼”）

    　　有卖饼王老（《广记》“有卖饼”上有“广陵”二字），无妻，独与一女居。王老昼日自卖饼所归家，见其女与他少年共寝于北户下，王老怒持刀逐之，少年跃走得免，王老怒甚，遂杀其女。而少年行至中路，忽流血满身，吏呵问之，不知所对，拘之以还王老之居。乡伍方按验其事，王老见而识之，遂抵（《广记》无“抵”字）其罪。（《广记》卷三百七十四）

    Explanation

    106

    A Pancake Seller Named Old Wang (Mao edition: "A Pancake Seller from Guangling")

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, there was a pancake seller named Old Wang (as recorded in The Strange Tales, with "pancake seller" preceded by "Guangling"). He had no wife and lived alone with his daughter. One day, after returning home from selling pancakes, Old Wang saw his daughter sleeping with another young man under the northern window. Enraged, he chased the young man with a knife, but the youth leaped away and escaped. Old Wang's anger intensified, and in a fit of rage, he killed his daughter. The young man, walking along the road, suddenly found himself covered in blood. When questioned by an official, he could not respond. He was detained and brought back to Old Wang's house. The local officials were investigating the matter when Old Wang saw the youth and recognized him, holding him accountable for his actions. (From The Strange Tales, Volume 374)

    107

    ○桃林禾稼（《广记》无“稼”字）

    　　闽王（《广记》有“审知”二字）初为泉州刺史，州北数十里，地名桃林。光启初，一夕村中地震，有声如鸣数百面鼓。及明视之，禾稼方茂，了无一茎。咸（《广记》作“试”）掘地求之，则皆倒悬在土下。其年审知克晋安，尽有瓯闽之地（《广记》有《传国》二字）六十年。至其子（《广记》无“其”字，“子”作“于”）延义（《广记》作羲，下同）立，桃林地中复有鼓声，禾已收获，余粳在田（《广记》“鼓声”下作“时禾已收，惟余梗在田”）。及明视之亦无一茎，掘地求之则亦倒悬土下。其年延义为左右所杀，王氏遂灭。（《广记》卷三百七十四）

    Explanation

    107

    Peach Forest Crops

    The First Instance

    Wang Shenzhi was initially the governor of Quanzhou. In the early years of the Guangqi era, one night, there was an earthquake in the village, accompanied by a sound like hundreds of drums. By morning, it was discovered that the crops were flourishing, but there was not a single stem above ground. The villagers dug into the soil to find the crops, and they were all found upside down in the soil. That year, Wang Shenzhi conquered Jian'an and completely controlled the regions of Ou and Min.

    The Second Instance

    When his son, Wang Yanyi, ascended the throne, the Peach Forest area again heard drum-like sounds. The crops had already been harvested, leaving only the stalks in the fields. By morning, it was discovered that there was not a single stem above ground. The villagers dug into the soil to find the crops, and they were again found upside down in the soil. That year, Wang Yanyi was killed by his attendants, and the Wang family thus perished.

    Source: Yuejue Shu (Records of the Yue Kingdom), Volume 374

    108

    ○王延政

    　　王延政为建州节度。延平村人夜梦人告之曰：“与汝富，旦入山求之。”明日入山，终于所得。其（《广记》作“迩”）夕复梦如前，村人曰：“旦（《广记》作“日”）已入山，无所得也。”其人曰：“但求之，何故不得？”于是，明日复入，向暮息大树下，见方丈之地独明净，试掘之，得赤土如丹，既无他物，则负之归，以饰墙壁，焕然可爱。人闻者竞以善价从此人求市。延政闻之，取以饰其宫室，署其人以牙门之职。数年建州亦败。（《广记》卷三百七十四）

    Explanation

    108

    Wang Yanzheng was appointed as the military governor of Jianzhou. A villager from Yanping Village had a dream in which someone told him, "I will make you rich; go into the mountains in the morning to find it." The next morning, he went into the mountains and eventually found what he was looking for. That same night, he had another dream similar to the previous one. The villager said, "I went into the mountains in the morning but found nothing." The person in the dream replied, "Just keep looking for it; why haven't you found it?" The next day, he went into the mountains again and rested under a large tree in the evening. He saw a square patch of ground that was uniquely bright and clean. He tried digging it up and found red soil like cinnabar. Since there was nothing else, he carried it back and used it to decorate the walls, making them look bright and beautiful. People who heard about it competed to buy it from him at a good price. Wang Yanzheng heard about it and took some to decorate his palace. He appointed the man to a position as a gatekeeper. After several years, Jianzhou also fell.

    109

    ○洪州樵人

    　　洪州樵人，入西山岩石之下，藤萝甚密，中有一女冠，姿色绝世，闭目端坐，衣帔皆如新。近（《广记》作“众”）观之，不能测。或为整其冠髻，即应手腐坏，众惧散去，复寻之，不能得见。（《广记》卷三百七十四，按《广记》明钞本不注出处，无“见”字，引作《稽神录》）

    　　○法曹吏

    　　庐州有法曹吏，尝劾一僧，曲致其死，具狱上州。尔日（毛本“尔日”作案入），其妻女在家，方纫缝于西窗下，忽有二青衣卒（毛本作“者”），手执文书自厨中出，厉声谓其妻曰：“语尔夫，何故（《广记》“何故”作“无枉”）杀僧？”遂出门去。妻女皆惊怪，流汗久之，乃走出视其门扃，闭固如旧（“固如旧”《广记》作“如故”）。吏归，具言之。吏甚恐，明日将窃取其案，已不及矣。竟杀其僧。死之日即遇诸涂，百计穰谢，月余（《广记》“月余”作“旬月”）竟死。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Explanation

    109

    ○洪州樵人

    A woodcutter from Hongzhou entered the rocks beneath the Western Hills, where the vines and creepers were very dense. Inside, there was a female Taoist priestess of extraordinary beauty, sitting with closed eyes and dressed in robes as fresh as if just made. Upon closer observation, her nature was incomprehensible. If someone tried to fix her hair, it would immediately decay. Frightened, the onlookers scattered, and when they returned to look for her, they could not find her again.

    ○法曹吏

    In Luzhou, there was a legal official who once accused a monk and caused his death through indirect means, presenting the case to the prefecture. On that day, the official's wife and daughter were at home, sewing at the west window. Suddenly, two officials dressed in green robes, holding documents, emerged from the kitchen and sternly told the wife, "Tell your husband why he killed the monk." They then left. The wife and daughter were both startled and remained sweating for a long time. They went out to check the door, which was still closed as usual. When the official returned home, he told them about it. The official was very frightened and the next day planned to secretly take the case file, but it was too late. He finally killed the monk. On the day of the monk's death, he met him on the road and tried every method to appease him, but a month later, he finally died.

    110

    ○刘存

    　　刘存为舒州刺史，辟儒生霍某为团练判官，甚见信任，后为左右所谮，因构其罪下狱，白使府，请杀之。吴帅知其冤，使执送扬都，存遂缢之于狱。即而，存迁鄂州节度使，霍友人在舒州，梦霍素服自司命祠中出，抚掌大笑曰：“吾罪（《广记》作已）得雪矣。”俄而，存帅师征湖南。霍表兄马邺为黄州刺史，有夜扣齐安城门者，曰：“舒州霍判官将往，军前马病，与（《广记》作“白”）使君借马。”守陴者以告，邺叹曰：“刘公枉杀霍生，今此人往矣，宁无祸乎？”因画马数匹，焚之以祭（《广记》“以祭”作“水际”）。数日，存败绩死之。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Explanation

    110

    Liu Cun, the governor of Shuzhou, recruited a scholar-official named Ho to serve as a local administrative officer, and he was highly trusted by Liu Cun. However, Ho was later betrayed by those around him, and a crime was fabricated against him, leading to his imprisonment. Liu Cun reported this to the provincial government and requested that Ho be executed. The commander of Wu, recognizing Ho's innocence, ordered him to be sent to Yangzhou, where Liu Cun ultimately had him strangled in prison. Shortly after, Liu Cun was transferred to the position of military governor of Ezhou. Meanwhile, Ho's cousin, who was living in Shuzhou, had a dream in which Ho emerged from the shrine dedicated to the god of fate in plain clothes, laughing and saying, "My crime has been cleared!" Soon after, Liu Cun led a campaign against Hunan. Ho's cousin, Ma Ye, was the governor of Huangzhou. One night, a mysterious figure knocked on the city gate of Qian'an and said, "The local administrative officer of Shuzhou is heading to the front lines, and his horse is sick. Could you, sir, lend him a horse?" The guard reported this to Ma Ye, who sighed and said, "Liu Cun wrongfully killed Ho. Now that this person is going, can there be no consequences?" Ma Ye then drew several horses and burned them as an offering. A few days later, Liu Cun suffered a defeat and died.

    111

    ○袁州录事

    　　袁州录事参军王某，尝以（《广记》作“劾”）一盗，狱具而遇赦，王以盗罪重不可恕，乃先杀之，而（《广记》有“后”字）宣赦。罢归，至新喻邑，邑（《广记》无“邑”字）客冯氏具卮（《广记》无“卮”字）酒，请王明日当往，晚止僧院，乃见盗者，曰：“我罪诚合死，然已赦矣，君何敢逆王命而杀我？我今得请于所司矣。君明日往冯家耶？不往亦可。”言讫乃没。院僧但见其与人言而不见其他。（《广记》“其他”作“也字”）明日方饮，暴卒。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Explanation

    111

    Yuan Prefecture Registrar and Judicial Officer Mr. Wang

    Once, Mr. Wang, the Registrar and Judicial Officer of Yuan Prefecture, accused (or impeached) a thief. When the case was complete, he encountered a general amnesty. Despite the amnesty, Mr. Wang killed the thief first, and then the amnesty was announced. He was dismissed and returned home. When he arrived at Xin Yu County, Mr. Feng, a guest in the county, prepared wine and invited Mr. Wang to visit the next day. In the evening, he stayed at a temple and then saw the thief. The thief said, "My crime truly deserves death, but I have already been pardoned. How dare you defy the imperial decree and kill me? I have now appealed to the authorities. Are you going to Mr. Feng's house tomorrow? It's okay if you don't." After speaking, he disappeared. The temple monk only saw him talking to someone but didn't see anything else. The next day, while drinking, Mr. Wang suddenly died.

    112

    ○刘璠

    　　军将刘璠，性强直勇敢，坐法徙海陵，郡守褚仁规嫌之，诬其谋叛，诏杀于海陵（《广记》脱“陵”字）市。璠将死，谓监刑者曰：“与（《广记》作“为”）我白诸妻（《广记》无“妻”字）儿，多置纸笔于棺中，予将（《广记》作“必”）讼之。”后数年，仁规入朝，泊舟济滩江口，夜半闻岸上连呼“褚仁规，尔知当死否？”舟人（《广记》有“尽”字）惊起，视岸上无人，仁规谓左右曰：“尔识此声否？即（《广记》无“即”字）刘璠也。”命以酒食祭（《广记》作“立命酒食祭而谢之”）之。仁规至都，以残虐下狱。狱吏夜梦一人，长大黥面，后（《广记》无“后”字）从二十余人，至狱执仁规而去。既寤，为仁规说其人（三字《广记》作“所亲说之”），乃（《广记》“乃”字作“其人”二字）抚膺叹曰：“吾必死，此人即刘璠也。”其日中使至，遂缢于狱中矣。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Explanation

    112

    Liu Fan

    Liu Fan, a military commander, was strong, upright, and brave. Due to his crimes, he was sentenced to exile to Hailling. The governor of Hailling, Cù Rénɡuī, disliked him and falsely accused him of plotting rebellion. The emperor ordered him to be executed in the market of Hailling. As Liu Fan was about to die, he told the executioner, "Tell my wife and children for me. Put many papers and pens in my coffin. I will appeal for justice."

    Several years later, Cù Rénɡuī entered the capital and docked his boat at the mouth of Jitān River. In the middle of the night, he heard someone calling from the shore, "Cù Rénɡuī, do you know you will die?" The boatmen were all startled and woke up. They looked around the shore but saw no one. Cù Rénɡuī said to his attendants, "Do you recognize this voice? It's Liu Fan." He ordered a feast to be prepared and offered it to Liu Fan. When Cù Rénɡuī arrived in the capital, he was imprisoned for his cruelty. One night, the jailer dreamed of a tall man with a tattooed face, followed by more than twenty people, who came to the prison and took Cù Rénɡuī away. Upon waking, the jailer told Cù Rénɡuī about the dream. Cù Rénɡuī, upon hearing this, said, "I am doomed. That man was Liu Fan." That day, an imperial messenger came and hanged him in the prison.

    113

    ○吴景

    　　浙西军校吴景者，辛酉岁（《广记》作丁酉。案辛酉当宋建隆二年，丁酉当南唐升元元年），设斋于石头城僧院。其夕，既陈设，忽闻妇女哭声甚哀，初远渐近，俄在斋筵中矣。景乃告院僧曰：“景顷岁从军克（《广记》作“克”）豫章，获一妇人，殊有姿色，未几其夫求赎，将军令严肃，不可相容。景即杀之，后甚以为恨，今之设斋，正为是也。”即与僧俱往，乃见妇人在焉。僧为之祈告，妇人曰：“我从吴景索命，不知其他。”遽前逐之，景急走上佛殿，大呼曰：“我（《广记》无“我”字）还尔命。”于是颠仆而卒。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    113

    ○Wu Jing

    In the year of Xin You (961 AD, the second year of the Jianlong era of the Song Dynasty), Wu Jing, a military officer stationed in Zhe Xi, set up a vegetarian meal at a Buddhist temple in Shitou City. That evening, after everything was arranged, he suddenly heard a woman's cry of great sorrow, which initially came from afar and gradually grew closer, until she appeared in the dining hall. Wu Jing then told the temple monk, "A few years ago, while serving in the army, I conquered Yuzhang and captured a woman of extraordinary beauty. Not long after, her husband came to redeem her, but the general's orders were strict, and she could not be spared. I had her killed, and later I deeply regretted it. This vegetarian meal is set up specifically for this purpose." He then went with the monk to the dining hall, where they saw the woman. The monk prayed for her, and the woman said, "I am seeking revenge from Wu Jing, and I know nothing else." She quickly approached and chased him, and Wu Jing hurriedly ran up to the Buddha hall, shouting, "I will return your life to you." He then fell and died. (From Guangji, Volume 124)

    ○周宝

    　　周宝为浙西节度使，治城隍，至鹤林门，得古冢棺椟，将腐，发之，有一女子，面如生，铅粉衣服皆不败。掌墓（《广记》作“役”）者以告，宝亲视之，或曰：“此当是尝饵灵药，待时而发，发则解化（《广记》作“化解”）之期矣。”宝即命改葬之。其而（《广记》“其而”作“具车”）声乐以送，宝与僚属登城望之。行数里，有紫云覆而车之上，众咸见一女子出自车中，坐于紫云之，冉冉（四字《广记》作“冉冉而上”）久之乃没。开棺则空矣。（《广记》卷七十）

    　　○陈师

    Explanation

    114

    ○Zhou Ba

    Zhou Ba, the military governor of Zhejiang West, was repairing the city walls and moat. He reached the鹤林门 and found an ancient tomb with a coffin. When he opened it, there was a woman whose face looked as if she were still alive, and her cosmetics and clothes were not decayed. The person in charge of the tomb reported this to Zhou Ba, who personally inspected it. Someone said, "This is likely because she had taken a miraculous medicine, was waiting for the right time to emerge, and would then transform." Zhou Ba immediately ordered her to be reburied. The funeral procession was accompanied by music, and Zhou Ba and his officials watched from the city walls. After traveling several miles, a purple cloud covered the funeral carriage. Everyone saw a woman emerge from the carriage, sit on the purple cloud, and ascend slowly. After a while, she disappeared. When the coffin was opened, it was empty.

    ○Chen Shi

    Notes on Uncertainty

    • 鹤林门 - The exact location and significance of "鹤林门" are not explicitly clear, but it is treated as a specific gate in the city.
    • 灵药 - The nature of the "miraculous medicine" is not specified, but it is understood to be a transformative substance.
    • 化解 - The process of "transformation" is not fully explained, but it is understood to be a supernatural event.
    • 紫云 - The appearance of the "purple cloud" is a common motif in Chinese mythology, but its exact significance in this context is not elaborated upon.
    115

    豫章逆旅梅氏，颇济惠，行旅僧道投止，皆不求直。恒有一道士，衣服蓝缕，来止其家，梅厚待之。一日谓梅曰：“吾明日当设斋，从君求新瓷碗二十事及七箸，君亦宜来会，可于天宝洞前访陈师也。”梅许之，道士持碗渡江而去，梅翌日诣洞前，问其村人莫知其处，久之将回，偶得一小径，甚明静（《广记》作“净”），试寻之，果得一院，有青衣（《广记》无“衣”字）童应门，问之，乃陈之居也。既（《广记》无“既”字）入，见道士衣冠华洁（《广记》作“楚”），延与之坐，命具食。顷之，食至，乃熟蒸一婴儿，梅惧不食。良久，又进食，乃蒸一犬子，梅亦不食。道士叹息，命取昨所得碗赠客，视之乃金碗也。谓梅曰：“子善人也，虽（《广记》无“虽”字）然不得仙，千岁人参、枸杞皆不肯食，乃分也。”谢而遣之曰：“（《广记》无“曰”字）此而后不可复继见矣。”（《广记》卷五十一，“此作比”，无“而后”二字及“可”字）

    Explanation

    115

    In the inn of the Mei family in Yuzhang, they were very generous, and travelers, monks, and Taoists who sought lodging did not ask for payment. There was always a Taoist priest who came to stay at their inn, and the Mei family treated him generously. One day, the priest said to the innkeeper, "Tomorrow I will set up a vegetarian meal, and I ask you for twenty new porcelain bowls and seven chopsticks. You should also come to the gathering, and you can find Master Chen at the front of the Tianbao Cave." The innkeeper agreed, and the Taoist priest took the bowls across the river and left. The next day, the innkeeper went to the front of the cave, asked the villagers, but no one knew the location. After some time, he was about to return, when by chance he found a small path that was very clear and quiet. He followed it and indeed found a courtyard with a servant dressed in green answering the door. It was Master Chen's residence. After entering, he saw the Taoist priest with clean and elegant attire, who invited him to sit and ordered food to be prepared. Shortly after, the food arrived, and it was a steamed baby. The innkeeper was afraid and did not eat. After a long time, another dish was served, and it was a steamed puppy. The innkeeper also did not eat. The Taoist priest sighed and ordered the bowls taken from yesterday to be given as a gift to the guest. Upon looking at them, they turned out to be golden bowls. The priest said to the innkeeper, "You are a good person, although you cannot become immortal, you do not eat thousand-year-old ginseng and wolfberry, which is your destiny." The priest thanked and sent him away, saying, "After this, we cannot meet again."

    116

    ○陈金

    　　陈金者，少为军士，隶江西节度使，刘信围处（《广记》作“虔”）州，金私与其徒五人发一大冢，开棺见（《广记》有“一”字）白髯老人，面如生，通身白罗衣，衣皆如新。开棺时（《广记》无“时”字）即有白气冲天，墓中有非常香馥（《广记》作“气”），金独视棺盖上有物如粉，微作硫黄气。金素闻棺中硫黄为药成仙（二字《广记》无），即以衣襟掬取怀归。墓中无他珍宝，即共掩（《广记》有“塞”字）之而出（《广记》作“去”）。

    Explanation

    116

    Tin Jin, a young soldier, served under the Military Governor of Jiangxi, Liu Xin, who was besieging Quzhou (also known as Qian). One day, Jin and his five companions secretly opened a large tomb. Inside, they found an old man with a white beard, whose face looked as if he were still alive. He was dressed in brand new white silk clothing. When the coffin was opened, there was immediately a white vapor rising to the sky, and the tomb had an unusual fragrance. Jin alone noticed something like powder on the coffin lid, which had a faint smell of sulfur. Jin had always heard that sulfur in the coffin could turn into an elixir of immortality. He immediately scooped it up with his sleeve and took it home. There were no other precious treasures in the tomb, so they quickly covered it up and left.

    117

    既至营中，营中人皆惊云：“今日那得（《广记》有“有”字）香气？”金知硫黄之异，旦辄汲水浸（《广记》作“服”）食至尽。城平（《广记》作“中”）入舍僧寺，偶与寺僧言之，僧曰：“此城中富人之远祖也。子孙相传，其祖好道，有异人教（《广记》作“数”）饵硫黄，云，数尽当死，死后三百年，墓开，当（《广记》作“当开”）即解化之期也，今正三百年矣。”即相与复视之，棺中空，惟衣裳（《广记》无“裳”字）尚存，如蝉蜕之状。金自是无病，今为清海军小将，年七十余矣，形体枯瘦，轻健如故。（《广记》卷五十一）

    Explanation

    117

    When he arrived at the camp, the people there were all surprised and said, "How can there be such a fragrance today?" Gold, aware of the unusual nature of sulfur, began to soak and consume it daily until he had eaten it all. When the city was quiet, he entered a temple and chanced to speak with a monk there. The monk said, "This was the distant ancestor of a wealthy person from this city. Passed down through generations, his ancestor loved the Dao and was taught by an extraordinary person to consume sulfur. It was said that when the number of years was exhausted, he would die, and after three hundred years, his tomb would open, and that would be the time of his transformation. Now, exactly three hundred years have passed." They then examined the coffin again, and it was empty, with only his clothes still remaining, in the appearance of a cicada's shell. From then on, Gold remained free of illness. He is now a minor general in the Qinghai navy, over seventy years old, with an emaciated body but still light and agile as before.

    118

    ○沈彬

    　　吴兴沈彬，少而好道，及致仕归高安，恒以焚修服饵为事。尝游都下洞观，忽闻空中乐声，仰视云表（《广记》作“际”）见仙女数十，冉冉而下，往（《广记》作“迳”）之观中，遍至像前焚香，良久乃去。彬匿室中不敢出，既去，入殿视之，几案土皆有遗香，彬悉取置炉中，已而，自悔曰：“吾平生好道，今见神仙而能礼谒，得仙香而不能食之，是其无分欤？”初彬恒诫其子云：“吾所居室（《广记》作“堂”，毛本同）中，正是吉地，死即葬之。”及卒，如其言，掘地得自然砖圹，制造甚精，砖上皆作吴兴字彬，年八十余卒。其（《广记》无“其”字）后豫章有渔人投生米于潭中捕鱼，不觉行远，忽入一石门，焕然明朗，行数百步见一白髯翁，谛视之，颇类（《广记》有“于”字）彬，谓矣。故老有知者云：“此即西山（《广记》作“仙”）天宝洞之南门也。”（《广记》卷五十四）

    Explanation

    118

    Final Translation

    Shen Bin

    Shen Bin from Wu County loved the Dao from a young age. After retiring to Gao'an, he always engaged in burning incense, practicing meditation, and taking medicinal elixirs. Once, while visiting a cave temple in the capital, he suddenly heard heavenly music. Looking up, he saw dozens of fairy maidens descending gracefully from the clouds into the cave temple. They circled the statues, burning incense before them, and stayed for a long time before leaving. Shen Bin hid in his room and did not dare to come out. After they left, he entered the hall and found that the stone seats and tables were all scented with the lingering fragrance of the incense. He collected the scent and placed it in his incense burner. Later, he regretted, saying, "I have always loved the Dao, but now that I see the immortals, I can only bow to them and cannot partake of their divine fragrance. Is this because I lack the merit?"

    Initially, Shen Bin often warned his son, "The place where I live (the Shen Family Hall according to the Guangji and Mao's version) is a place of good fortune. When I die, bury me here." After his death, as he had said, they dug the ground and found a naturally formed brick-lined tomb, which was very finely crafted. The bricks were inscribed with the characters "Wu County" and "Shen." He died at the age of over eighty.

    After this, a fisherman from Yuzhang threw rice into a pond to catch fish and, without realizing it, walked far. Suddenly, he entered a stone gate that was bright and clear. After walking several hundred steps, he saw an old man with a long white beard. Upon closer inspection, the old man resembled Shen Bin. The old man said to him. Some elderly people who knew about it said, "This is the southern gate of the Tianbao Cave in the West Mountain." (From Guangji, Volume 54)

    119

    ○梅真君

    　　汝阴人崔景唐，家甚富。尝有道士，自言姓梅，来访崔，崔客之。数月，景唐市得玉案（《广记》作“鞍”），将之寿春，以献节度使高审思，谓梅曰：“先生但居此，吾将诣寿春，旬月而还，使儿（毛本作“尔”）侄辈奉事，无所忧也。”梅曰：“吾乃寿春人也，将（《广记》有“此”字）访一亲知，已（《广记》作“比”）将还矣，君其先往也。久居于此，思有以奉报，君家有水银乎？”曰：“有。”即以十两奉之，梅乃置鼎中，以水（《广记》有“银”字）炼之，少久即成白银矣。因以与景唐曰：“以此为路粮，君至寿春，可于城东访吾家也。”即与景唐分路而去。景唐至寿春，即诣城东访梅氏，数日不得，村人皆曰：“此中无梅家，亦无为道士者。惟淮南岳庙中有梅真君像，得非此耶？”如其言访之，果梅真君矣。自后竟不复遇。（《广记》卷四十五）

    119
    No. 1

Mr. Cui Jingtang from Ruyin was very wealthy. Once, a Daoist, claiming to be surnamed Mei, visited Cui, and Cui treated him as a guest. After several months, Cui bought a jade table (or a jade saddle according to the *Guangji* version) and was about to travel to Shouchun to present it as a gift to the military governor Gao Shenshi. He told Mei, "Sir, just stay here. I will go to Shouchun, and in a month or two, I will return. Have my sons and nephews take care of things, and you have nothing to worry about." Mei replied, "I am actually from Shouchun. I am already on my way back to visit a close friend. You should go first. Since I have been staying here for a long time, I want to find a way to repay you. Do you have mercury at home?" Cui said, "Yes." He immediately gave Mei ten taels of mercury. Mei placed it in a cauldron and refined it with water, and after a short while, it turned into silver. He then said to Cui, "Use this as your travel provisions. When you arrive in Shouchun, you can visit my family in the east of the city." With that, they parted ways. Cui arrived in Shouchun and went to the east of the city to look for Mei's family. After several days, he could not find them. The villagers all said, "There is no family named Mei here, nor any Daoists. There is only an image of Lord Mei in the Yue Temple in Huainan. Could it be this?" Following their advice, Cui visited the Yue Temple, and indeed, it was the image of Lord Mei. After that, they never met again. (Volume 45 of *Guangji*)
    120

    ○康氏

    　　伪吴杨行密，初定扬州，远方（《广记》作“坊”）居人稀少，烟火不接。有康氏者，以佣贷为业。僦一室于太平坊空宅中。康晨出未返，其夕（《广记》作“妻”）生一子，方席藁，忽有一异人，赤面朱衣冠，据门而坐。妻惊怖，久（《广记》作“叱”）之，乃走如舍西，訇（《广记》作“踣”）然有声。康适归，欲至家而（《广记》无“而”字）路左忽有钱五千，羊牛控（《广记》作“边”）樽酒在焉。伺之久，无行人，因持之归。妻亦告其所见，即往舍西寻之，乃一金人仆于草间，亦曳之归。因烹羊饮酒，得以周给。自是出入（《广记》作“必”）获富（《广记》作“利”），日以富赡，而金人留为家宝。所生子名曰平平，及（《广记》无“及”字）长，遂（《广记》有“为”字）富人。有李浔者，为江都令，行县至新宁乡，见大宅，即平平家也，其父老为李言如此。（《广记》卷四百一）

    Explanation

    120

    Translation

    Kang Family

    In the late Tang Dynasty, Yang Xingmi, who declared himself king of Wu, initially established his base in Yangzhou. The distant areas were sparsely populated, with little sign of human activity. There was a man named Kang who made a living by lending money. He rented a room in an empty house in Taiping Ward. One morning, Kang left the house and had not yet returned when his wife gave birth to a son. As she lay on a mat, a strange figure with a red face, wearing red robes and a hat, suddenly appeared and sat by the door. His wife was terrified, and after a long while, the figure ran to the west side of the house, making a loud noise. Kang just returned home and, on the way, found five thousand coins and a sheep, a cow, and a wine container on the left side of the road. After waiting for a long time with no one passing by, he took them home. His wife also told him what she had seen, and they went to the west side of the house to look for the figure. They found a golden person lying in the grass and dragged it back home. They cooked the sheep and drank the wine, and thus were able to sustain themselves. From then on, every time they went out, they gained wealth, and day by day, they became more prosperous. The golden figure remained as a family treasure. The son they had, named Pingping, grew up to become a wealthy person. There was a person named Li Xun, who was the magistrate of Jiangdu. On his rounds, he reached Xinning Village and saw a large house, which was Pingping's home. The elderly of the village told Li Xun about it.

    121

    ○豫章人

    　　天复中，豫章有人治舍掘地，得一木匮，发之，得金人十二躯（《广记》作“头”），各长数寸，皆古衣冠，首戴十二辰属，镌刻（《广记》“镌刻”作“数款”）精妙（《广记》作丽），殆非人功，其家宝祠之，因以致□福（《广记》“福”上不空格，毛本作“因携到金福”）。时兵革未定，遂为戍将劫（《广记》有“取”字）之，后不知所终。（《广记》卷四百一）

    　　○陈浚

    　　江南陈浚尚书，自言其诸父在乡里好为诗，里人谓之陈白舍人，比之乐天也，性疏简，喜宾客。尝有二道士，一黄衣，一白衣，诣其家求舍（《广记》作“宿”）。舍之厅事，夜分闻（三字《广记》作“夜间”二字）二客床坏，訇然有声，久之，若无人者。秉烛视之，见白衣人（《广记》无“人”字）卧于壁（《广记》有“下”字），乃银人也；黄衣人（《广记》无“人”字）不复见矣。自是丰（《广记》作“致”）富。（《广记》卷四百一）

    Explanation

    121

    Translation

    ○豫章人

    During the Tianfu era, a man from Yuzhang was building a house and digging the ground when he found a wooden chest. Upon opening it, he discovered twelve golden figures (or heads, according to Guangji), each several inches long, all dressed in ancient attire, with the twelve earthly branches on their heads. The figures were carved with exquisite precision (or beauty, according to Guangji), hardly the work of human hands. The family treasured and worshipped them, thereby bringing good fortune (or "carried to gold fortune," according to Mao's version). At a time when warfare was still unsettled, the figures were then seized by a military commander (or "taken," according to Guangji), and their fate was later unknown.

    ○陈浚

    Chen Jun, a high-ranking official from the Jiangnan region, himself said that his father or uncles were fond of writing poetry in the countryside. The villagers called him Chen Bai, the Gentleman of the Village, comparing him to Bai Juyi, and he had a simple and unpretentious nature, liking to entertain guests. Once, two Taoist priests came to his house seeking lodging (or "staying overnight," according to Guangji). They were given a room, and at midnight they heard the guests' beds collapse, making a loud sound. After a while, it was as if no one was there. Lighting a candle to look, they saw the white-robed priest lying against the wall (or "below the wall," according to Guangji), who turned out to be a silver figure; the yellow-robed priest was no longer seen. From then on, Chen Jun became wealthy (or "brought about wealth," according to Guangji).

    122

    ○建安村人

    　　建安有人村居者，常使一小奴出（《广记》有“入”字）城市，经过（《广记》无“过”字）舍南大冢，冢旁恒有一黄衣人（《广记》作“儿”）与之较力为戏，其主因归迟将责之（《广记》无“归”字及“将责”二字），奴以实告，往（《广记》无“往”字）觇之，信然。一日挟挝而往，伏于草间。小奴至，黄衣儿复出，即起击之，应手而仆（《广记》作“踣”），乃金儿也。因持以归，家遂殷（《广记》“遂殷”作“自是”）富。（《广记》卷四百一）

    Explanation

    122

    A Villager from Jian'an

    During the Jian'an period, there was a villager who often sent a small servant to (or from) the city. One day, the servant passed by (or through) the large tomb south of his house. There was always a person dressed in yellow (or a child) by the tomb who played wrestling games with him. The master returned late and was about to scold him (or him). The servant told the truth, went (or checked) to see, and indeed found it to be true. One day, he took a stick and went, hiding in the grass. When the small servant arrived, the yellow-clad child came out again, and he immediately hit him, causing him to fall (or collapse). It turned out to be a golden child. He then took it home, and his family became prosperous (or from then on).
