    ○蔡彦卿

    　　庐州军吏蔡彦卿为拓皋镇将，暑夜坐镇门外纳凉，忽见道南桑林中，有白衣妇人独舞，就视即灭。明夜，彦卿扶（《广记》作“挟”）杖先往，伏于草间，久之，妇人复出而（《广记》作“方”）舞，即击之坠（《广记》作“堕”）地，乃白金一饼（《广记》作“<缶并>”）。复掘地，获银数（《广记》无“数”字）千两，遂致富裕云（《广记》卷四百一，“致”作“为”，“裕”作“人”）。

    Explanation

    123

    Pianqing, a military officer of Luzhou, was stationed as the commander of the Tuo'ao Garrison. One hot night, he sat outside the gate to cool off and suddenly saw a white-clad woman dancing alone in the mulberry grove to the south of the road. When he approached, she vanished. The next night, Pianqing, holding (as noted in the Guangji, "carrying") a staff, went ahead and lay hidden in the grass. After a while, the woman reappeared and began to dance again. He struck her, and she fell to the ground, revealing a piece of white metal (silver). He dug further and found several thousand taels of silver. Thus, he became wealthy and prosperous. (As noted in the Guangji, volume 401, "became a person" instead of "became wealthy and prosperous.")

    124

    ○岑氏

    　　临川人岑氏，尝游山溪水中，见二白石，大如莲实，自相驰逐，捕而获之，归置巾箱中。其夕，梦二白衣美女，自言姊妹，来侍左右。既寤，益知二石之异也，恒结于衣带中。后至豫章，有波斯国（《广记》作“胡”）人，邀而问之“君有宝耶”？（《广记》作“乎”）曰：“然。”即出二石示之，胡人欲（《广记》作“求”）以三万为价（《广记》作“市”）得之（《广记》无“得之”二字）。岑虽宝藏（《广记》作“之”）而实（《广记》无“实”字）无用，得钱甚（《广记》无“甚”字）喜，因（《广记》作“即”）以与之，胡谢而去。岑氏因此而赡（以上十字广记作“以钱为生资遂致殷赡”九字），但恨不能问其名与所用云。（《广记》卷四百四）

    Explanation

    124

    Cen of Linchuan

    A man from Linchuan named Cen once went for a walk in a mountain stream, where he saw two white stones, as large as lotus seeds, chasing each other. He caught them and brought them home, placing them in his cloth box. That night, he dreamed of two beautiful women dressed in white, who introduced themselves as sisters and came to serve him. Upon waking, he realized even more how strange these two stones were, and he often tied them to his belt. Later, he traveled to Yuzhang, where a Persian (or "foreigner" as noted in the Yingya Shenglan) approached him and asked, "Do you have any treasures?" Cen replied, "Yes." He then showed the two stones to the Persian, who wanted to buy them for 30,000 units of currency (or "market" them, as noted in the Yingya Shenglan). Although Cen valued the stones highly but found them useless, he was very pleased to receive the money and gave the stones to the Persian, who thanked him and left. As a result, Cen became wealthy (or "with money as his livelihood, he became prosperous," as noted in the Yingya Shenglan), but he regretted not being able to ask their names and their uses.

    125

    ○建州（《广记》作“安”）村人

    　　建安有村人，乘小舟，往来建溪中，卖薪为业。尝泊舟登岸，将伐薪，忽见山上有数百钱流下，稍上寻之，累获数十；未（《广记》作“可”）及山半，有大树下一（《广记》“一”字作“有大”二字）瓮，高五六尺，钱满其中，而瓮小欹，故钱流出。于是推而正之，以石支之，纳衣襟得（《广记》“纳”作“以”，“得”作“贮”）五百而归。尽率其（《广记》无“其”字）家人复往（《广记》有将字）尽取，既至，得旧路，见大树，而亡其瓮。村人徘徊数日不能去，夜梦人告之曰：“此钱有主，向为瓮欹，以五百雇而（《广记》而作尔）正之，不可再得也（《广记》，“再得”作“妄想”，“不可”上有“余”字）。”（《广记》卷四百五，字曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    125

    A Tale of the Villagers from Jianzhou (or Anzhou, as noted in the Guangji)

    In the Jian'an district, there were villagers who traveled on small boats up and down the Jian River, making a living by selling firewood. One day, they moored their boat and went ashore to cut wood. Suddenly, they saw hundreds of coins flowing down from the mountains. They gradually climbed up to search for them, collecting dozens in succession. Before reaching the halfway point of the mountain (or could reach the halfway point, according to the Guangji), they saw a large earthenware jar beneath a big tree, about five or six feet tall, filled with coins. The jar was slightly tilted, causing the coins to spill out. They pushed it upright and propped it up with a stone. They stuffed the coins into their sleeves and collected five hundred before returning home. They led their entire family back to take all of the coins. After arriving, they found the old path, saw the large tree, but lost the jar. The villagers wandered for several days, unable to leave. One night, they dreamed of a person who told them, "These coins have an owner. Before, the jar was tilted, and with five hundred coins, you had it fixed. It cannot be obtained again (or it is a delusion, according to the Guangji)." (This story is recorded in volume 405 of the Guangji, also cited in Zeng Zao's Leishuo.)

    126

    ○徐仲宝

    　　徐仲宝者，长沙人，所居道南，有大枯树，合数大抱。有仆夫，洒扫其下，沙中获钱百余，以告仲宝。仲宝自往，亦获数百。自尔，每需钱即往扫其下，必有所得，如是积年，凡得数十万。仲宝后至扬都，选授舒城令。暇日与家人共坐，地中忽有白气甚劲烈，斜飞向外而去，中若有物。其妻以手攫之，得一玉蛱蝶，制作精妙，人莫能测。后为乐平令，家人复于厕厨（《广记》作“厨侧”）鼠穴中得钱甚多。仲宝即率人掘之，深数尺，有一白雀飞出，止于庭树。其下获钱至百万钱，尽，白雀乃去，不知所之。（《广记》卷四百五）

    Explanation

    126

    Muzhongbao, a man from Changsha, lived south of a road. There was a large, withered tree nearby that could embrace several people. One of his servants, while sweeping and cleaning under the tree, found over a hundred coins in the sand and told Muzhongbao about it. Muzhongbao went there himself and also found hundreds of coins. From then on, whenever he needed money, he would go and sweep under the tree, and he would always find something. Like this, over many years, he accumulated tens of thousands of coins. Later, Muzhongbao went to Yangzhou, where he was selected and appointed as the magistrate of Shucheng. On a leisure day, he sat with his family. Suddenly, a strong white vapor rose from the ground, flying diagonally outward and away, as if there was something inside. His wife grabbed it with her hand and found a jade butterfly, exquisitely crafted, which no one could measure or understand. Later, he became the magistrate of LePing, and his family found a lot of coins in a mouse hole in the kitchen or the side of the kitchen. Muzhongbao then had people dig there, and after digging several feet deep, a white sparrow flew out and landed on a tree in the courtyard. Underneath, they found a million coins. Once the coins were all taken, the white sparrow left, and no one knew where it went. (From Guangji 卷四百五)

    127

    ○邢氏

    　　建业有库子，姓邢，家贫，聚钱满二千辄病，或失去。其妻窃聚钱，埋于地中。一日（《广记》作“夕”）忽闻有声如虫，飞自地，出穿窗户而去，有触墙壁堕（《广记》作“坠”）地者。明旦（《广记》作“日”）视之，皆钱也（《广记》无“也”字）。其妻乃告邢，使埋（《广记》无“邢”字，“埋”作里）瘗之，再（《广记》作“发”）视则皆亡矣。（《广记》有“后”字）邢得一自然石龟，其状如真，置庭中石榴树下。或见之曰：“此宝物也。”因装（《广记》作“收”）置巾（《广记》作“筐”）箱中。自尔稍稍（《广记》少一“稍”字）充足，后颇富饶矣。（《广记》卷四百五，无“饶”字）

    Explanation

    127

    ○邢氏

    In Jianye, there was a storekeeper named Xing, who was poor. Whenever he collected two thousand coins, he would fall ill, or the money would disappear. His wife secretly collected the money and buried it in the ground. One day (or evening, according to The Extensive Records), he suddenly heard a sound like insects, flying out from the ground, passing through the windows and leaving. Some touched the wall and fell to the ground. The next morning (or day, according to The Extensive Records), he looked and saw that they were all coins. His wife then told him and had him bury them. When he looked again, they were all gone. Xing found a natural stone turtle, which looked very real, and placed it under a pomegranate tree in the courtyard. Some saw it and said, "This is a treasure." He then put it in his pouch or box. From then on, he gradually became well-off and eventually became quite wealthy.

    128

    ○林氏
    　　汀州有林氏，其先尝为郡守，罢任家居。一日，天忽雨钱，充积其家。林氏乃整衣冠，仰天而祝曰：“非常之事，必将为祸于此（《广记》“于此”作“愿天”）。速止，林氏之福也。”应声而（《广记》作“则”）止。所收已钜万，至今为富人云。（《广记》卷四百五）

    　　○曹真

    　　寿春人曹真，出行野外，忽见坡下有数千钱，自远而来，飞声如铃。真逐之，入一小穴，以手掬之，可得数十而已。又舒州桐城县双戍港，有回风卷钱，经市而过，市人随攫其钱，以衣襟贮之。风入石城（《广记》作“古墓”）荆棘中，人不能入而止。所得钱归家视之，与常钱无异，而皆言亡八九矣。（《广记》卷四百五）

    　　○破木有肉

    Explanation

    128

    The Lin Family

    In Tingzhou, there was a family surnamed Lin, whose ancestors once served as prefects. After their term ended, they returned home. One day, coins suddenly rained from the sky, accumulating in their household. The Lin family then dressed formally and looked up to the heavens, offering a prayer: "This is an extraordinary event, and it will surely bring disaster if not stopped. Stop quickly, for it is a blessing for the Lin family." Upon hearing this, the rain of coins ceased. The amount collected was enormous, and the Lin family remains wealthy to this day.

    Cao Zhen

    Cao Zhen, a man from Shouzhou, was traveling in the countryside when he suddenly saw thousands of coins at the bottom of a slope, appearing to come from a distance and making a sound like bells. Cao Zhen followed the coins and entered a small hole, where he scooped up the coins with his hands, managing to collect only a few dozen. In another instance, in the area of Shuzhou's Tongcheng County at Shuangshu Port, a whirlwind gathered coins and passed through the market. People in the market grabbed the coins and stored them in their sleeves. The whirlwind then entered a stone city (or ancient tomb) filled with thorns, and people could not enter, so it stopped. The coins collected were taken home and examined, and they looked the same as ordinary coins, though it was said that they were missing about one-tenth of their usual value.

    129

    建康（《广记》无“建康”二字）有木工（《广记》“木工”二字作“人”）破（《广记》有“大”字）木，木中有肉，（《广记》有“可”字）五斤许，其香（《广记》无“许其香”三字）如熟猪肉。此又不可以理穷究者矣。（《广记》卷四百七，无“此又”句）

    　　○登第皂荚

    　　泉州文宣王庙，庭宇严峻，学校之盛于藩府。庭中有皂荚树，每州人将登第，即（《广记》作“则”）生一荚，以为常矣。梁贞明中，忽然生二（《广记》作“一”）荚，一半荚，（《广记》作“人”）莫喻其意。乃其年州人陈逖进士及第，黄仁隶（《广记》作“颖”，下同）学究及第，仁隶耻之，复应进士举。至同光中，旧生半荚之后（《广记》作“所”）复生全荚，其年仁隶及第。后数年，庙为火焚，其年（《广记》有“闽”字）自称尊号，不复生荚，（《广记》作“贡士”）遂至今矣（《广记》“至”下有“于”字，无“矣”字）。（《广记》卷四百七）

    Explanation

    129

    Translation

    In Jiankang (as recorded in the Guangji without the characters "Jiankang"), there was a carpenter (as recorded in the Guangji as "person") who cut (as recorded in the Guangji as "cut a large") piece of wood. The wood contained meat (as recorded in the Guangji as "can be about five catties"), which smelled like cooked pork. This phenomenon cannot be fully explained by reason (as recorded in the Guangji without the phrase "this cannot be fully explained by reason").

    ○ The Soapberry Tree of Success

    In the Temple of Confucius in Quanzhou, the buildings were imposing, and the school was prominent in the region. In the courtyard, there was a soapberry tree. Whenever someone from the state passed the imperial examinations, a pod would grow, which was considered a common occurrence. During the reign of Emperor Zhuangzong of Later Liang, the tree suddenly produced two pods (as recorded in the Guangji as "one pod"), and half a pod (as recorded in the Guangji as "a person"), the meaning of which was not understood. That year, a man from the state named Chen Ti passed the imperial examinations as a Jinshi, and Huang Renli (as recorded in the Guangji as "Ying") passed as a Xuezhou. Huang Renli was ashamed of this and reapplied for the Jinshi examination. During the reign of Emperor Taizong of Later Tang, after the half pod had grown, a full pod grew again, and that year Huang Renli passed the imperial examinations. Several years later, the temple was burned down, and that year (as recorded in the Guangji with the character "Min"), it declared its own title, and no longer produced pods (as recorded in the Guangji as "offered scholars"), and so it continues to this day (as recorded in the Guangji with the character "to" but without the character "now"). (From the Guangji, Volume 407)

    130

    ○张怀武

    　　南平王钟传镇江西，遣道士沈太虚祷庐山九天使者庙。太虚醮罢，夜坐庙庑间，忽然若梦，见壁画一人前揖太虚曰：“身张怀武也。尝为军将，上帝以微有阴功及物，今配此庙，为灵官。”既寤，起视壁画，署曰五百灵官。太虚归，以语进士沈彬。彬后二十年游醴陵，县令陆生客之。方食，有军吏许生后至，语及张怀武。彬因问之，许曰：“怀武者，蔡之裨将某之长吏也。顷甲辰年，大饥，闻豫章独稔，即与一他将，各帅其属奔豫章。既即路，两军稍不相能，比至武（《广记》作“五”）昌，衅（《广记》作“一”）隙大作，克日将决战，禁之不可。

    Explanation

    130

    The Southern Prince Zhong was stationed in Jiangxi, and he sent the Taoist priest Shen Taixu to pray at the Nine Heavenly Generals Temple on Mount Lu. After the ritual was completed, Shen Taixu sat in the temple porch at night. Suddenly, as if in a dream, he saw a person in the wall painting bowing to him and saying, "I am Zhang Huawu. I once served as a military commander. The Supreme Deity, because I had some minor merits that benefited others, now I am stationed in this temple as a spirit official." After he woke up, he got up and looked at the wall painting, which was inscribed with "Five Hundred Spirit Officials." Shen Taixu returned and told the scholar Shen Bin about it. Twenty years later, Shen Bin traveled to Liling, where the county magistrate, Mr. Lu, treated him as a guest. While they were eating, a military official named Xu arrived later, and they talked about Zhang Huawu. Shen Bin then asked about him. Xu replied, "Zhang Huawu was a deputy general under someone in Cai. In the year Jia Chen, there was a great famine. He heard that Yuzhang (Jiangxi) had a bountiful harvest. He immediately went with another general, each leading his own troops, to Yuzhang. After they set out, the two armies began to have some friction. By the time they reached Wuchang, the conflicts had escalated. They planned to fight a decisive battle, but could not prevent it."

    131

    怀武乃携剑上戍楼云（《广记》“云”字作“去其”二字）梯，谓其徒曰：‘吾与汝今日之行，非有他图，直救性命耳，奈何不忍小而相攻战？夫战必强者伤而弱者亡，如是则何为去父母之国而死于道路耶？凡两军所以致争者，以有怀武故也，今为汝等死，两军为一，无徒召（《广记》“徒召”二字作“御名”二字并写）难矣。’遂自刎。于是，两军之士皆伏楼下恸哭，遂相与和亲。比及豫章，无（《广记》有“一”字）人逃亡者。许但怀其旧恩，亦不知灵官之事，枢密述记以申明之。”岂天意将感发死义之士，故以肸蚃告人乎？（《广记》卷三百十三）

    Explanation

    131

    Huai Wu took his sword and went up to the watchtower (《广记》“云”字作“去其”二字梯), telling his followers: "Our journey today is not for any other purpose, but simply to save our lives. Why are we not willing to spare a little and fight each other? In battle, the strong always get hurt while the weak die. If so, why leave our homeland and die on the road? The reason for the conflict between the two armies is because of Huai Wu. Now I will die for you, and the two armies will become one, eliminating needless troubles." He then cut his own throat. The soldiers of both armies wept bitterly at the foot of the tower and then made peace with each other. By the time they reached Yuzhang, no one had deserted. Xu only remembered his old favor and did not know about the affairs of Lingguan. The Chief Military Councillor recorded it to clarify the matter. Is it that heaven intended to inspire those who die for righteousness, therefore using the divine message to inform people? (《广记》卷三百十三)

    132

    ●卷六

    　　○李攻

    　　天祐初，舒州有仓官李攻（《广记》作“玫”，下同），自言少时因病遂见鬼，为人言祸福多中。淮南大将张颢，专废立之权，威震（《广记》作振）中外。攻时宿于鬻（《广记》作“灊”）山司命真君庙，翌日与道士崔绰（《广记》作“繟”下同）然数人将入城，去庙数里，忽止同行于道侧，自映大树以窥之，良久乃行。绰然曰：“复见鬼耶？”曰：“向见一人，桎梏甚严，吏卒数十人卫之，向庙而去。是必为真君考召也，虽意气尚在，已不自免矣。”或问为谁，久之乃肯言曰：“张颢也。”闻者皆惧，共秘之。不旬月（《广记》作“日”）而闻颢诛。李宗造开元寺成，大会文武僧道于寺中，既罢，攻复谓绰然曰；“向坐中有客为二吏固缉（《广记》作“揖”）之而去，是不久矣。”言其衣服容貌，则团练巡官陈绛也。不数月绛暴疾，卒。道士邵修默、崔之弟皆（《广记》作“子”）亲见之。（《广记》卷三百十三）

    Explanation

    132

    In the early years of the Tianyou era, there was a granary official named Li Gong in Shuzhou who claimed that due to an illness in his youth, he had seen ghosts and often predicted good or bad fortune with great accuracy. Zhang Hao, a prominent general of the Huainan region, held the power to depose and install rulers and instilled fear both inside and outside the empire. Li Gong once stayed at the Temple of the True Lord of Life and Death on Yushan Mountain. The next day, he and Daoist priest Cui Chuo, along with several others, were about to enter the city. When they were a few miles away from the temple, they suddenly stopped and hid beside the road, observing something through a large tree. After a long time, they continued their journey. Cui Chuo asked, "Did you see a ghost again?" Li Gong replied, "I saw a person with very tight shackles, accompanied by dozens of officials and soldiers, heading towards the temple. This must be for the True Lord's examination and summoning. Although he still has spirit, he cannot escape his fate." Someone asked who it was, and after a long time, Li Gong reluctantly said, "It was Zhang Hao." Those who heard this were all afraid and kept it secret. Within a month, news came that Zhang Hao had been executed. When Li Zongzao completed the construction of the Kaiyuan Temple and held a grand gathering of civil and military officials, monks, and Taoists, after the banquet, Li Gong told Cui Chuo, "Yesterday, a guest at the table was greeted by two officials and left. This means something significant is about to happen soon." Describing the guest's clothing and appearance, it turned out to be Chen Jiang, a local official. Within a few months, Chen Jiang fell ill suddenly and died. Daoist priest Shao Xiumo and Cui's brother both witnessed these events. (From the Guangji Volume 313)

    133

    ○赵瑜

    　　明经赵瑜，鲁人，累举不第，困厄甚矣（《广记》无“矣”字）因游太山，祈死于岳庙。将出门，忽有小吏自后至曰：“判官召。”随之而去。奄至一厅事，帘中有人云：“所重者生，君何为求（《广记》作“祈”）死？”对曰：“瑜应乡荐，累举不第，退无归耕之资，湮厄贫病，无复生意，故祈死耳。”良久，闻帘中检阅簿书，既而言曰：“君命至薄，名与（《广记》作“第”）禄仕皆无分。然不可置家，置家则贫矣。”瑜拜谢而出，至门外，空中飘大桐叶至瑜，（《广记》有“前视之”三字）乃书巴豆丸方于其上，（《广记》有“亦”字）与人间之方正同。瑜遂（《广记》有“自”字）称前长水令，卖药于夷门，市饵其药者，病无不愈，获利甚多。道士李德阳亲见其桐叶，已十余年，尚如新折者。（《广记》卷三百十三）

    Explanation

    133

    Suo Yu, a Scholar of the Classics

    Suo Yu, a scholar of the classics, was from the state of Lu. Despite repeated attempts, he failed to pass the imperial examinations, and his life became extremely difficult. During the reign of Emperor Ling, he decided to visit Mount Tai and pray for death at the temple of the mountain. Just as he was about to leave, a small official appeared behind him and said, "The magistrate summons you." He followed the official, who led him to a hall. Suddenly, he found himself in a grand hall with a curtain, and a voice from behind the curtain said, "Life is what we value most. Why do you seek death?" Suo Yu replied, "I should have been recommended for the local exams, but I failed repeatedly. Now, I have no means to return home and farm, and I am suffering from poverty and illness. There is no hope left, so I pray for death." After a long silence, the voice behind the curtain said, "Your fate is very weak. You will not achieve fame or an official position. However, you should not marry and start a family, as doing so will only make you poorer." Suo Yu bowed and thanked him before leaving. Outside the hall, a large leaf of the Chinese parasol tree floated down to him (as recorded in the Tang Huiyao, there is also the phrase "he looked at it in front of him"). On the leaf, the formula for making Croton tiglium pills was written, identical to the formula used in the human world. Suo Yu then claimed to be a former official of Changshui and began selling medicine in the eastern gate of the city. Those who took his medicine were cured of their illnesses, and he made a substantial profit. The Taoist priest Li Deyang personally witnessed the leaf, and it had been more than ten years since the event, yet it still looked as fresh as if it had just been picked (as recorded in the Tang Huiyao, volume 313).

    134

    ○袁州老父

    　　袁州村中有老父，性谨厚，为乡里所推，家亦甚富。一日，有紫衣少年，车仆甚盛，诣其家求食。老父即延入，设食甚丰。（《广记》作“至”）遍及从者。老父侍食于前，因思长吏朝使行县，当有顿地，此何人哉？意色甚疑。少年觉之，谓曰：“君疑我，我不能复为君隐，仰山神也。”父悚然再拜曰：“仰山日献（《广记》作“厌”）于祭祀，奈何求食乎？”神曰：“凡人之祀我，皆从我求福，我有力不能致者。若（《广记》作“或”）非其人不当受福者，我皆不敢享之。以君长者，故从君求食尔。”食讫辞让而去，遂不见。（《广记》卷三百十四曾慥《类说》亦引）

    134

    In the village of Yuanzhou, there lived an elderly man who was gentle and honest in nature, respected by the villagers, and whose family was also very wealthy. One day, a young man dressed in purple clothing, accompanied by a large entourage of servants, came to his house to beg for food. The elderly man immediately invited him in and prepared a very generous meal, providing food for all his attendants. As he served the meal in front of him, the elderly man began to suspect that this might be the arrival of a high-ranking official or envoy from the capital, and wondered why this young man was begging for food. His expression showed great suspicion. The young man noticed his unease and said, "You suspect me. I cannot hide it from you any longer—I am the mountain god of Mount Yang." The elderly man, startled, bowed twice and said, "Mount Yang's mountain god daily offers sacrifices to be used in rituals. Why are you begging for food?" The mountain god replied, "All people who worship me ask for blessings from me. Those who have no power to grant blessings, or those who are not worthy of receiving them, I dare not accept their offerings. Because you are a virtuous person, I came to you to beg for food." After finishing the meal, the mountain god thanked and left, and then he disappeared. (This story is also cited in Volume 314 of the Guangji and in Zeng Zhao's Leishuo.)

    135

    ○朱廷禹

    　　江南内臣朱廷禹，言其所亲，泛海遇风，舟将覆者数矣，海师云，此海神有所求，可即取舟中所载，弃之水中。物将尽，有一黄衣妇人，容色绝世，乘舟而来，四青衣卒刺船，皆朱发豕牙，貌甚可畏。妇人径（《广记》作“竟”）上船，问有好发髢可以见与，其人忙怖不复记，但云物已尽矣，妇人云：“在船后挂壁箧中”，如言而得之。船屋上有脯腊，妇人取以食四卒，视其手鸟爪也，持髢而去，舟乃达。廷禹又言其所（《广记》作“诸”）亲，自江西如广陵，携一十岁儿，行至马当，泊舟（《广记》无“舟”字）登岸晚望，及还船，失其儿，遍寻之，得于茂林中，已如痴矣。翌日，乃能言，云为人召去，有所教我，乃吹指长啸，有山禽数十百只应声而至，彩毛（《广记》作“毛彩”）怪异，人莫能识。自尔东下，时时吹啸，众禽必至。至白沙不敢复入，博访医巫治之，积久（《广记》“积久”作“久乃”）愈。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    135

    ○Zhu Tingyu

    The eunuch Zhu Tingyu from the Jiangnan region reported that a relative of his encountered a storm while sailing across the sea, and the boat nearly capsized several times. The sea captain said that the sea deity was making a request and that one could immediately take what was on board and throw it into the water. As the items were almost all gone, a woman dressed in yellow, with a beautiful appearance beyond compare, suddenly boarded the boat. Four soldiers dressed in blue were rowing the boat, and they had red hair and pig-like tusks, which were quite fearsome. The woman directly boarded the boat and asked if there was good hair and a headdress that could be given to her. The man was too busy and terrified to remember, but he said that the items were almost all gone. The woman said, "They are on the boat behind, in a chest hung on the wall," and they found them as she said. On the boat, there was dried meat hanging, which the woman took to feed the four soldiers. When she looked at their hands, they had bird claws, and she took the hair and headdress and left. The boat then safely reached its destination.

    Zhu Tingyu also reported that a relative of his traveled from Jiangxi to Yangzhou, carrying a ten-year-old son. They reached Madang and moored the boat to go ashore in the evening. When they returned to the boat, the son was missing. They searched everywhere and found him in a dense forest, but he was in a state of confusion. The next day, he was able to speak and said that someone had summoned him away and taught him something. He then blew his fingers and emitted a long whistle, and hundreds of strange birds responded to the sound. From then on, while traveling eastward, he would often whistle, and many birds would come. He dared not enter the white sand area again. He sought medical and magical treatment, and after a long time, he recovered.

    136

    ○僧德林（《广记》作“秋”）

    　　浙西僧德林，少时游舒州，路左见一夫荷锄治方丈之地，左右数十里不见居人，问之，对云：“顷时自舒之桐城，至此暴得痞疾，不能去，因卧草中，及稍醒，已昏矣，四望无人烟，惟虎豹吼叫，自分必死。俄有一人，部从如大将，至此下马，据胡床坐，（《广记》有“良”字）久，乃（《广记》无“乃”字）召二卒曰：善守此人，明日送至桐城县下。’遂上马去，倏忽不见，惟二卒在焉。某即强起问之，答，此茅将军也，常夜出猎虎，忧汝被伤，故使护汝。欲更问之，困而复卧，及觉已日出，不复见二卒，即起行，意甚轻健，若无疾者。至桐城，顷之疾愈，故以所见之处立祠祀之。”德林上舒州十年，及回，则村落皆立茅将军祠矣。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    136

    Monk De Lin (in "Guangji" it is written as "Qiu")

    A monk from Zhejiang named De Lin, when he was young, traveled to Shuzhou. Along the way, he saw a man carrying a hoe and tilling a plot of land. For dozens of miles in all directions, there was no sign of human habitation. He asked the man, who replied, "Recently from Shuzhou to Tongcheng, I suddenly contracted an abdominal illness and could not continue my journey. I lay down in the grass, and by the time I woke up, it was already dark. Looking all around, there was no one in sight, only the roars of tigers and leopards. I believed that I would surely die. Suddenly, there was a person, accompanied by a retinue like a general, who came here and sat on a trundle bed. After a long time, he called two soldiers and said, 'Guard this person well, and tomorrow take him to the outskirts of Tongcheng County.' Then he got on his horse and left, disappearing without a trace, leaving only the two soldiers behind. I struggled to get up and asked them, and they told me that this was General Mao. He often goes out at night to hunt tigers and worried that I would be injured, so he sent someone to protect me. I wanted to ask more, but I became tired again and lay down. When I woke up, it was already daylight, and the two soldiers were no longer there. I got up and continued my journey, feeling very light and healthy, as if I had never been ill. When I reached Tongcheng, my illness had completely disappeared. Therefore, I built a shrine at the place where this happened." Monk De Lin stayed in Shuzhou for ten years, and when he returned, all the villages had built shrines to General Mao. (From "Guangji," Volume 314)

    137

    ○司马正彝

    　　司马正彝者，始为小吏，行溧水道中，去前店尚远，而饥渴甚，意颇忧之。俄而，遇一新草店数间，独一妇人迎客，为设饮食，甚丰洁。正彝谢之，妇人云：“至都有好粉燕支（《广记》作“胭脂”），宜以为惠。”正彝许诺。至建业，遇其所知往溧水，因以粉燕支托遗其妇（九字广记作“因市粉脂遗之”七字），具告其处。既至，不复见店，有（《广记》作“但”）一神女庙，因置所遗而去。正彝后为溧水令。（《广记》有“相”字）传云，往往有遇（《广记》有“之”字）者，不知其详。（《广记》卷三百十四，不作未，详作审）

    Explanation

    137

    Chapter: Sima Zhengyi

    Sima Zhengyi, initially serving as a minor official, was traveling on the road to Lixiu. Still far from the previous inn, he was very hungry and thirsty, feeling quite anxious about it. Shortly thereafter, he encountered a new thatched inn with several rooms. A single woman greeted the guests and prepared food and drink, which was abundant and clean. Zhengyi thanked her, and the woman said, "In the capital, there is good powder and lipstick (as recorded in the Guangji, it is 'yānzhī' 胭脂). It would be appropriate to bring them as a gift." Zhengyi agreed.

    When he arrived in Jianye, he met someone he knew who was going to Lixiu. So he entrusted the powder and lipstick to be given to her wife (as recorded in the Guangji, it is "because he bought powder and lipstick to give to her" 七字), and told him where to find the place. After arriving, he no longer saw the inn. There was (as recorded in the Guangji, it is "only") a temple dedicated to a goddess, and he then placed the gift and left. Later, Zhengyi became the magistrate of Lixiu (as recorded in the Guangji, there is an additional "xiāng" 相).

    It is said that often met by others (as recorded in the Guangji, there is an additional "zhī" 之), but the details are unknown. (As recorded in the Guangji, Volume 314, it does not contain "wèi" 未, and "xiáng" 详 is written as "shěn" 审.)

    138

    ○刘宣

    　　戊寅岁（案：戊寅当梁贞明四年，吴天祐十五年），吴（师）征越，败于临安，裨将刘宣，伤重卧于死人中。至夜，有官吏数人持簿书至，遍阅死者，至宣乃扶起视之，曰：“此汉非是。”引出十余步，置路左而去。明日贼退，宣乃得归。宣肥白如瓠，初伏于地越人割其尻肉，宣不敢动。后疮愈，肉不复生，臀竟小偏，十余年而卒。（《广记》卷三百十四，“而”作“乃”。曾慥《类说》亦引）

    138

    In the year of Wu Yin (戊寅岁, corresponding to the fourth year of the reign of Emperor Zhuangzong of Later Liang and the fifteenth year of the reign of Emperor Taizu of Wu), the Wu army (吴师) campaigned against the Yue kingdom but was defeated at Lin'an, the capital of Yue. A subordinate general named Liu Xuan (刘宣) was seriously wounded and lay among the dead. At night, several officials arrived carrying documents and examined all the dead bodies. When they reached Liu Xuan, they lifted him up and looked at him, saying, "This man is not one of them." They led him out several steps and placed him on the side of the road before leaving. The next day, when the enemy retreated, Liu Xuan was able to return. Liu Xuan was fat and white like a gourd. Initially, he lay on the ground while the Yue people cut off his buttock flesh, and he dared not move. Later, when the wound healed, the flesh did not grow back, and his buttocks remained smaller and uneven. He died after more than ten years. (This account is found in volume 314 of the "Guang Ji" (《广记》), where "而" is rendered as "乃". It is also cited in Zeng Zao's "Lei Shuo" (曾慥《类说》).)

    139

    ○黄鲁

    　　徐三诲为抚州录事参军，其下干力黄鲁者，郡之俚人，年少颇白皙，有父母在乡中，数月一告归，归旬日复来。一旦归来，月余不至，三诲遣吏至其家召之。家人云：“久不归矣。”于是散寻之，又月余乃见，在深山中，黄衣屣履挟弹而游，与他少年数人皆衣服相同（《广记》作“类”），捕之不获。鲁家富，乃召募（《广记》有“人”字）伏于（《广记》无“于”字）草间以伺之。数日，果擒之，而诸少年皆走，归问其故，曰：“山中有石氏者，其家如王公，纳我为婿。”他无所言，留数日，复失去，又于山中求得之，如是者三。后一日，竟去，遂不复见。寻石氏之居亦不能得。此山乃临川人采石之所，盖石之神也。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    139

    Huang Lu

    Xu Sanhui served as the registrar of Fuzhou. Among his subordinates was Huang Lu, a young and fair-skinned local man from the region. Huang Lu had parents in the countryside and would return home every few months, staying for ten days before coming back. One day, after returning, he did not come back for over a month. Xu Sanhui sent officials to his home to summon him. His family said, "He hasn't been back for a long time." They then searched for him, and after another month, they found him in a deep mountain, wearing yellow clothes and wooden shoes, carrying a slingshot and playing with several other young men who were all dressed similarly. They tried to capture him but failed. Huang Lu's family was wealthy, so they recruited people to hide in the grass and wait for him. After several days, they finally caught him, and the other young men fled. When they asked him why, he said, "There is a family named Shi in the mountains, and they are like nobles, and they took me as a son-in-law." He said nothing else. They kept him for a few days, but he disappeared again. They found him again in the mountains, and this happened three times. On a later day, he finally left and was never seen again. They also could not find the residence of the Shi family. This mountain is where people from Linchuan mine stones, and it seems to be the spirit of the stone. (From the Yingyai Shenglan Volume 314)

    140

    ○张鋋

    　　张鋋者，累任邑宰，以廉直称。后为彭泽令，至县宅，堂后有神祠，祠前巨木成林，乌鸢（《广记》“乌鸢”二字作“为”字）野禽，群巢其上，粪秽积于堂中，人畏其神，故莫敢犯。鋋大（《广记》无“大”字）恶之，使巫祝（《广记》作“祀”）于神曰：“所为土地之神，当洁清，县署以奉居人，奈何使腥秽如是耶？尔三日中当尽逐众禽，不然吾将焚庙而伐树矣。”居二日有数大鹗奋击而至，尽壤群巢。又一日，大雨，粪秽皆净。自此，宅居清洁矣。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    140

    Zhang Zhan, who served repeatedly as a magistrate, was known for his integrity and uprightness. Later, he became the magistrate of Pengze County. Upon arriving at the county office, he found a shrine located behind the main hall, with a grove of giant trees in front of it. Wild birds, including crows and hawks, nested in large numbers on the trees, and their droppings and other waste had accumulated in the main hall. People feared the spirit of the shrine, so no one dared to interfere. Zhang Zhan was greatly displeased with this situation and sent a shaman to pray to the spirit, saying, "The spirit of the land should be clean and pure, and the county office should serve the residents. Why is it so dirty and foul? You will drive away all the birds within three days, otherwise, I will burn the temple and cut down the trees." After two days, several large eagles flew in aggressively and destroyed all the nests. On the next day, it rained heavily, and the droppings were washed away. From then on, the residence was clean.

    141

    ○浔阳县吏

    　　庚寅岁（案：庚寅当唐长兴元年，吴大和二年），江西节度使徐知谏，以钱百万修庐山使者庙。浔阳令遣一吏典其事，此吏尝入城，召一画工俱往，画工负荷丹彩，杂物从之。始出城，吏昏然若醉，自解衣带投地，画工以吏（《广记》无吏字）为醉，而随之，须臾复脱衣弃帽，比至山中，殆至裸身。近庙，涧水中有一卒，青衣白韦蔽膝，吏至乃执之，画工救之曰：“此醉人也。”卒怒曰：“交交加加，谁能得会？”竟擒之，坐于水中。工知其非人也，走往庙中告人，竞往视之，卒已不见，其吏犹坐水中，已死矣。乃阅其出纳之籍，则已乾没过半。进士谢岳见（《广记》“见”上有“亲”字）之。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    141

    In the year of Gengyin (930 AD, during the Longxing era of the Tang Dynasty and the Tahe era of the Wu Dynasty), the military governor of Jiangxi, Xu Zhiyan, spent one million coins to repair the Temple of the Messenger on Mount Lu. The magistrate of Xunyang sent an official to oversee the project. One day, this official entered the city and summoned a painter to accompany him. The painter carried his painting tools and followed the official. As they left the city, the official became dazed and disoriented, as if drunk, and removed his belt and threw it on the ground. The painter, thinking the official was drunk, followed him. Soon after, the official took off his clothes and hat. By the time they reached the temple, he was nearly naked. Near the temple, in a stream, there was a soldier dressed in a blue robe and a white leather knee guard. When the official approached, the soldier seized him. The painter, realizing something was wrong, said, "This man is drunk." The soldier angrily replied, "Confused and disoriented, who can understand this?" He then captured the official and placed him in the water. The painter, knowing the soldier was not human, ran to the temple and told others about the incident. When they went to see, the soldier had disappeared, and the official was found dead in the water. Upon reviewing the records of the funds, it was discovered that more than half had been embezzled. The scholar Xie Yue witnessed this event.

    142

    ○朱元吉

    　　乌江县令朱元吉，言其所知，泛舟至采石遇风，同行者数舟皆没。某既溺，不复见水，道路如人间，其人驱之东行，可在东岸，山下有大府署，门外堆坏船版木如邱陵，复有诸（《广记》“诸”字在“运”字下）人运溺者财物入库中甚多。（《广记》作“众”）入门堂上有官人，遍召溺者，阅籍审之。至某独曰：“此人不合来，可令送出”，吏即引去。复至舟所，舟中财物亦皆还之。怳然不自知，出水已在西岸沙上矣。举船俨然，亦无沾湿。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    142

    The Magistrate of Wujia County, Zhu Yuanji, recounts his experience: While sailing to Cai Shi, he encountered a storm, and all the boats traveling with him sank. After drowning, he no longer saw water around him. The path he saw was like the human world, and someone drove him eastward, where he could reach the eastern bank. At the foot of the mountain, there was a large government office, outside of which were piled ruined boat planks like hills. There were also many people transporting the property of the drowned into the treasury in great quantities. Upon entering the hall, he saw an official who called all the drowned and reviewed their records. When it came to him, the official said alone, "This person should not be here, can be sent out," and an official immediately led him away. He returned to the boat, and the property in the boat was also returned to him. Suddenly, without knowing, he emerged from the water and found himself on the west bank sand. The entire boat was intact, and it was also not wet.

    ○酤酒王氏

    　　建康江宁县廨之后，有酤酒王氏，以平直称。癸卯岁，二月既望，夜，店人将闭外户，忽有朱衣数人，仆（《广记》有“马”字）甚盛，奄至户前，叱曰：“开门，吾将暂憩于此。”店人奔告其主，其主曰：“出迎。”则已入坐矣。主人因设酒食甚备，又犒诸从者，客甚谢焉。顷之，有仆夫执细（《广记》作“捆”）绳百千丈，又一人执撅弋数百枚，前白请布围，紫衣可之。即出以弋钉地，系绳其上，围坊曲人家使遍。良久曰：“事讫。”紫衣起，至户外，从者白此店亦在围中矣。

    Explanation

    143

    A Wine Shop of the Wang Family

    After the official residence in Jiangning County, Jiankang, there was a wine shop owned by the Wang family, known for its fairness and straightforwardness. In the year of the Water Rabbit, on the 15th day of the second month, at night, the shopkeeper was about to close the outer door when suddenly several people dressed in red, riding on magnificent horses, arrived abruptly at the door and shouted, "Open the door, we will take a brief rest here." The shopkeeper rushed to inform the owner, who said, "Go out and greet them." By the time he did, they had already entered and sat down. The owner then prepared a well-stocked feast and also rewarded the followers, to which the guests thanked him greatly. Shortly after, a servant carried a rope hundreds or thousands of feet long, and another person held hundreds of wooden stakes. They came forward and requested permission to set up a perimeter. The purple-clad person approved it. They then drove the stakes into the ground, tied the rope to them, and enclosed the alleys and homes of the neighborhood. After a long while, they said, "The matter is completed." The purple-clad person stood up, went to the threshold, and the followers informed him that the shop was also within the enclosure.

    144

    紫衣相谓曰：“主人相待甚厚，空（《广记》作“免”）此一店可乎？”皆曰：“一家耳，何为不可？”即命移代，出店于围外。顾主人曰：“以此相报。”遂去，倏忽不见。顾视绳弋已亡矣。俄而，巡使欧阳进逻（《广记》有“巡”字）夜至店前，问：“何故深夜开门？又不灭灯烛，何也？”主人具告所见，进不信，执之下狱，将以妖言罪之。居一日，江宁（《广记》“江宁”作“建康”）大火，（《广记》有“自”字）朱雀桥西至凤台山，居人焚之殆尽，此店四邻皆为煨烬，而王氏独免。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    144

    The purple-clad officials spoke to each other, saying, "The host treated us very well. Can we leave this store empty?" All replied, "It's just one store, what's the problem?" They immediately ordered to move it and relocated the store outside the enclosure. Turning to the host, they said, "As a way to repay, we will do this." They then left, disappearing suddenly. Looking back, the ropes and hooks were already gone. Soon after, the patrol officer Euang Jin arrived at the store at night and asked, "Why did you open the door so late at night? And why didn't you extinguish the lights?" The host fully reported what he saw, but Jin did not believe him and arrested him, putting him in jail, intending to punish him for spreading rumors. After one day, a great fire broke out in Jiangning, from west of Zhuge Bridge to Fengtai Mountain, most of the residents were burned to death, and the four neighboring stores were all reduced to ashes. But the Wang family alone was spared.

    ○鲍回

    　　鲍回者，尝入深山捕猎，见一少年裸卧大树下，毛发委地，回欲射之，少年曰：“我山神也，避君不及，勿杀我，富贵可致。”回以刃刺其口，血皆逆流，遂杀之，无何回卒。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    　　○梨山庙

    　　建州梨山庙，土人云：“故相李回之庙。”回贬为建州刺史，后卒于临川。卒之夕，建安人咸梦回乘白马入梨山，及凶问至，因立祠焉，世传灵应。王延政在建安，与福州构隙，使其将吴某帅兵向晋安，吴新铸一剑，甚利，将行，携剑祷于梨山庙，且曰：“某愿以此剑手杀千（毛本作“十”）人。”其夕梦神谓己曰：“人不当发恶愿，（《广记》有“吾”字）祐汝，使汝不死于人之手。”既战败绩，左右皆溃散。追兵将及，某自度不免，即以此剑自刎而死。（《广记》卷三百十五）

    Explanation

    145

    ○鲍回

    Bo Hui once entered a deep mountain to hunt and saw a young man lying naked under a large tree with his hair hanging to the ground. Bo wanted to shoot him, but the young man said, "I am a mountain god, I could not avoid you, do not kill me, wealth and nobility can be achieved." Bo stabbed his mouth with a blade, and the blood all flowed backward, thus killing him. Shortly after, Bo died. (From Volume 314 of the Guangji)

    ○梨山庙

    The Li Mountain Temple in Jianzhou, according to the locals, is the temple of the former Prime Minister Li Bo. Li was demoted to be the governor of Jianzhou and later died in Linchuan. On the night of his death, all the people of Jian'an dreamed that Li rode a white horse into Li Mountain. When the news of his death arrived, a shrine was established there, and it is said to be miraculous and responsive. King Yan Zheng was in Jian'an, and he had a conflict with Fuzhou. He sent his general Wu to lead troops towards Jin'an. Wu newly forged a sword, which was very sharp. Before leaving, he carried the sword and prayed at the Li Mountain Temple, saying, "I wish to use this sword to kill a thousand (Mao's version says 'ten') people by hand." That night, he dreamed that a god said to him, "One should not make evil wishes, I will protect you, so that you do not die at the hands of others." After the battle, he suffered defeat, and his attendants all fled. The pursuing soldiers were about to catch up, and he realized he could not escape. He immediately cut his own throat with the sword and died. (From Volume 315 of the Guangji)

    ○吴延瑫

    　　广陵有仓官吴延瑫者，其弟既冠，将为求妇，邻有某妪，素受吴氏之命。一日，有人诣门云：“张司空家使召。”随之而去，在正（《广记》作“政”）胜寺之东南，宅甚雄壮，妪云：“初不闻有张公在是。”其人云：“公没于临安之战，故少人知者。”久之（《广记》作“知”），其家陈设炳焕如王公家，见一老姥，云是县君，及（《广记》作“之”）坐顷之，其女亦出，姥谓妪曰：“闻君为（毛本作“谓”）吴家求婚，吾欲以此女事之。

    Explanation

    146

    There was a warehouse official named Wu Yantao in Guangling. His younger brother had just come of age and would be seeking a wife for him. A certain old woman who had always received the command of the Wu family came to the door and said, "The envoy from Zhang the Grand Works Commissioner's household summoned." Wu Yantao followed him and went away, to the southeast of Zhengsheng Temple. The residence was very grand and imposing. The old woman said, "I never heard that there was a Mr. Zhang here." The person replied, "He died in the battle of Lin'an, so few people know about it." After a while, the household's furnishings were splendid like those of a noble family. They saw an old woman who said she was the County Lady. After sitting for a while, her daughter also came out. The County Lady said to the old woman, "I heard that you are seeking a wife for the Wu family. I wish to marry this daughter to him."

    147

    ”妪曰：“吴氏小吏贫家，岂当与贵人为婚耶？”女因自言曰：“儿以母老无兄弟，家业既大事托善人，闻吴氏子孝谨可事，岂求高门耶？”妪曰：“诺。”将问之归以告延瑫，异之，未敢言。数日，忽有车与数乘诣邻妪之室，乃张氏女与二老婢俱至，使召延瑫之妻，即席具酒食甚丰，皆张氏所备也。其女自议婚事，瑫妻内思之，此女虽极端丽，然可年三十余，其小郎年却（《广记》作“节”）少，未必欢也。其女即言曰：“夫妻皆系前定，义（《广记》有“如有”二字）合岂当嫌老少耶？”瑫妻耸然，不敢复言。女即出红白罗二匹，曰：“以此为礼。”其他赠遣甚多。至暮，邀邻妪俱归其家，留数宿，谓妪曰：“吾家至富，人不知尔，他日皆吴郎所有也。”室中三大厨，其厨高至屋，因开示之一，厨实以银。

    Explanation

    147

    The old woman said, "The Wu family is a poor household with a minor official; how could they marry into a noble family?" The daughter then spoke, saying, "I am marrying because my mother is old and I have no brothers. I need to entrust the family affairs to a virtuous person. I have heard that the Wu family's son is filial and diligent; I do not seek a high-status marriage." The old woman replied, "Agreed."

    A few days later, several vehicles suddenly arrived at the old woman's house. Zhang's daughter and two elderly maids came together, and they summoned Yan Tuo's wife. A well-prepared feast was set up immediately, all provided by the Zhang family. The daughter discussed the marriage matter herself. Yan Tuo's wife thought to herself, "This daughter is extremely beautiful, but she is likely in her thirties, and her son is much younger. They may not be happy together." The daughter said, "Marriage is predestined. If there is a good match, should we care about age differences?" Yan Tuo's wife was startled and did not dare to speak further.

    The daughter then offered two pieces of red and white silk, saying, "Take this as a gift." She also gave many other gifts. By evening, she invited the old woman to stay at her home for several nights. The daughter said, "Our family is very wealthy, and people do not know it. In the future, everything will belong to Wu Lang." There were three large kitchens in the house, one of which was as tall as the house. The daughter showed one of them, which was filled with silver.

    148

    （《广记》作“金”，下有“二厨实以银”五字）又指地曰：“此中皆钱也。”即命掘之，深尺余，即见钱充积。又至外厅，庭中系朱鬣白马，傍有一豕，曰：“此皆礼物也。”厅之西，复有广厦，百工制作毕备，曰：“此亦造礼物也。”至夜就寝，闻豕有被惊声（《广记》“被”作“如无声”字），呼诸婢曰：“此豕不宜在外，是必为蛇所啮也。”妪曰：“蛇岂食猪者耶？”女曰：“此中常有之。”即相与秉烛视之，果见大赤蛇自地出，萦绕其豕，复入地去，救之得免。明日，方与妪别，忽召二青衣夹侍左右，谓妪曰：“吾有故近，出少选当还。”即与青衣凌虚而去。妪大惊，其母曰：“吾女暂之天上会计，但坐无苦也。

    (The Comprehensive Records notes that the original text read "gold" instead of "silver" and included the phrase "two cabinets filled with silver.") She then pointed to the ground and said, "This place is all money." Immediately, she ordered digging, and after digging about a foot deep, they found the ground filled with money. She then went to an outer hall, where in the courtyard was a red-maned white horse and beside it a pig. She said, "These are all gifts." To the west of the hall was another large house, fully equipped with craftsmen, and she said, "This is also for making gifts." At night, as she was about to sleep, she heard the pig make a sound as if it were being startled (The Comprehensive Records notes that the original text read "as if it were silent"). She called her maidservants and said, "This pig should not be outside; it must have been bitten by a snake." The elderly woman said, "Would a snake eat a pig?" The girl replied, "There are often snakes here." They then lit candles and looked, and indeed they saw a large red snake emerge from the ground, coil around the pig, and then return to the ground. They managed to save the pig. The next morning, as she was about to bid farewell to the elderly woman, she suddenly summoned two maidservants to attend her on either side and said to the elderly woman, "I have something urgent nearby; I will return shortly." She then left with the maidservants, floating through the air. The elderly woman was greatly surprised, and her mother said, "My daughter has temporarily gone to a heavenly accounting; just sit and there is no need to worry."

    149

    ”少（《广记》作“食”）顷，乃见自外而入，微有酒气，曰：“诸仙留饮，吾以媒妪在此，固辞得还。”妪回（《广记》作“归”）益骇，异而不敢言。又月余，复召妪“县君疾亟”，及往，其母已卒。同（《广记》作“因”）妪至葬，葬于杨子县北徐氏村中，尽室往会。徐氏有女，可十余岁，张氏抚之曰：“此女有相，当为淮北一武将之妻，善视之。”既葬，复厚赠妪，举家南去，莫知所之。婚事（《广记》无“事”字）亦竟不成。妪归，访其故居，但里舍数间，问其里中，云：“住此已久，相传云张司空之居。”竟不得其处，（《广记》作“是”）后十年，广陵乱，吴氏之弟归于建业，亦竟无恙。（《广记》卷三百十五）

    Explanation

    149

    A short while later (or after eating), she saw someone entering from outside, with a faint smell of alcohol, who said, "The immortals invited me to drink, and I declined firmly because the matchmaker was here, so I was allowed to return." The matchmaker returned (or went home) even more startled, finding it strange but dared not speak of it. Another month later, she was summoned again, "The Lady of the County is gravely ill," and when she went, her mother had already passed away. Along with the matchmaker, they attended the burial, which took place in the village of Xu in the north of Yangzhi County, and the entire family attended. The Xu family had a daughter, about ten or more years old, whom the Zhang family comforted, saying, "This girl has a good appearance and will become the wife of a military officer in Huaibei; treat her well." After the burial, they gave the matchmaker generous gifts and the whole family went south, and no one knew where they went. The marriage also ultimately did not take place. The matchmaker returned and visited the old residence, but there were only a few houses in the neighborhood. When she asked the locals, they said, "They have lived here for a long time, and it is said to be the residence of Zhang Sike." She could not find the place. (In the Guangji version, it is written as "is") Ten years later, during the turmoil in Guangling, the younger brother of the Wu family returned to Jianye and remained unharmed. (From the Guangji, Volume 315)

    150

    ○贝禧

    　　义兴人贝禧，为邑之乡胥。乾宁甲寅岁十月，宿于菱渎别业，夜分，忽闻扣门者，人马之声甚众，出视之，见一人绿衣秉简西面而立，从者百余。禧摄衣出迎，自通曰：“某（《广记》作“隆”）姓周殷名（《广记》“殷名”二字作“第十八”三字）。”即延入坐，问以来意，曰：“余（《广记》无“余”字）身为地府南曹判官，奉王命召君为北曹判官尔。”禧初甚惊，殷（《广记》作“惧”）“徐谓”（《广记》徐“谓”二字作“隆”字）曰：“此乃阴府要职，何易及此！君无（毛本作“何”）辞也。”俄有从者持床褥（《广记》作“榻”）、食案、帷幕，陈设毕（《广记》有“满”字）置，酒食对饮。良久，一吏趋入，白（《广记》有“殷”字）判官至。

    Explanation

    150

    Bei Xi, a native of Yixing, served as a village scribe. In the tenth month of the year Jia Yin during the Qian Ning period, he stayed at his summer residence by the Lingdu Creek. At midnight, he suddenly heard many people and horses knocking on the door. He went out to see, and saw a man in green clothing holding a tablet facing west, with over a hundred attendants. Bei Xi hurriedly dressed and went out to greet him, introducing himself. The man said, "My name is Zhou Yin." Bei Xi invited him in to sit and asked about his purpose. The man said, "I am the Southern Department Judge of the Underworld, and I have been ordered by the King to summon you as the Northern Department Judge." Initially very surprised, Zhou Yin calmly said, "This is a high-ranking position in the Underworld, how could it be so easy to attain! Do not refuse." Soon, attendants brought beds, tables, and curtains, setting everything up. They drank wine and ate together. After a long time, a clerk hurried in and reported that the Judge had arrived.

    151

    复有一绿衣，秉简，二从者捧箱（《广记》作“简”）随之。箱中亦绿衣，殷揖禧曰：“命赐君，兼同奉召。”即以绿裳为禧衣之。就坐共饮，将（《广记》作“可”）至五更，曰：“王命不可留矣。”即（《广记》有“相”字）与偕行，禧曰：“此去家不远，暂归告别可乎？”皆曰：“君今已死，纵复（《广记》无“复”字）归，安得（《广记》作“可复”）与家人相接耶。”乃出门与周殷各乘一马，其疾如风行水上（“行水上”《广记》作“涉水不溺”），至暮宿一村居（《广记》作“店”），店中具酒食而无居人，虽设灯烛，如隔帷幔，云：“已行二千余里矣。”向晓复行，久之，至一城，门卫严峻，周殷先入，复出召禧，凡经三门，左右吏卒皆趋拜，复入一门，正北大殿垂帘，禧趋走参谒，一同人间。

    Explanation

    151

    There was another man in green attire, holding a bamboo tablet, with two attendants carrying a box (according to the Guangji, it is "简") following him. Inside the box was also a green robe. Yin bowed to Xī and said, "The order is to grant you this, and you are also summoned together." They then dressed Xī in the green robe. They sat down and drank together, and as it approached the fifth watch (according to the Guangji, it is "可"), they said, "The king's order cannot be delayed." They then went out together, and Xī said, "This place is not far from my home; can I temporarily return to bid farewell?" They all replied, "You are now dead; even if you return, how can you meet your family again?" They then went out, and Zhou and Yin each rode a horse, moving as swiftly as the wind on water (according to the Guangji, it is "涉水不溺"). By evening, they reached a village and stayed overnight in an inn (according to the Guangji, it is "店"). The inn had prepared food and drink, but there were no inhabitants. Even though lamps and candles were set up, it was as if separated by curtains. They said, "We have traveled over two thousand miles." They resumed their journey at dawn and, after a long time, reached a city. The gate guards were strict, and Zhou and Yin entered first, then came out to summon Xī. They passed through three gates, and the officials and soldiers on both sides hurried to bow. They then entered another gate, and in front of the northern main hall, a curtain hung down. Xī hurried to pay his respects, just like in the human world.

    152

    既出，周殷（《广记》无“殷”字）谓禧曰：“此（《广记》作“北”）曹阙官多年，第宅曹署皆须整缉，君可暂止吾家也。”即自殿门东行，可一里，有大宅，止禧于东厅。顷之，有同官可三十余人，皆来造请庆贺，遂置宴，宴罢，醉卧至晚（《广记》作“晓”），遍诣诸官曹报谢。复有朱衣吏，以王命致泉（《广记》作至“钱”）帛车马，廪（《广记》作“饔”）饩甚丰备。翌日，周谓禧曰：“可视事矣。”又相与向王殿之东北，有大宅，陈设甚严，止禧于中，有典吏，可八十余人，参请给使。厅之南，空（《广记》作“大”）屋数十间，即曹局，簿书充积其内；厅之北，别室两间，有几案及有数（《广记》“有数”作“数书”）厨，皆宝五（《广记》“宝玉”作“杂宝”）饰之。

    After exiting, Zhou Yin (with "殷" omitted in the Guangji) told Xi, "This department has been without an official for many years, and the residence and offices all need to be tidied up and organized. You may temporarily stay at my home." They immediately went east from the palace gate, about one li, where there was a large mansion, and they stopped Xi in the east hall. After a while, about thirty colleagues came to congratulate him. They then held a banquet, and after the banquet, he slept drunk until late evening, visiting all the officials to thank them. Then there were officials in red robes, delivering money, silk, carriages, and horses according to the king's command, and the provisions were very abundant. The next day, Zhou told Xi, "You may now take office." They then went together to the northeast of the king's palace, where there was a large mansion with very strict arrangements, and they stopped Xi in the middle, where there were over eighty clerks, who came to serve him. To the south of the hall, there were dozens of empty rooms, which were the department's offices, filled with documents; to the north of the hall, there were two separate rooms, with tables and several cabinets, all decorated with precious materials.

    153

    周以金钥授禧曰：“此厨簿书最为秘要，管钥恒当自掌，勿轻委人也。”周既去，禧开视之，书册积叠，皆方尺余，首取一册，金题其上，作（《广记》无“作”字）陕州字，其中字甚细密，谛视之乃可见，皆世人之名簿也。禧欲知其家事，复开一厨，乃得常州簿，阅其家籍，见身及家人世代名字甚悉，其已死者以墨钩之。至晚，周殷判官复至曰：“王以君世寿未尽，遣暂还，寿尽当复居此职。”禧即以金钥还授于周。禧始阅簿时，尽记其家人及己祸福寿夭之事，将归（《广记》“将归”作“至是”）然尽忘矣。顷之，官吏俱至，告别周殷，二人送之归。翌日夜乃至菱渎村中，入室见己卧于床上，周殷与禧各就寝，俄而惊悟（《广记》作“寤”），日正午时，问其左右，云：“死殆（《广记》作“始”）半日”，而地府已四日矣。禧即愈，一如常人，亦无小异。又四十余年乃卒。（《广记》卷三百七十八）

    Explanation

    153

    Zhou handed over a golden key to Xi and said, "This kitchen ledger is the most secret and important. The key should always be held personally, do not lightly entrust it to others." After Zhou left, Xi opened it and saw that the books were piled up, all about one foot square. He took the first volume, which had golden characters inscribed on it, written in Shaanxi script. The characters were very fine and dense, and could only be seen upon careful examination. They were all ledgers of the names of people. Xi wanted to know about his family's affairs, so he opened another cabinet and obtained the Changzhou ledger. He read the family registry and saw the names of his own generation and his family's generations in great detail. Those who had died were marked with black ink. By evening, Zhou Yin and the judge returned and said, "The king believes your lifespan has not ended, and has sent you back temporarily. When your lifespan ends, you will return to this position." Xi immediately returned the golden key to Zhou. When Xi first read the ledger, he remembered everything about his family's and his own fortunes, misfortunes, lifespan, and death. Returning home, he suddenly forgot everything. Shortly after, officials all arrived, farewelled Zhou Yin, and the two of them sent him home. The next night he arrived at Lingdu Village, entered the room, and saw himself lying on the bed. Zhou Yin and Xi each went to sleep. Suddenly, he woke up. It was noon. He asked those around him, "It was almost half a day," but in the underworld it was already four days. Xi immediately recovered, just like an ordinary person, with no small differences. And he died forty years later.

    ○支戬

    　　江左有支戬者，余干人，世为小吏，至戬独好学为文，窃自称秀才。会正月望夜，时俗取饭箕衣之，衣服插箸为觜，使画盘粉以卜。戬见家人（毛本无“见”字“人”字）为之，即（毛本“即”字作“其时”二字）戏祝曰：“请卜支秀才他日至何官。”乃画粉宛成司空字。又戬尝梦至地府，尽阅名簿，至己籍云“至司空，（以上二十四字毛本脱）年五十余”，他人籍不可记，惟记其友人郑元枢（《广记》有“云”字）贫贱无官，（毛本有“亡”字）年四十八。元枢后居浙西廉使，徐知谏宾礼之，将荐于执政，行有日矣，暴疾而卒，实年四十八。戬后为金陵观察判官，检校司空，但（《广记》作“恒”）以此事话于亲友，竟卒于任，年五十一。（《广记》卷一百五十八）

    Explanation

    154

    支戬

    In the Jiangnan region, there was a man named Zhi Jian from Yudan County. His family had been minor officials for generations, but Zhi Jian alone was fond of learning and writing, secretly calling himself a scholar. During the first full moon of the lunar year, it was customary for people to wear a rice scoop as a hat and insert chopsticks into it to form a beak-like shape, then draw patterns on a plate of powder for divination. Zhi Jian saw his family (or someone) doing this, and he jokingly prayed, “Let’s predict what high office Zhi Jian will hold in the future.” The pattern drawn on the plate resembled the character for “司空” (an ancient high-ranking official).

    Zhi Jian also once dreamed of going to the underworld, where he thoroughly reviewed the records of fate. His own record stated, “He will become a 司空 and live to be over fifty,” though he could not remember the records of others, only recalling that his friend Zheng Yuanshu was poor, lowly, and without official rank, dying at the age of forty-eight. Later, Zheng Yuanshu became an official in charge of administrative and judicial affairs in western Zhejiang, where he was treated with respect by Xu Zhijian, who intended to recommend him to the central government. However, Zheng died suddenly from a severe illness, at the age of forty-eight.

    Afterward, Zhi Jian became an official in charge of overseeing and judging administrative matters in Nanjing, and was appointed as a 检校司空 (Inspector of Works). He often spoke of this matter to his friends and relatives, and eventually died in office at the age of fifty-one.

    ○食黄精婢

    　　临川有士人唐遇（《广记》无“唐遇”二字），虐其所使婢，婢不堪其毒，乃逃入山中。久之，粮尽饥甚，坐水边，见野草枝叶可爱，即拔取濯水中，连根食之，甚美。自是恒食，久之遂不饥，而更轻健。夜息大树下，闻草中兽走，以为虎而惧，因念得上树杪乃生也，正尔念之，而身已在树杪矣。及晓又念当下平地，又效然而下。自是，意有所之，身辄（《广记》作“即”）飘然而去。或自一峰之一峰顶，若飞鸟焉。数岁，其家人伐薪见之，以告其主，使捕之不得。一日遇其在绝壁下。

    Explanation

    155

    A Maid Who Ate Huangjing

    In the region of Linchuan, there was a scholar named Tang Yu (the Guangji omits the name "Tang Yu"). He abused the maid he employed, and she could not bear his cruelty, so she fled into the mountains. After a long time, she ran out of food and was extremely hungry. Sitting by the water, she saw a wild grass with beautiful leaves and immediately pulled it out, washed it in the water, and ate the root, which was very delicious. From then on, she always ate it, and after a long time, she no longer felt hungry and became lighter and stronger. At night, she slept under a big tree and heard animals running in the grass, thinking it was a tiger and being afraid. She thought that if she could get up to the top of the tree, she would live, and just as she thought that, her body was already at the top of the tree. By morning, she thought about descending to the ground and effortlessly descended. From then on, whenever she had an intention, her body would suddenly and swiftly move. Sometimes, she would travel from the top of one peak to another, like a flying bird. After several years, her family members who were cutting firewood saw her, reported it to the master, and the master tried to capture her but failed. One day, he encountered her at the bottom of a steep cliff.

    即以网（《广记》作“细绳”）三面围之，俄而（《广记》无“而”字）腾上山顶，其主亦骇异，必欲致之。或曰：“此婢也，安有仙骨？不过得灵药饵之尔。试以盛馔，多其五味，令甚香美，致（《广记》作“值”）其往来之路，观其食（《广记》有“之”字）否？”果（《广记》无“果”字）如其言，常（《广记》作“果”）来就食，食讫不复能远去，遂为所擒。具述其故，问其所食草之形状（《广记》无“状”字），即黄精也。复使寻之，遂不能得，其婢数年亦卒。（《广记》卷四百十四，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    "Immediately using a net (or fine rope, according to Guangji) to encircle it on three sides, it soon after (or shortly, according to Guangji) leaped up to the top of the mountain.     ○豫章人

    　　豫章人好食蕈，有黄姑蕈者，尤为美味。有民家治舍，烹此蕈以食工人。工人有登厨（《广记》无“厨”字）屋施瓦者，下视无人，惟釜中（《广记》无“中”字）煮物，以盆覆之，俄有一（《广记》无“一”字）小鬼倮身绕釜而走，倏忽投（《广记》作“没”）于釜中。顷之，主人设蕈，工人（《广记》无“人”字）独不食，亦不言其故（《广记》无“其故”二字），既暮，其（《广记》无“其”字）食蕈者皆卒。（《广记》卷四百十七）

    Explanation

    157

    A Woman from Yuzhang

    The people of Yuzhang (Nanchang) enjoy eating mushrooms, and among them, the yellow mushroom is particularly delicious. One household was repairing their house and cooked this mushroom to feed the workers. Among the workers, there was one who climbed onto the roof to lay tiles. He looked down and saw no one, only a pot with something cooking, covered by a bowl. Suddenly, a small ghost, naked, ran around the pot and then jumped into the pot in a flash. Soon after, the owner served the mushrooms, but the worker alone did not eat and did not explain why. By evening, those who had eaten the mushrooms all died.

    ●拾遗

    　　○龙昌裔

    　　戊子岁（案：戊子当唐天成三年，吴乾贞二年），旱，庐陵人龙昌裔，有米数千斛粜。既而米价稍贱，昌裔乃为文祷神冈庙，祈更一月不雨，祠讫。还至路，憩亭中，俄有黑云一朵（《广记》作“片”）自庙后出，顷之雷雨大至，昌裔震死于亭外。官司检视之，脱巾，于髻中得书一纸（《广记》“书”在“纸下”），则祷庙之文也。昌裔有孙婿，（《广记》作“将”）应童子举，乡人以其事诉之，不获送考。（《广记》卷二百四十三，无“考”字）

    Explanation

    158

    In the year Wu Zi (which corresponds to the third year of the Tiancheng era of the Later Tang dynasty and the second year of the Qianzhen era of the Southern Tang dynasty), there was a severe drought. Long Changyi, a man from Luling, had several thousand hu of rice to sell. Soon after, the price of rice began to fall, so Long Changyi wrote a prayer and offered it at the Temple of the Mountain God, asking for rain not to fall for another month. After the worship, he returned to the road and rested in a pavilion. Suddenly, a black cloud (as recorded in Yuehui as "a piece") emerged from behind the temple. Soon, a fierce thunderstorm broke out, and Long Changyi was struck dead outside the pavilion. Government officials came to investigate and found that he had removed his headband, and in his bun, they discovered a piece of paper (as recorded in Yuehui, the word "paper" appears after "book"). It turned out to be the prayer he had offered at the temple. Long Changyi had a grandson who was participating in the examination for young scholars (as recorded in Yuehui, the word "participate" is used instead of "take part in"). The villagers reported the incident to the authorities, but the grandson did not pass the examination (as recorded in Yuehui, the word "examination" is omitted).

    159

    ○李生

    　　中和末，有明经李生应举如长安，途遇一（《广记》无“一”字）道士同行，宿数日，言意相孚（《广记》作“得”），入关相别，因言黄白之术，道士曰：“点化之事，神仙小（《广记》作“浅”）术也。但世人多贪，将以济其侈，故仙道秘之。夫至道不烦，仙方简易，今人或贵重其药，艰难其事，皆非也。吾观子性静而寡欲，似可教者，今以方授子，可以济乏绝而已。如遂能不仕亦当不匮衣食；如得禄则勿复为，如（《广记》无“如”字）为之则贪也，仙道所不许也。”因手疏方，授之而别，（《广记》有“方”字）常药草数种而已。每遇乏绝，依方为之，无不成者。后及第，历州县官，时时为之，所得转少，及为南昌令，复为之，绝不成矣。从子智修为沙门，李以数丸与之。智修后游钟离，止卖药家，烧银得二十两以易衣。时刘仁规为刺史，方好其事，为人所告，遁而获免。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    159

    Li Sheng

    At the end of the Zhonghe era, there was a candidate for the Mingjing examination named Li Sheng who went to Chang'an to take the imperial examination. On his journey, he met a Taoist priest who accompanied him for several days, and they developed a deep understanding and trust in each other's words and intentions. They parted ways at the pass, and during their time together, the Taoist priest spoke about the art of alchemy. The Taoist priest said, "The transformation of base metals into precious ones is a minor skill of the immortals. But people are often greedy, and they use it to satisfy their desires, which is why the immortals keep it secret. The highest truth is simple and not complicated; the methods of the immortals are straightforward. Nowadays, some people place great value on the ingredients and find the process difficult, which is not correct. I see that you are calm and have few desires, and it seems you can be taught. I will now give you a formula to help you in times of need. If you manage to live without an official position, you will still have enough food and clothing. If you obtain an official position, do not continue to practice alchemy. Practicing it would be greedy, and the immortals do not allow it." The Taoist priest then wrote down the formula by hand, gave it to Li Sheng, and parted ways. The formula consisted of only a few common herbs. Whenever Li Sheng faced dire straits, he followed the formula, and it always succeeded. After passing the examination, Li Sheng served as a state and county official, occasionally practicing alchemy, but the results became less successful over time. When he became the magistrate of Nanchang, he tried again, but it failed completely. His son, Zhi Xiu, became a monk, and Li Sheng gave him some alchemical pills. Later, Zhi Xiu traveled to Zhongli and stayed at a place where medicines were sold. He melted silver to get twenty taels to exchange for clothes. At the time, Liu Rengui was the governor and was fond of this practice. Someone reported him, and he fled and was able to escape. (From Volume 85 of the Yingya Shenglan)

    160

    ○徐明府

    　　金乡徐明府者，隐而有道术，（《广记》有“人”字）莫能测。河南刘崇远，崇龟从弟也，有妹为尼，居楚州。常有一客尼寓宿，忽病劳。瘦甚且死，其姊（《广记》作“妹”）省之，众共见病者身中有气如飞虫，入其姊衣中，遂不见，病者死，姊亦病，俄而刘氏举院皆病，病者辄死。刘氏既（函）崇远，求于明府，徐曰：“尔有别业在金陵，可致金陵绢一疋，吾为尔疗之。”如言送绢讫，翌日，刘氏梦一道士执简而至，以简遍（毛本作编）抚其身，身中白气腾上如炊，既寤，遂轻爽能食，异于常日。顷之，徐封绢而至曰：“置绢席下，寝其上即差矣。”如其言，遂愈。已而神（《广记》作“视”）其绢，乃画（《广记》有“一”字）持简道士如所梦者。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    160

    Mr. Xu of Jinxiang

    Mr. Xu of Jinxiang was a reclusive official with esoteric knowledge and powers that could not be fathomed. Liu Chongyuan, the younger brother of Chonggui, from Henan, had a sister who became a nun and lived in Chuzhou. One day, a guest nun stayed there and suddenly fell ill with labor, becoming extremely thin and on the verge of death. Her sister visited her, and everyone saw a gas like a flying insect enter the sister's clothing, after which the gas disappeared and the patient died. The sister also fell ill, and soon the entire Liu household became sick, with each sick person dying in turn. Liu Chongyuan, upon hearing of this, sought help from Mr. Xu, who said, "You have a property in Jinling; bring one bolt of silk from there, and I will treat you." As instructed, the silk was sent, and the next day, Liu Chongyuan dreamed of a Taoist priest arriving with a tablet. The priest used the tablet to stroke his body, and white vapor rose from his body like cooking. Upon waking, he felt light and could eat, unlike before. Soon after, Mr. Xu arrived with the silk and said, "Place the silk under your mat and sleep on it, and you will recover." Following his advice, Liu Chongyuan recovered. Later, he examined the silk and found a painting of a Taoist priest holding a tablet, just as he had seen in his dream. (From Volume 85 of the Guangji)

    161

    ○华阴店妪

    　　杨彦伯，庐陵新淦人也，童子科（《广记》无“科”字）及第。天复辛酉岁，赴选至华阴，舍于逆旅，时京国多难，朝无亲识，选事不能如意（《广记》作“期”），亦（《广记》作“意”）甚忧闷。会豫章郎（《广记》作“邸”）吏姓杨，乡里旧知，同宿，于是因教己云：“凡行旅至此，未尝不祷于（《广记》作“金”）天，必获梦寐之报。纵无梦，则此店之妪亦能知方来事，苟获一言亦可矣。”彦伯因留一日，精意以祠之，尔夕竟无梦。既曙，店妪方迎送他客，又无所言，彦伯愈怏怏。将行忽失所著鞋，诘责僮仆甚喧，既即路，妪乃从而呼之曰：“少年何其喧耶？”彦伯因具道其事，妪曰：“嘻，此即神告也。

    Explanation

    161

    A Woman from Huayin Inn

    Yang Yanbo, a native of Xingan, Luzhou, passed the Tongzi examination. In the year Tianfu, Xin You (911 AD), he went to take the imperial examination and stayed at an inn in Huayin. At that time, the capital was in turmoil, and he had no close friends or acquaintances in the court. His selection process did not go as planned, and he was deeply troubled. Coincidentally, he met a government official from Yuzhang who shared the same surname, a fellow villager, and stayed with him for the night. The official then advised him, "Whenever travelers come here, they always pray to heaven, and they are sure to receive a dream as a response. Even if no dream comes, this innkeeper can also foresee future events. If you get even one word, it will suffice." Yanbo stayed for a day, worshipping with sincere intent, but that night, he had no dream. By dawn, the innkeeper was just welcoming and sending off other guests and had nothing to say, which made Yanbo even more dejected. As he was about to leave, he suddenly lost one of his shoes, and he scolded his servants loudly. Just as he was about to continue his journey, the innkeeper called out to him, saying, "Why are you so noisy, young man?" Yanbo then recounted his story, and the innkeeper said, "Ah, this is the divine message!"

    162

    夫将行而失其鞋，则（《广记》无“则”字）是事皆不谐矣。非徒如此而已也，京国将有乱，当不可复振（《广记》作“不复振振”，无“当”字，“可”字），君（毛本作“官”）当百艰备历，然不足为（《广记》“不足为”三字作“无”字）忧也。子之爵禄皆在江淮，官（《广记》作“宜”）当至门下侍郎。”彦伯因思之，江淮安得有门下侍郎？遂行至长安，适会大驾西幸，随至岐陇，梁寇围城（《广记》有“三年”二字），彦伯辛苦备至。驾既出城，彦伯逃还，吉州刺史彭珍厚遇之，累摄县邑。伪吴平江西，复见选用，登朝至户部侍郎，会临轩策命齐王，彦伯摄为门下侍郎行事，既受命，思店妪之言，大不悦，数月遂卒。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    162

    If one loses one's shoes before embarking on a journey, then all these matters will not go well. Not only that, but the capital will have turmoil, which will not be able to be restored. You will face a hundred hardships, but there is no need to be worried about it. Your rank and salary are all in the Jianghuai region, and you will become a Menxia Shilang (a high-ranking official). Yanbo thought about this and wondered, how could the Jianghuai region have a Menxia Shilang? So he traveled to Chang'an, happening to coincide with the emperor's western tour, and followed to Qiliang. The Liang rebels surrounded the city, and Yanbo suffered greatly. After the emperor had already left the city, Yanbo fled back. The Governor of Jizhou, Peng Zhen, treated him generously, and he frequently served as county magistrate. The pseudo-Wu state pacified Jiangxi, and he was again selected for service, rising to the position of Cao Bu Shilang (a high-ranking official). He happened to coincide with the emperor's audience to confer the title of Prince of Qi, and Yanbo was appointed as acting Menxia Shilang. After receiving the appointment, thinking of the shopkeeper's words, he was greatly displeased, and died several months later.

    ○刘处士

    　　张易在洛阳，遇处士刘某，颇有奇术，易恒与之游。（《广记》有“刘”字）常（《广记》作“尝”）卖药于市（《广记》作“卖银与市”，下“市”字无），市中人负（《广记》作“欠”）其直，刘从易往诉（《广记》作“索”）之，市人既不酬直，又大骂刘，刘归谓易曰：“彼愚人不识理，于是吾当小惩之，不尔必将为土地神灵之所（《广记》有“重”字）谴也。”既夜，灭烛就寝，积薪（《广记》“积薪”作“刘床前”三字）炽炭烧药。

    Final Translation

    Liu, the Reclusive Scholar

    Zhang Yi was in Luoyang when he met Liu, a reclusive scholar, who possessed some extraordinary skills. Zhang Yi always accompanied him on his travels. Liu often sold medicine in the market. One day, someone in the market owed Liu money. Liu went with Zhang Yi to demand the payment. The person in the market not only refused to pay but also insulted Liu. Liu returned and told Zhang Yi, "Those foolish people do not understand reason. Therefore, I will give them a small punishment. Otherwise, they will surely be punished by the local deities." After nightfall, they extinguished the candles and went to bed. Liu piled up wood and heated charcoal to burn the medicine.

    164

    易寐未熟，暗中见一神（《广记》作“人”）就炉吹火，火光中识其面，乃向之市人也，迨曙不复见。易后求其间（《广记》“其间”二字作“之”字）问市人，云：“一夕梦人召去，逼（毛本“逼”作“通”）使吹火，气殆不续，既寤唇肿气乏，旬日乃愈。”刘恒为河南尹张全义所礼，会与梁太祖食，思鱼鱠，全义曰：“吾有客，能立致之。”即召刘使掘小坎，汲水满之，垂钩，良久，即获鱼数头。梁祖大怒曰：“妖妄之甚者也。”即杖背二十，械系于狱。翌日，将杀之，其夕亡去。刘友人为登封令，其日至县谓令曰：“吾有难，从此逝矣。”遂去，不知所之。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    164

    Yi easily fell asleep but not fully, and in the dark, he saw a deity (or a person, according to Guangji) tending the fire. In the firelight, he recognized his face, and it was the market person they had seen before. Until dawn, he was no longer seen. Later, Yi sought out the market person to ask him, who reported: "One night, I was summoned in a dream to blow fire, which nearly exhausted me, causing lip swelling and breathlessness. I recovered after ten days." Liu Heng was respected by Zhang Quanyi, the Governor of Henan. When dining with Liang Taizu, he thought of fish fillets. Zhang Quanyi said: "I have a guest who can bring it immediately." He then summoned Liu to dig a small pit, fill it with water, and after a while, caught several fish. Liang Taizu became very angry and said: "This is the most absurd thing." He then beat Liu on the back twenty times and imprisoned him in chains. The next day, they were going to kill him, but that night he escaped. Liu's friend was the magistrate of Dengfeng, and when Liu came to the county, he told the magistrate: "I am in trouble, I will leave from here." He then left, and no one knew where he went. (Volume 85 of Guangji)

    ○张武

    　　张武者，始为庐（《广记》有“江道”二字）中一镇副将，颇以拯济行旅为事。尝有老僧过其所，武谓之曰：“师年老，前店尚远，今夕止吾庐中，可乎？”僧忻然。其镇将闻之，怒曰：“今南北交战，间谍如林，知此僧为何人而敢留之也？”僧乃求去，武曰：“吾（《广记》有“业”字）已留师，行日（《广记》作“益”）晚，但宿无苦也。”武室中惟有一床，即以奉其僧，己即席地而寝，盥濯之备皆自具焉。夜数起视之，至五更，僧乃起而叹息，谓武曰：“少年（《广记》有乃字）能如是耶。吾有药赠子，十丸，每正旦吞一丸，可延十年之寿，善自爱。”珍重而去，出门忽不见。武今为常州团练副使，有识者计其年已百岁，常自称七十，轻健如故。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    165

    Zhang Wu

    Zhang Wu was originally a deputy general in a town within a fortress. He often rescued and assisted travelers as his duty. Once, an old monk passed by, and Zhang Wu said to him, "Master, you are old, and the next inn is still far away. Can you stay in my lodge tonight?" The monk was pleased. When the town's general heard of this, he became angry and said, "Now that the north and south are at war, spies are as numerous as trees. How can I know what kind of monk this is and dare to keep him?" The monk then asked to leave, but Zhang Wu said, "I have already kept you, and it will be even later if we wait. Just stay here, there is no hardship." Zhang Wu's room had only one bed, which he gave to the monk, and he slept on the ground himself, preparing all the washing facilities. At night, he got up several times to check on the monk. At dawn, the monk got up and sighed, saying to Zhang Wu, "Can a young man be like this? I have a medicine to give you. Ten pills, take one each New Year's Day, and you can extend your life by ten years. Take good care of yourself." He bid farewell and left, and when he opened the door, he suddenly disappeared. Zhang Wu is now the deputy commander of the local militia in Changzhou. Those who know him estimate that he is already a hundred years old, but he often claims to be seventy, and he is as agile as ever. (From Volume 85 of the Guangji)

    166

    ○茅山道士

    　　茅山道士陈某，壬子岁，游海陵，宿于逆旅，雨雪方甚，有同宿者，身衣单葛，欲与同寝，而嫌其垢弊，乃曰：“雪寒如此，何以过夜？”答曰：“君（毛本无“君”字）但卧，无以见忧。”既皆就寝，陈窃视之，见怀中出三角碎瓦数片，铁条贯之，烧于灯上，俄而火炽，一室皆暖，陈去衣被乃得寝。未明而行，竟不复见也。（《广记》卷八十五无见字）

    　　○逆旅客

    　　大梁逆旅中，有客不知所从来，恒卖皂荚百茎于市，其荚丰大，有异于常者（《广记》无“者”字），日获百钱，辄饮而去。有好事者，知其非常人，乃与同店而宿，及夜穴壁窥之。方见锄（《广记》作“椎”）治床前数尺之地甚熟，既而出皂荚实数枚，种之，少顷即生。时窥之，转复滋长，向晓则已垂实矣，即自采掇，伐去其树，判而焚之，及明携之而去。自是遂出，莫知所之。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    166

    Mount Mao Taoist Priest

    In the year Renzi, Taoist priest Chen from Mount Mao traveled to Hailin and stayed at an inn. It was snowing heavily, and there was a stranger who wore a thin, light garment. He wanted to sleep with Chen but was disliked due to his dirty and worn appearance. The stranger said, "The snow is so cold, how can we spend the night?" Chen replied, "Just lie down, there is no need to be concerned." They both went to bed. Chen secretly watched as the stranger took out several triangular pieces of broken tiles from his chest, strung them together with an iron rod, and burned them on the lamp. Soon, the fire blazed, warming the entire room. Chen removed his clothes and blankets and managed to sleep. Before dawn, the stranger left, and he was never seen again.

    Guest at the Inn in Daliang

    In an inn in Daliang, there was a guest whose origin was unknown. He sold a hundred stems of soapberry daily in the market. The pods were large and abundant, different from the usual ones. He earned a hundred coins a day and then drank and left. Someone interested in unusual things, knowing that the guest was not an ordinary person, stayed in the same inn and slept there. At night, he dug a hole in the wall to spy on the guest. He saw the guest thoroughly tilling the ground in front of the bed. Then, he took out several soapberry seeds, planted them, and they sprouted quickly. By dawn, they were already bearing fruit. The guest picked the fruit, cut down the tree, split it, and burned it. By morning, he had gathered the fruit and left, and no one knew where he went.

    167

    ○教坊乐人子

    　　教坊乐人某，有儿年十余岁，恒病，黄瘦尤甚。忽遇（《广记》有“一”字）道士于路谓之曰：“汝病食症耳，吾能瘳（《广记》作“疗”）之。”因袖中出药数丸，使吞之。既而复视袖中曰：“讶，赚（《广记》“讶赚”作“嘻误”）矣，此辟谷药也，自此当不食，然病亦瘳矣，尔必欲食，常取少木耳食之，吾他日复以食症药遗尔也。”遂去。儿归三（《广记》“三”作“一二”两字）日病愈。然其父母恒以不食为忧，竟逼使饵木耳，遂饮啖（《广记》“饮啖”作“饭啖”）如故矣（《广记》无“矣”字）。已而自悔曰：“我饵仙药而不自知，道士许我后（《广记》作“复”）送药来，会当再见乎？”因白父母，求遍历名山寻访道士，母不许，其父许之曰：“（《广记》有“向”字）使儿病（《广记》无“儿病”二字）不愈，今亦死矣，既志坚如此，或当有分也。”遂遣之，今不知所在。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    167

    A Musician's Son from the Imperial Music Bureau

    A musician from the imperial music bureau had a son who was around ten years old and was always sick, extremely pale and emaciated. One day, he suddenly met a Taoist priest on the road who said to him, "Your son is suffering from a food-related ailment, and I can cure it." The priest then took out several pills from his sleeve and had the boy swallow them. Afterward, the priest looked in his sleeve again and said, "Mistake, mistake! This is a medicine for abstaining from food. From now on, he will not need to eat, but his illness will also be cured. If he wants to eat, he should often consume a little black fungus. I will send him more of this food-related medicine later." The priest then left. The boy returned home three days later and was completely cured. However, his parents were always worried about his not eating, so they forced him to eat black fungus, and he resumed eating and drinking as before. Later, the boy regretted that he had taken the Taoist medicine without knowing it and wondered if the priest would send him more medicine. He told his parents and asked to travel to famous mountains to find the priest. His mother did not agree, but his father said, "If my son had not been cured, he would have died by now. Since he is so determined, perhaps he will find the priest." So he sent him off, and now his whereabouts are unknown.

    ○蒋舜卿

    　　光州检田官蒋舜卿，行山中，见一人方采林檎，以（《广记》作“一”）二枚与之，食，因尔不饥。家人以为得鬼食，不治将病，求医甚切，而不能愈。后闻寿春有人善医，令（《广记》作“乃”）往访之，始行一日，宿一所村（《广记》作“岁”）店，有老父问以所患，具告之，父曰：“吾能救之，无烦远行也。”出药方寸匕，使服之。吐（《广记》作“此”）二林离如新，父收之去。舜卿之（《广记》有“饮”字）食如常。既归，他日（《广记》有“复”字）访之，店与老父俱不见矣。（《广记》卷八十五）

    Explanation

    168

    Jiang Shunqing, the land inspector of Guangzhou, was walking in the mountains when he saw a man picking linli (a type of fruit). The man gave him two pieces, which he ate, and as a result, he did not feel hungry. His family thought he had obtained food from ghosts, and without treatment, he would fall ill, so he sought medical help very earnestly, but could not be cured. Later, he heard that there was someone skilled in medicine in Shouchun, and he then went to visit him. After traveling for one day, he stayed at a village inn. An old man asked about his illness, and he told him in detail. The old man said, "I can save him; there is no need to travel far." He gave him a small amount of medicine and told him to take it. The medicine caused Shunqing to vomit two new linli, and the old man took them away. Shunqing's eating and drinking were as usual. After returning home, on another day, he visited the place again, but the inn and the old man were both gone.

    169

    ○卢延贵

    　　卢延贵者，为宣州安仁场官，赴职，中途阻风，泊舟（《广记》作“大”）江次。数日，因登岸，闲步不觉行远，遥窥（《广记》作“望”）大树下，若有屋室，稍近，见室中一物若人若兽，见人即行起而来逐（《广记》无“逐”字）。延贵惧而却走，此物连呼“无惧，吾乃人也。”即往就之，状貌奇怪（《广记》作“伟”），裸袒而通身有毛长数寸，自言：“我（《广记》无“我”字）商贾也，顷岁漂（《广记》作“泛”）舟至此遇风，举家没溺而身独得就岸，数日食草根，饮涧水，因得不死，岁余身乃生毛，自尔（《广记》有“乃”字）不饮不食，自伤孤独，无复世念，结庐于此千（《广记》“千”字作“已十二”字）余年矣。

    Explanation

    169

    Lu Yan Gui, an official in charge of the Anren salt field in Xuanchou, was on his way to take up his post when he was delayed by strong winds and had to anchor his boat at the riverbank. After several days, he went ashore to walk leisurely and, without realizing it, walked far away. From a distance, he saw a large tree under which there seemed to be a house. As he approached, he saw a creature inside the house that looked like a person or an animal. When the creature saw him, it stood up and came towards him. Lu Yan Gui was afraid and ran away, but the creature called out, "Do not be afraid, I am a person." Lu Yan Gui returned and approached the creature, which had a strange appearance and was naked, with long hair covering its body. The creature said, "I am a merchant. Last year, I was sailing a boat here when a storm hit, and my entire family drowned, but I alone managed to reach the shore. For several days, I ate grass roots and drank stream water, and thus survived. After more than a year, my body began to grow hair, and since then, I have not eaten or drunk anything. I feel lonely and have no worldly concerns left. I have lived here in a hut for over a thousand years."

    ”因问独居于此，得无虎豹之害（《广记》有“乎”字），答曰：“吾已能腾空上下，虎豹无奈何也。”延贵留久之，又问“有所需乎？”对曰：“亦有之，每浴于溪中，恒患身不速乾，得数尺布为巾，乃佳也。又得一（《广记》无“一”字）小刀以掘药物，益善。君能致之耶？”延贵延之过（《广记》作“至”）船，固不肯，乃送巾与刀而去。罢任复寻之，遂□（《广记》作“迷”）失路，后复（《广记》作“无”）有遇之者。（《广记》卷八十六）

    　　○杜鲁宾

    　　建康人杜鲁宾，以卖药为事。尝有客自称豫章人，恒来市药，未尝还直，鲁宾善待之。一日复至，市药甚多，曰：“吾欠君药钱多矣，今更从君求此，吾将还西天（毛本作“大”）市版木，比（三字毛本作“服术此”）及再求，足以并酬君矣。”杜许之。既去，久之乃还，赠杜山木棒十条，委之而去，莫知所之。杜得之不以介意，转遗（《广记》作“移”）亲友。
