    170

    A Man with Supernatural Abilities

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a man named Du Lubin from Jiankang was known for selling medicine. One day, he asked if the person living alone there was in danger from tigers and leopards. The person replied, "I can already fly up and down, and tigers and leopards cannot do anything to me." Du Lubin stayed with him for a long time and then asked, "Do you have anything you need?" The person replied, "Yes, every time I bathe in the stream, I always worry that my body does not dry quickly. If I could get several feet of cloth to make a towel, it would be good. If I could also get a small knife to dig up herbs, it would be even better. Can you bring them to me?" Du Lubin invited him to cross the boat, but he firmly refused. So, Du Lubin sent the towel and knife and left. After leaving office, Du Lubin went back to look for him, but he then got lost. Later, someone else met him.

    ○ Du Lubin

    Du Lubin from Jiankang made a living by selling medicine. Once, a guest who claimed to be from Yuanchang came to buy medicine frequently without ever paying. Du Lubin treated him well. One day, the guest came again and bought a lot of medicine, saying, "I owe you a lot of money for the medicine. Now, I will ask you for more, as I am going back to Western Heaven (or 'Great') to buy books and texts. By the time I come back to ask again, I will have enough to pay you back." Du Lubin agreed. The guest left, and after a long time, he returned, giving Du Lubin ten pieces of mountain wood, left them, and disappeared without a trace. Du Lubin did not take it seriously and passed the wood on to his friends and relatives.

    171

    所存三条，偶命工人剖之，其中得小铁杵二具焉（《广记》“杵”下有“臼”字，“二”作“一”，“焉”作“高”），可五六寸，旧（《广记》作“臼”）有八（《广记》作“入”）足，间作兽头，制作精巧，不类人力，杜亦凡人，不知所用，竟为人取去，今失所在。杜又尝（《广记》作“常”）治舍，有卖土者，自言金坛县人，来往甚数，杜亦厚资给之。治舍毕，卖土者将去，留方寸之土曰：“以此为别。”遂去不复来。其土坚致，有异于常，杜置药肆中，不以为贵。数年，杜之居为火所焚，屋壤土裂（毛本脱“裂”字），视之有小赤蛇在其隙中，剖之，蛇萦绕一白石龟，大可三二寸，蛇去而龟尚（《广记》无“而”字“尚”字）存，至今宝藏于杜氏。（《广记》卷八十六）

    Explanation

    171

    There were three items that were kept. Once, Du, an ordinary person, had them cut open, and two small iron pestles were found. They were about five or six inches long, originally had eight feet, and sometimes had animal heads. They were exquisitely crafted and did not resemble human effort. Du, being an ordinary person, did not know what they were used for, and ultimately, they were taken by someone. Now, they are lost and unknown.

    Du also renovated his house, and there was a seller of soil who claimed to be from Jintan County. He visited frequently, and Du generously provided him with funds. After the house was completed, the seller was about to leave, and he left a small amount of soil as a parting gift. Then he left and never returned. The soil was hard and dense, different from the usual, and Du placed it in his pharmacy, not considering it valuable.

    Several years later, Du's residence was burned down by fire, and the walls and soil cracked. Upon inspection, a small red snake was found in the crack. Cutting it open, the snake was found coiled around a white stone turtle. The snake left, but the turtle remained, and until now, it is treasured by the Du family.

    ○建州狂僧

    　　建州有僧，不知其名，常如狂人，其所言动，多有微验。邵武县前临溪有大磐石，去水犹百步，一日忽以墨画其石之半，因坐石上，为（《广记》“为”在“竿”下）持竿钓鱼之状。明日山水大发，适（毛本作“遇”）至其墨画而退。癸卯岁，尽砍（《广记》作“斫”）去临路树枝之向南者，人问之，曰：“免碍旗幡。”又曰：“要归一边。”及吴师之入，皆行其下。又城外僧寺，大署其壁，某等若干人处书之。及军至城下，分据僧寺，以为栅，所安置人数亦（《广记》作“一”）无所差。其僧竟为军士所杀。初王氏之季，闽建多难，民不聊生，或问狂僧曰：“待（《广记》“待”字作“时世”二字）何时当安？”答曰：“侬去即安矣。”及其既死，闽岭竟平，皆如其言。（《广记》卷八十六）

    Explanation

    172

    The Crazy Monk of Jianzhou

    There was a monk in Jianzhou, whose name is unknown. He often behaved like a madman, and many of his words and actions proved to be slightly accurate. In front of Shaowu County, there was a large boulder by a stream, about a hundred steps away from the water. One day, he suddenly drew half of the rock with ink and sat on it, adopting the posture of holding a fishing rod to fish. The next day, a sudden flood came, just as it reached the spot where he had drawn the ink, and then receded. In the year of Gui Mao, he cut down all the branches facing south along the road. When asked why, he said, "To avoid obstructing flags and banners." He also said, "To return to one side." When the Wu forces entered, they all moved along the path he had marked. At a temple outside the city, he made large inscriptions on the wall, writing the names and numbers of certain people. When the army arrived at the city, they divided and occupied the temple, using it as a fort, and the number of people they stationed there was exactly as he had predicted. The monk was eventually killed by the soldiers. In the later years of the Wang family, Fujian and Jianzhou were in turmoil, and the people were suffering greatly. Someone asked the crazy monk, "When will it be peaceful?" He replied, "When I leave, it will be peaceful." And indeed, after his death, Fujian and the mountains were eventually pacified, all as he had said. (From Volume 86 of the Taiping Guangji)

    ●补遗

    　　○李汉雄

    　　李汉雄者，尝为钦州刺史，罢郡居池州，善风角推步之奇术，自言当以兵死。天祐丙子岁，游浙西，始入府而叹曰：“府中气候甚恶，当有兵乱，期不远矣，吾必速回。”既见，府公厚待之，留旬日，未得遽去。一日晚出逆旅，四顾而叹曰：“祸在明日，吾不可留。”翌日晨入府辞，坐客位中，良久曰：“祸即今至，速出犹或可。”遂出至府门，遇军将周交作乱，遂遇杀害于门下。（《广记》卷八十）

    Supplementary Entries

    Li Hanxiong

    Li Hanxiong, a former governor of Qinzhou, later settled in Chizhou. He was skilled in the esoteric arts of wind divination and astronomical calculations, and he claimed that he would die by military means. In the Tianyou era of the Later Liang dynasty (904 AD), he traveled to the western part of Zhejiang province. Upon entering the government office, he sighed and said, "The atmosphere in the government office is very bad; there will be a military uprising, and it is not far off. I must leave quickly."

    When he met the governor, he was treated generously and stayed for ten days, unable to leave immediately. One evening, as he was about to leave the inn, he looked around and sighed, saying, "Disaster is tomorrow; I cannot stay." The next morning, he entered the government office to bid farewell and sat in the guest seat for a long time before saying, "Disaster has arrived; leave quickly and perhaps you can escape." He then left and reached the gate of the government office, where he encountered a military officer named Zhou Jiao who started a rebellion. He was subsequently killed at the gate.

    (From Guangji volume 80)

    ○高安村小儿

    　　高安村人，有小儿作田中，为人所杀，不获其贼。至明年死日，家人为设斋。尔日有里中儿，方见其一小儿谓之曰：“我某家死儿也，今日家人设斋，吾与而同往食乎？”里中儿即随之至其家，共坐灵床，食至辄餐，家人不见也。久之，其舅后至，望灵床而哭，儿即迳指之曰：“此人杀我者也，吾恶见之。”遂去。儿既去，而家人见里中儿坐灵床上，皆大惊，问其故，儿具言之，且言其舅杀之，因执以送官，遂伏罪。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Explanation

    174

    A Child from Gao'an Village

    In Gao'an Village, there was a young boy who was working in the fields when he was killed by someone, and the murderer was not caught. On the same day the following year, the boy's family set up a vegetarian meal in his memory. On that day, a child from the village saw a little boy who said to him, "I am the dead child from a certain family. Today, my family is setting up a vegetarian meal, and I will go with you to eat." The child from the village then followed him to the boy's home, where they sat together on the spirit bed. When the food arrived, they ate immediately, but the family did not see them. After some time, the boy's uncle arrived later, looked at the spirit bed, and began to cry. The child immediately pointed to him and said, "This person killed me, and I hate seeing him." The ghost then left. After the child left, the family saw the child from the village sitting on the spirit bed, and they were all very surprised. They asked why, and the child explained everything, stating that the uncle had killed him. The family then took the uncle to the authorities, and he confessed his crime. (From Guangji, Volume 124)

    ○陈勋

    　　建阳县录事陈勋，性刚狷不容物。为县吏，十人共诬其罪，竟坐弃市。至明年死日，家为设斋，妻哭毕，独叹于灵前曰：“君平生以刚直称，今枉死，逾年精魂何寂然耶？”是夕即梦勋曰：“吾都不知死，向闻□□□□卿言，方大悟尔，若尔，吾当报仇，然公署非可卒入者，卿明日为我入县诉枉。吾当随之。”明日妻如言而往，出门即见勋仗剑从之，至县遇一雠吏于桥上，勋以剑击其首，吏即颠仆而死。既入门，勋径之曹署，以次击之，中者皆死，十杀其八，二吏奔至临川，乃得免。勋家在盖竹乡，人恒见之，因为立祠，号陈府君庙，至今传其灵。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    175

    Chen Xun

    Chen Xun, a county official in Jianyang, was known for his stubborn and intolerant nature. As a county clerk, he was falsely accused by ten people, and despite his innocence, he was executed publicly by beheading. On the anniversary of his death, his family held a memorial service. After the wife wept, she sighed before the spirit tablet, saying, "You were always known for your integrity and righteousness. Now that you have died unjustly, why is your spirit so silent?" That night, she dreamed that Chen Xun appeared and said, "I did not know I was dead. Just now, I heard your words and suddenly realized it. If that is the case, I will seek revenge. However, the government office is not a place where one can easily enter. You should go to the county tomorrow and file a complaint on my behalf. I will follow you."

    The next day, the wife went to the county as instructed. As soon as she left the house, she saw Chen Xun with a sword following her. When they reached the bridge, they encountered one of the officials who had wronged him. Chen Xun struck him down with his sword, and the official fell dead. Upon entering the county, Chen Xun proceeded to the office and killed the others in turn, killing eight out of the ten. Two officials managed to escape to Linchuan and thus avoided being killed.

    Chen Xun's home was in Gai Zhu Village. People often saw him, and they established a shrine in his honor, calling it the Temple of Lord Chen. To this day, it is said that the shrine has miraculous powers. (From Yiwen Leiju, Volume 124)

    ○钟遵

    　　江南大理评事钟遵，南平王传之孙也，历任贪浊。水部员外郎孙岳素知其事，密纵于权要，竟坐下狱。会赦除名，遵既以事在赦前，又其祖尝赐铁券，恕子孙二死，因复诣阙自理，事下所司，大理奏赃状明白，遂弃市。临刑，或与之酒，遵不饮，曰：“吾当讼于地下，不可令醉也。”遵死月余，岳方与客坐，有小青蛇出于栋间，岳视之惊起曰：“钟评事，钟评事。”变色而入，遂病，翌日死。（《广记》卷一百二十四）

    Zhong Zun

    Zhong Zun, a Censor of the Dali Temple in the Jiangnan region, was the grandson of the Prince of Nanping. He held multiple positions marked by corruption and impropriety. Sun Yue, the Assistant of the Water Department, had always known about his misconduct and secretly influenced powerful officials, eventually leading to Zhong Zun's imprisonment. Coinciding with a pardon, he was removed from his official record. Since the matter occurred before the pardon, and his ancestor had once been granted an iron edict that forgave two deaths for his descendants, Zhong Zun went to the imperial court to clear himself. The matter was handed over to the relevant authorities, and the Dali Temple reported that the charges of embezzlement were clear. Consequently, he was executed publicly. At the time of execution, someone offered him wine, but Zhong Zun refused, saying, "I will appeal to the underworld, I cannot allow myself to be drunk." About a month after Zhong Zun's death, Sun Yue was sitting with guests when a small green snake emerged from between the rafters. Sun Yue looked at it in shock and exclaimed, "Zhong the Censor, Zhong the Censor." He changed color and entered, then fell ill and died the next day. (From The Extensive Records, Volume 124)

    ○鲁思郾女

    　　内臣鲁思郾，女生拾七年，一日临镜将妆，镜中忽见一妇人，披发徒跣，抱一婴儿，回顾则在其后，因恐惧顿仆，久之乃苏。自是日日恒见，积久，其家人皆见之。思郾自问其故，答曰：“己扬子县里民之女，往岁建昌录事某以事至扬子，因聘己为侧室，君女即其正妻，岁余生此子，后录事出旁县君女因投己于井，并此子，以石填之，诈其夫云“逃去”我方讼于所司，适会君女卒。今虽后身，固当偿命也。”思郾使人驰至建昌验事，其录事老犹在，如言发井，果得骸骨。其家多方以禳之，皆不可。其女后嫁褚氏，厉愈甚，旦夕惊悸，以至于卒。（《广记》卷一百三十）

    Explanation

    ○The Daughter of Lu Siyan

    The eunuch Lu Siyan, whose daughter was born in the 17th year of a certain reign period, one day stood in front of the mirror about to put on makeup when she suddenly saw a woman with disheveled hair, barefoot, and holding a baby. When she turned back, the woman was behind her. Filled with fear, she collapsed and remained unconscious for a long time before regaining consciousness. From then on, she saw the apparition every day consistently, and over time, all her family members also saw it. Lu Siyan asked herself why this was happening, and the apparition replied, "I am a commoner's daughter from Yangzi County. Last year, a certain magistrate from Jianchang came to Yangzi for official business and engaged me as a concubine. Your daughter is his main wife. After a year, I gave birth to this child. Later, the magistrate sent your daughter to another county and had me and this child thrown into a well and covered with stones. He lied to his husband, saying I had fled. I was just about to sue the authorities, but just then, your daughter died. Now that I have been reborn, I must repay the debt of life." Lu Siyan sent someone to Jianchang to verify the facts. The magistrate is still alive. As said, they dug up the well and found the bones. Her family tried many ways to ward off the spirit, but none worked. Her daughter later married a man surnamed Chu, and the haunting became even worse. She was terrified day and night until she died.

    ○袁弘御

    　　后唐袁弘御为云中从事，尤精算术。同府令算庭下桐树叶数，即自起量树，去地七尺围之，取围径之数布算，良久曰若干叶，众不能覆，命撼去二十二叶，复使算，曰：“已少向者二十一叶矣。”审视之，两叶差小，止当一叶耳。节度使张敬达有二玉碗，弘御量其广深，算之曰：“此碗明年五月十六日已时当破。”敬达闻之曰：“吾敬藏之，能破否？”即命贮大笼，籍以衣絮缫之库中。至期，库屋梁折，正压其笼，二碗俱碎。太仆少卿薛文美同府亲见。（《广记》卷二百十五）

    Explanation

    178

    ○Yuan Hongyu's Mastery of Mathematics

    Yuan Hongyu, a subordinate official in Yunzhong during the Later Tang dynasty, was especially skilled in mathematics. The same office ordered him to calculate the number of leaves on the paulownia tree in the courtyard. He immediately got up to measure the tree, measuring seven feet from the ground around it. He took the circumference and diameter measurements and set them out for calculation. After a long time, he said there were so many leaves. Everyone could not verify it. He was then ordered to shake off twenty-two leaves, and he calculated again, saying, "There are twenty-one leaves fewer than before." Upon careful examination, two leaves were slightly smaller and only counted as one leaf.

    Jiangang, the Military Governor of Zhang Jingda, had two jade bowls. Yuan Hongyu measured their width and depth and calculated, saying, "These bowls will break on the 16th day of the fifth month next year at noon." Jingda heard and said, "I will carefully store them. Can they still break?" He immediately ordered them to be stored in a large cage, wrapped in clothes and silk, and stored in the warehouse. On that day, the beam of the warehouse collapsed, exactly pressing the cage, and the two bowls both broke. The Imperial Steward Xiao Wenmei, who was also in the same office, personally witnessed it.

    This translation aims to be faithful to the original text while maintaining a natural flow in English. It addresses the idiomatic expressions, cultural allusions, syntactic ambiguities, and proper nouns as planned during the pre-drafting research phase.

    ○蒯亮

    　　处士蒯亮，言其所知额角患瘤，医为割之，得一黑石棋子，巨斧击之，终不伤缺。复有足胫生瘤者，因至亲家，为■〈犭制〉犬所齰，正啮其瘤，其中得针百余枚，皆可用，疾亦愈。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    　　○张易

    　　江南刑部郎中张易，少居菑川，病热困惙且甚，恍惚见一神人，长可数寸，立于枕前，持药三丸曰：“吞此可愈。”易受而亟吞之，二丸谦之，一丸落席有声，因自起求之，不得。家人惊问何为，具述所见，病因即愈，尔日出入里巷，了无所苦。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    179

    Final Translation

    ○蒯亮

    There was a recluse named Kuai Liang, who recounted that he knew a person who had a tumor on his forehead. The doctor cut it out and found a black stone chess piece inside. When struck with a large axe, it did not break. Another person had a tumor on his leg. He went to a relative's house and was bitten by a ■〈犭制〉 dog, which bit precisely on the tumor, revealing over a hundred needles inside, all of which were usable, and the illness was cured.

    ○张易

    Zhang Yi, a mid-level official in the Ministry of Justice in southern China, lived in Zichuan when he was young. He suffered from a severe fever and was exhausted. In a daze, he saw a divine figure, about several inches tall, standing beside his pillow, holding three pills and saying, "Swallow these to be cured." Zhang Yi took them and quickly swallowed them. Two of the pills were swallowed, but one fell onto the mat with a sound. He got up to look for it but could not find it. His family members asked in surprise what was happening. He described what he had seen, and the cause of his illness was immediately cured. That day, he went in and out of the neighborhood without any discomfort.

    180

    ○广陵木工

    　　广陵有木工，因病，手足皆拳缩，不能复执斤斧。扶踊行乞，至后土庙前，遇一道士，长而黑色，神采甚异，呼问其疾，因与药数丸曰：“饵此当愈，旦日平明复会于此。”木工辞曰：“某不能行，家去此远，明日虽晚尚未能至也。”道士曰：“尔无忧，但早至此。”遂别去。木工既归，饵其药，顷之，手足痛甚，中夜乃止，因即得寐，五更而寤，觉手足甚轻，因下床，趋走如故，即驰诣后土庙前，久之乃见道士倚杖而立，再拜陈谢，道士曰：“吾授尔方，可救人疾苦，无为木匠耳。”遂再拜受之，因问其名居，曰：“吾在紫极宫，有事可访吾也。”遂去。木匠得方，用以治疾，无不愈者。至紫极宫访之，竟不复见。后有妇人久疾，亦遇一道士与药而差，言其容貌，亦木工所见也。广陵寻乱，木工竟不知所之。（《广记》卷二百二十）

    Explanation

    180

    The Carpenter of Guangling

    In the city of Guangling, there was a carpenter who fell ill. His hands and feet became so contracted that he could no longer hold his axe and saw. He began to beg, hopping along with crutches, and eventually arrived at the front of the Hou Tu Temple. There, he met a Taoist priest who was tall and dark-skinned, with an extraordinary appearance. The priest called out and asked about the carpenter's illness, then gave him several pills and said, "Eat these and you will recover. Meet me here again at dawn tomorrow."

    The carpenter replied, "I cannot walk. My home is far from here. Even if I leave early tomorrow, I still won't be able to arrive in time." The priest reassured him, saying, "Do not worry. Just come here early." Then he left.

    After returning home, the carpenter took the medicine. After a short while, his hands and feet became very painful, and the pain subsided at midnight. He then fell asleep and woke up at the fifth watch of the night, feeling his hands and feet were very light. He got out of bed and walked as before. He rushed to the front of the Hou Tu Temple, and after a long time, he saw the Taoist priest standing with a staff. He bowed twice and thanked him. The priest said, "I will teach you a formula that can relieve people's suffering, but not just for carpentry." The carpenter bowed twice again and accepted it. He then asked for the priest's name and address, and the priest replied, "I am at the Zǐjí Palace. If you have any business, you can visit me." Then he left.

    The carpenter obtained the formula and used it to treat illnesses. No one failed to recover. He went to the Zǐjí Palace to visit the priest, but he never saw him again. Later, a woman who had been ill for a long time also met a Taoist priest who gave her medicine and she recovered. She described the priest's appearance, and it was the same as what the carpenter had seen. Guangling soon fell into chaos, and the carpenter eventually disappeared without a trace.

    181

    ○郭厚

    　　李宗为舒州刺史，重造开元寺，工徒始集，将浚一废井，井中（下有脱）如言而得之，船屋上有脯腊，妇人取以食。四卒视其手（下有脱）。王寇犯阙，天下乱，僧辈利吾行资，杀我投此井中，今骸骨在是，为我白李公，幸葬我，无见弃也。主者以告宗，翌日观至井上，使发之，果得骸骨，即为具衣衾棺椁，设祭而葬之。葬日，伍伯复仆地鬼语曰：“为我谢李公，幽魂处此已三十年，藉公之惠，今九州社令已补我为土地之神，配食于此矣。”寺中至今祀之。（《广记》卷三百十四）

    Explanation

    181

    De Guo Hou

    Li Zong, the governor of Shuzhou, rebuilt Kaiyuan Temple. As the workers began to gather, they were about to dredge an abandoned well. In the well, they found (a part of the text is missing) as they had been told. On a boat-shaped structure above the well, there were meat and dried meat. A woman took some to eat. Four soldiers looked at her hands (a part of the text is missing). During a time when rebellious forces attacked the imperial palace and the world was in chaos, the monks coveted our travel funds, killed us, and threw us into this well. Now, the bones are here. Tell Master Li on my behalf, bury me, do not abandon me. The supervisor reported this to Li Zong. The next day, they went to the well, ordered it to be opened, and indeed found the bones. They immediately prepared shrouds and coffins, held a ceremony, and buried them. On the day of the burial, the five officials fell to the ground and spoke in ghostly voices, saying, "Thank Master Li on my behalf. My spirit has been here for thirty years, thanks to your kindness. Now, the land deity has appointed me as a local god, and I am now worshipped here." The temple continues to worship me to this day. (From Guangji, Volume 314)

    182

    ○彭虎子

    　　彭虎子少壮有膂力，常谓无鬼神。母死，俗巫诫之云：“某日殃煞当还，重有所杀，宜出避之。”合家细弱悉出逃隐，虎子独留不去，夜中有人排门入，至东西屋，觅人不得，次入屋向庐室中。虎子遑遽无计，床头先有一瓮，便入其中，以板盖头，觉母在板上，有人问：“板下无人耶？”母云：“无。”相率而去。（《广记》卷三百十八。按：今人李剑国考证明钞本《广记》注出《幽明录》当从之）

    Explanation

    182

    彭虎子年轻力壮，常说自己不信有鬼神。母亲去世后，一个普通的巫婆警告他说：“某天恶煞会回来，可能会再杀人，应该出去躲避。”全家老小都逃走了，只有彭虎子留下来没有走。夜里有人破门而入，搜查东屋西屋，没有找到人，接着进入主屋。彭虎子惊慌失措，无计可施，床头先有一个瓮，他就钻了进去，用木板盖住头。他感觉到母亲也在木板上，有人问道：“板下没人吗？”母亲回答：“没有。”于是他们就离开了。（《广记》卷三百十八。按：今人李剑国考证认为钞本《广记》注出《幽明录》应从之）

    ○马举

    　　马举尝为山南步奏官，问道入蜀，时兵后，僻路绝无人烟。夜至一馆，闻东廊下有人语声，因往告之，有应者云：“中堂有床，自往宿去。”举至中堂，唯有上榻，求火，答云：“无火。”求席，隔屋掷出一席，可重十余斤。举亦壮士，殊不介意。中夜，有一物如猴，升榻而来，举以铁椎急击之，叫呼而走。及明告别，其人怒去，更云：“夜来见伊独处，令儿子往伴，打得几死。”举推其门不可开，自隙窥之，积壤而已。举后为太原大将，官至淮南节度使。（《广记》卷三百六十六）

    Explanation

    183

    Ma Ju, once a steppe official in the southern region, traveled to Shu (Sichuan) after a war, on a remote path with no human habitation. One night, he arrived at an inn and heard voices coming from under the eastern veranda. He went to inquire and was told, "There is a bed in the central hall; go there to rest." Upon entering the central hall, he found only a bed. He asked for fire, and was told, "There is no fire." He requested a mat, and one was thrown through the wall, weighing over ten pounds. Being a strong man, he took no notice. In the middle of the night, an animal resembling a monkey climbed onto the bed. Ma Ju struck it sharply with an iron mallet, and it cried out and ran away. The next morning, as he was leaving, the innkeeper became angry and said, "Last night I saw him alone, so I sent my son to keep him company, and he nearly killed him." Ma Ju pushed the door but it would not open. Looking through a crack, he saw only a pile of earth. Later, Ma Ju became a general in Taiyuan and rose to the position of governor of Huainan. (From Guangji, Volume 366)

    184

    ○陈龟范

    　　陈龟范，明州人，客游广陵，因事赞善马潜。一夕暴卒，至一府署，有府官视牒曰：“吾追陈龟谋，何故追龟范耶？”范对曰：“范本名龟谋，近事马赞善，马公讳言，故改一字耳。”府公乃曰：“取明州簿来。”顷之，一吏持簿至，视之乃龟谋也。因引至曹署，吏云：“有人讼君已引退矣，君当得还也。”龟范因自言：“平生多难，贫苦备至，人生固当死，今已至此，不愿还也。”吏固遣之，又曰：“若是，愿知将来穷达之事。”吏因为检簿曰：“君他日甚善，虽不至富贵，然职禄无阙。”又问寿几何，曰：“此固不可言也。”又问卒于何处，曰：“不在扬州，不在鄂州。”送还家，寤后潜历典二郡，甚见委用。潜卒，归于扬州，奉使鄂州，既还，卒于彭泽。（《广记》卷三百八十五）

    Explanation

    184

    Tian Gui Fan, a man from Mingzhou, was a guest in Guangling, where he became involved with Zan Shang Ma Qian. One night, he suddenly died and found himself in a government office. A government official looked at a document and said, "I am chasing after Chen Guimou, why am I chasing after Guifan instead?" Tian replied, "My original name was Guimou. Recently, I have been involved with Zan Shang Ma Qian, whose name is taboo, so I changed one character." The official then said, "Fetch the register of Mingzhou." Soon, a clerk brought the register, and upon checking, it was indeed Guimou. The clerk then led him to the office, saying, "Someone has accused you of resigning, so you should be allowed to return." Tian then spoke for himself, "My life has been full of difficulties, and I have suffered greatly from poverty. Death is inevitable, and now that I am here, I do not wish to return." The clerk insisted on sending him back, and Tian asked, "If so, I wish to know about my future prospects of poverty or prosperity." The clerk then checked the register and said, "You will be very fortunate in the future, though you may not reach great wealth, but you will have a stable position and salary." Tian then asked about his lifespan, and the clerk said, "This cannot be said." Tian also asked where he would die, and the clerk replied, "Not in Yangzhou, not in Ezhou." He was then sent back home. After waking up, Ma Qian served as governor of two prefectures and was highly trusted and employed. After Ma Qian's death, Tian returned to Yangzhou, was sent on a mission to Ezhou, and after returning, died in Pengze. (From the Yanyi)

    ○马思道

    　　洪州医博士马思道，病笃，忽自欢曰：“吾平生不省为恶，何故乃为女子？今在条子坊，朱氏妇所托生矣。”其子试寻之，其家妇果娠，乃作襁褓以候之，及思道卒，而朱氏生实女子也。（《广记》卷三百八十八）

    　　○海陵夏氏

    　　戊戌岁（案：戊戌，晋天福三年，南唐升元二年），城海陵县为郡，侵人冢墓。有市侩夏氏，其先尝为盐商，墓在城西，夏改葬其祖，百一十年矣，开棺唯有白骨，而衣服器物皆俨然如新，无所损污，有红锦被，文彩尤异，夏方贫，皆取卖之，人竞以善价买去。其余冢虽历年未及而皆腐败矣。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    Explanation

    185

    马思道

    洪州医博士马思道，病笃，忽自欢曰：“吾平生不省为恶，何故乃为女子？今在条子坊，朱氏妇所托生矣。”其子试寻之，其家妇果娠，乃作襁褓以候之，及思道卒，而朱氏生实女子也。

    Translation:
    Ma Sidao, a medical doctor in Hongzhou, was seriously ill. Suddenly, he spoke cheerfully, saying, "I have never done any evil in my life. Why should I be reborn as a woman? Now I am being reborn as a woman named Zhu in the Tiaozifang area." His son tried to find out about it. The woman in the Zhu family indeed became pregnant, and they prepared a cradle to wait for her. When Ma Sidao died, the Zhu family indeed gave birth to a girl.

    海陵夏氏

    戊戌岁，城海陵县为郡，侵人冢墓。有市侩夏氏，其先尝为盐商，墓在城西，夏改葬其祖，百一十年矣，开棺唯有白骨，而衣服器物皆俨然如新，无所损污，有红锦被，文彩尤异，夏方贫，皆取卖之，人竞以善价买去。其余冢虽历年未及而皆腐败矣。

    Translation:
    In the year戊戌 (938 CE), the city of Haiting was made into a prefecture, and it disturbed people's tombs. There was a merchant named Xia, whose ancestors used to be salt merchants. His tomb was located in the western part of the city. Xia had his ancestor's remains reburied, which had been there for 110 years. When the coffin was opened, there were only bones, but the clothes and objects were still as good as new, without any damage or dirt. There was a red brocade blanket, its patterns were especially beautiful. Xia was poor, so he sold them all, and people competed to buy them at high prices. The other tombs, though not as old, were all rotten.

    Final Translation

    ○庐陵彭氏

    　　庐陵人彭氏，葬其父，有术士为卜地曰：“葬此当世为藩牧郡守。”彭从之。又掘坎，术士曰：“深无过九尺。”久之，术士暂憩他所，役者遂掘丈余，欻有白鹤自地出，飞入云中。术士叹恨而去。今彭氏子孙有为县令者。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    　　○武夷山

    　　建州武夷山，或风雨之夕，闻人马箫管之声，及明，则有棺椁在悬崖之上，中有胫骨一节，土人谓之仙人换骨函。近代有人深入绝壑，俯见一函，其上题云“润州朝京门内染师张某第三女”，好事者记之。后至润州，果得张氏之居，云第三女，未嫁而卒，已数岁。因发其墓，则空棺矣。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    Explanation

    186

    ○庐陵彭氏

    The Peng family from Luxi buried their father, and a fortune-teller chose a burial site, saying, "Burying here will make you a governor of a border region, a provincial governor, or a county magistrate." The Peng family followed his advice. They then dug a grave, and the fortune-teller instructed, "The depth should not exceed nine feet." After some time, the fortune-teller took a temporary rest elsewhere, and the workers dug more than ten feet. Suddenly, a white crane emerged from the ground and flew into the clouds. The fortune-teller regretted his mistake and left. Now, some descendants of the Peng family have become county magistrates.

    ○武夷山

    In Wuyi Mountain, during stormy nights, people sometimes hear the sounds of people and horses playing musical instruments. By morning, there is a coffin on a cliff, containing only one leg bone. Locals call this a "casket of the immortal transformed." In modern times, someone ventured into a deep ravine and saw a coffin with an inscription reading, "The third daughter of Zhang, a dyeing master living inside the Chaojing Gate of Runzhou." Those interested in such things recorded this. Later, they found the residence of the Zhang family in Runzhou, confirming that the third daughter had died unmarried several years ago. When they opened her tomb, it was empty.

    187

    ○林赞尧

    　　丙午岁（案：丙午晋开运三年，南唐保大四年），漳州裨将林赞尧杀监军中使，据郡及保山岩以为营，掘地得一古冢，棺椁皆腐，中有一女子，衣服容貌皆如生，举体犹有暖气。军士取其金银钗而弃其尸。又发一冢，开棺见一人被发覆面，蹲于棺中，军士骇惧，致死者数人。赞尧竟伏诛。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    　　○张绍军卒

    　　丙午岁（案：丙午当南唐保大四年），江南之师围留安，军政不肃，军士发掘冢墓以取财物，诸将莫禁。监军使张匡绍所将卒二人，发城南一冢，得一椰实柸以献匡绍，因曰：“某发此冢，开棺见绿衣人面如生，惧不敢犯，墓中无他珍，唯得此枉耳。”既还营而绿衣人已坐某房矣，一日数见，意甚恶之。居一二日，二卒皆战死。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    Explanation

    187

    ○林赞尧

    In the year of Bingwu (which corresponds to the third year of the Kaiyuan era in the Later Jin dynasty and the fourth year of the Baodao era in the Southern Tang dynasty), Lin Zanyao, a subordinate general in Zhangzhou, killed the imperial envoy stationed in the military, took control of the prefecture and the Baoshan rock as a base, and while digging up an ancient tomb, found a coffin and casket that were both rotten. Inside was a woman whose clothes and appearance were as if she were still alive, and her entire body still had warmth. The soldiers took her gold and silver jewelry and discarded her body. They then opened another tomb, where they found a person with their face covered by hair, crouching inside the coffin. The soldiers were so frightened that several of them died. Lin Zanyao was eventually executed. (From The Collection of Wide Records, Volume 390)

    ○张绍军卒

    In the year of Bingwu (which corresponds to the fourth year of the Baodao era in the Southern Tang dynasty), the Southern Tang forces surrounded Liu'an. Military discipline was lax, and the soldiers were digging up tombs to steal valuables, with no officers stopping them. Two soldiers under the command of Zhang Kuangshao, the military supervisor, opened a tomb in the southern part of the city and found a coconut cup, which they presented to Zhang Kuangshao. One of the soldiers said, “I opened this tomb and saw a green-clad figure with a living-like face. I was too afraid to disturb it. The tomb contained no other valuables, only this coconut cup.” After returning to camp, the green-clad figure appeared in his room and was seen several times a day, which the soldier found very disturbing. After a few days, both soldiers died in battle. (From The Collection of Wide Records, Volume 390)

    188

    ○马黄谷冢

    　　安州城南马黄谷冢，左有大冢，棺椁已腐，唯一骷髅，长三尺，陈人左鹏亲见之焉。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    　　○秦进崇

    　　周显德乙卯岁，伪涟水军使泰进崇修城，发一古冢，棺椁皆腐，得古钱、破铜镜数枚，复得一瓶，中更有一瓶，黄质黑文，隶字云“一双青鸟子，飞来五两头。借问船轻重，寄信到扬州。”其明年，周师伐吴，进崇死之。（《广记》卷三百九十）

    　　○陈褒

    　　清源人陈褒，隐居别业，临窗夜坐，窗外即广野，忽闻有人马声，视之，见一妇人骑虎自窗下过，径入西屋内。壁下先有一婢卧，妇人即取细竹枝从壁隙中刺之，婢忽尔腹痛，开户去如厕。褒方愕骇，未及言，婢已出，即为虎所搏，遽前救之，仅免。乡人云村中恒有此怪，所谓虎鬼者也。（《广记》卷四百三十二）

    Explanation

    188

    ○马黄谷冢

    In the southern part of Anzhou City, there is a tomb in Ma Huang Valley. To the left of the tomb, there is a large mound where the coffin and its outer case have rotted, leaving only a skull that is three feet long. Chen Ren Zuo Peng personally witnessed this.

    ○秦进崇

    In the second year of Xiande during the Later Zhou Dynasty, the false Liangshui military commander Tai Jinchong was repairing the city walls and unearthed an ancient tomb. The coffin and its outer case were both rotted, and he found ancient coins, a broken bronze mirror, and a bottle. Inside the bottle was another bottle, which had a yellow body with black inscriptions in clerical script. The inscription read: "A pair of green birds, flying to five pounds. Ask about the weight of the boat, delivering a letter to Yangzhou." The following year, the Zhou forces attacked Wu, and Tai Jinchong died in the campaign.

    ○陈褒

    In Qingyuan, Chen Bao lived in a secluded retreat and sat by the window at night. Outside the window was the vast wilderness. Suddenly, he heard the sound of people and horses. Looking out, he saw a woman riding a tiger pass by the window and directly enter the western room. There was already a maid lying at the wall, and the woman immediately took a thin bamboo branch and pricked her through the wall crack. The maid suddenly felt abdominal pain, opened the door, and went to the toilet. Chen Bao was startled and had not yet spoken when the maid came out and was immediately seized by the tiger. He rushed forward to save her, barely escaping. The villagers said there was always this kind of strange phenomenon in the village, which is called the Tiger Ghost.

    189

    ○朱氏子

    　　广陵有朱氏子，家世勋贵，性好食牛，所杀无数。尝于暑月中，欲杀一牛，其母止之曰：“暑热如此，汝已醉，所食几何？勿杀也。”子向牛言曰：“汝能拜我，我赦汝。”牛应声下泪而拜，朱反怒曰：“畜生安能会人言？”立杀之。数日，乃病，恒见此牛为厉，竟作牛声而死。（《广记》卷四百三十四）

    　　○张某妻

    　　晋州神山县民张某妻，忽梦一人，衣黄褐衣，腰腹甚细，逼而淫之，两接而去。已而妊娠，遂好食生肉，常恨不饱，恒舐唇咬齿而怒，性益狠戾。居半岁，生二狼子，既生即走，其父急击死之。妻遂病恍惚，岁余乃复。乡人谓之狼母。（《广记》卷四百四十二）

    Explanation

    189

    The Son of the Zhu Family

    In Guangling, there was a son of the Zhu family, who came from an illustrious family with military or official titles. He had a fondness for eating beef and had killed countless cows. Once during a hot month, he wanted to kill a cow, but his mother stopped him, saying, "It is so hot, you are already drunk, how much have you eaten? Do not kill it." The son told the cow, "If you can bow to me, I will spare you." The cow responded by weeping and bowing. The son then became angry and said, "How can an animal understand human words?" He immediately killed the cow. A few days later, he fell ill and constantly saw the cow as a ghost, finally dying while making a cow's sound.

    The Wife of Zhang from Shen Mountain County

    In Shen Mountain County, Jin Prefecture, there was a man named Zhang whose wife suddenly had a dream of a person wearing yellowish-brown clothes, with a very slender waist and abdomen. The person forced and had sexual intercourse with her, after two encounters, he left. She then became pregnant and started liking to eat raw meat, often feeling unsatisfied, licking her lips and gnashing her teeth in anger, her character becoming increasingly fierce and cruel. After half a year, she gave birth to two wolf cubs, which ran away as soon as they were born. Her father quickly killed them. Her wife then fell ill and became delirious, after more than a year, she recovered. The villagers called her the Wolf Mother.

    190

    ○张谨

    　　道士张谨者，好符法，学虽苦而无成。尝客游至华阴市，见卖瓜者，买而食之。旁有老父，谨觉其饥色，取以遗之，累食百余，谨知其异，奉之愈敬。将去，谓谨曰：“吾土地之神也，感子之意，有以相报。”因出一编书曰：“此禁狐魅之术也，宜勤行之。”谨受之，父亦不见。尔日宿近县村中，闻其家有女子啼呼，状若狂者，以问主人，对曰：“家有女，近得狂疾，每日昃辄靓妆盛服，云召胡郎来。非不疗理，无如之何也。”谨即为书符，施檐户间。是日晚间，檐上哭泣且骂曰：“何物道士，预他人家事，宜急去之。”谨怒呵之。良久，大言曰：“吾且为奴矣。”遂寂然。谨复书数符，病即都差。主人遗绢数十匹以谢之。谨尝独行，既有重赍，须得傔力，停数日，忽有二奴诣谨，自称曰德儿、归宝，尝事崔氏，崔出官，因见舍弃。

    Explanation

    190

    A Taoist Priest Named Zhang Jin

    Zhang Jin, a Taoist priest, was fond of talismans and magical formulas. Although he studied diligently, he achieved no success. Once, while traveling as a guest to Huayin Market, he saw a seller of melons and bought one to eat. Nearby, there was an old man whom Zhang Jin noticed looked hungry. He took the melon and gave it to the old man, who ate it repeatedly, about a hundred times. Zhang Jin realized that the old man was unusual and treated him with even greater respect. As he was about to leave, the old man said to Zhang Jin, "I am the local land deity. I am grateful for your kindness and have something to repay you." He then produced a scroll and said, "This is a method for warding off fox spirits. You should practice it diligently." Zhang Jin accepted the scroll, and the old man disappeared. That night, Zhang Jin stayed in a nearby village and heard that a woman in the household was crying and calling out, acting as if she were possessed. He asked the host about it, and the host replied, "We have a daughter who recently became possessed. Every afternoon, she puts on fine clothes and makeup, claiming to summon 'Trickster Young Master' to come. We have tried to treat her, but nothing works." Zhang Jin then wrote several talismans and placed them on the eaves and door. That evening, someone cried and cursed from the eaves, saying, "What kind of Taoist priest are you, interfering in someone else's affairs? You should leave quickly!" Zhang Jin angrily rebuked them. After a long time, the voice shouted, "I will become your slave!" and then fell silent. Zhang Jin wrote several more talismans, and the woman's illness was completely cured. The host gave him dozens of bolts of silk as a token of gratitude. Once, Zhang Jin traveled alone with valuable possessions and needed an attendant. He stayed for several days when suddenly two servants came to see him, introducing themselves as De'er and Gui Bao. They had once served the Cui family but were dismissed from their positions and subsequently abandoned.

    191

    今无归矣，愿侍左右。谨纳之，二奴皆谨愿黠利，尤可凭信。谨东行，凡书囊、符法、过所、衣服，皆付归宝负之，将及关，归宝忽大骂曰：“以我为奴，如役汝父。”因绝走。谨骇怒，逐之，其行如风，倏忽不见。既而德儿亦不见，所赍之物皆失之矣。时秦陇用兵，关禁严急，客行无验，皆见刑戮。既不敢东度，复还主人，具以告之，主人怒曰：“宁有是事，是无厌复将挠我耳。”因止于田夫之家，绝不供给，遂为耕夫，邀与同作，昼耕夜息，疲苦备至，因憩大树下，仰见二儿，曰：“吾德儿、归宝也，汝之为奴，苦否？”又曰：“此符法，我之书也。失之已久，今喜再获，吾岂无情于汝乎？”因掷过所还之曰：“速归，乡人待尔书符也。”即大笑而去。谨得过所，复诣主人，方异之，更遗绢数匹乃得去。自尔遂绝书符矣。（《广记》卷四百五十五）

    Explanation

    191

    I have no place to return, and I wish to remain in your service. I respectfully accept your kindness. The two slaves, Gui Bao and De Er, are both diligent, cunning, and reliable, especially worthy of trust. I respectfully proceed eastward, entrusting all my books, talismans, travel permits, and clothes to Gui Bao to carry. As I approach the border checkpoint, Gui Bao suddenly starts cursing, saying, "To treat me as a slave, like serving your father!" Then he runs away. I am horrified and angry, chasing after him, but his running is as swift as the wind, and he disappears suddenly. Soon after, De Er also disappears, and all the items entrusted to me are lost. At the time, there were military campaigns in Qin and Long, and the border checkpoints were strictly controlled. Travelers without proper documentation were all subjected to punishment. I dare not proceed eastward, so I return to the master and report everything to him. The master angrily says, "How could there be such a thing? This is just another attempt to trouble me." Therefore, I stop at a farmer's house, no longer providing any support, and become a farm laborer. I am invited to work together, working during the day and resting at night, exhausted and suffering greatly. I rest under a large tree and look up to see two children, who say, "I am De Er and Gui Bao. Is being a slave hard for you?" They then say, "This talisman, it is my writing. I have lost it for a long time. I am glad to have it back. How could I be无情 to you?" Then they throw the travel permit back and say, "Hurry back, the people of your hometown are waiting for your talisman." They then laugh loudly and leave. I get the travel permit and return to the master, who finds it strange. The master then gives me several bolts of silk and lets me go. From then on, I no longer practice talismanic writing. (From Guangji Volume 455)

    192

    ○合肥富人

    　　合肥有富人刘某，好食鸡，每杀鸡，必先刖双足，置木柜中，血沥尽乃烹（曾慥《类说》作“膏血沥尽乃烹之”），以为去腥气。某后病，生疮于鬓。既愈，复生小鸡足于疮瘢中，每巾栉必伤其足，伤即流血被面，痛楚竟日。如是积岁，无日不伤，竟以是卒。（《广记》卷四百六十一，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    Explanation

    192

    合肥富人

    There was a wealthy man named Liu from Hefei who loved eating chicken. Whenever he killed a chicken, he would first cut off its feet, place it in a wooden cabinet, and let the blood drain completely before cooking it, in order to remove the fishy smell. Later, he fell ill and developed sores on his temples. After recovering, he again grew small chicken feet in the scabs. Every time he combed his hair, it would inevitably hurt his feet; the wound would bleed and cover his face, and the pain would last all day. In this way for many years, every day would be injured, and he eventually died because of this.

    (From "Guangji" Volume 461, also cited in "Leishuo" by Zeng Zao)

    193

    ○平固人

    　　处州平固人访其亲家，因留宿，夜分闻寝室中有人语声，徐起听之，乃群鹅语曰：“明旦主人将杀我，善视诸儿。”言之甚悉。既明，客辞去，主人曰：“我有鹅甚肥，将以食子。”客具告之，主人于是举家不复食鹅。顷之，举乡不食矣。（《广记》卷四百六十二）

    　　○海陵斗鹅

    　　乙卯岁（案：乙卯，周显德二年），海陵郡西村中，有二鹅斗于空中，久乃坠地。其大可五六尺，双足如驴蹄，村人杀而食之者皆卒。明年兵陷海陵。（《广记》卷四百六十二）

    　　○海陵人

    　　海陵县东居，人多以捕雁为业，恒养一雁，去其六翮以为媒。一日，群雁回塞，时雁媒忽人语谓主人曰：“我偿尔钱足，放我回去。”因腾空而去。此人遂不复捕雁。（《广记》卷四百六十二）

    Explanation

    193

    Translation

    A Person from Pinggu

    A person from Pinggu, a place in the state of Chu, visited a relative and stayed overnight. In the middle of the night, he heard voices in the bedroom. He slowly got up to listen and realized that the voices were coming from a group of geese. The geese said, "Tomorrow morning, the master will kill us. Take good care of the others." They spoke very clearly. The next morning, the guest bid farewell and left. The host said, "I have a very fat goose that I will eat." The guest informed him of the geese's warning, and the host then decided that his entire family would no longer eat geese. Soon after, the whole village stopped eating geese.

    Geese Fighting in Hailing

    In the year Bimao (955 AD, the second year of the reign of Emperor Shizong of the Zhou dynasty), in a western village of the Hailing Prefecture, two geese fought in the air for a long time before falling to the ground. The geese were as large as five or six feet, with feet like donkey hooves. Anyone who ate these geese died. The following year, the city of Hailing was conquered by the army.

    A Person from Hailing

    In the eastern part of Hailing County, many people made a living by hunting geese. They often kept a trained goose, removing its wings to use as a decoy. One day, when a flock of wild geese returned to their nesting grounds, the trained goose suddenly spoke to its owner in human language, saying, "I have paid you enough money. Let me go back." It then flew away into the sky. After this, the person stopped hunting geese.

    194

    ○广陵少年

    　　广陵有少年畜一鸜鹆，甚爱之，笼槛八十日，死，以小棺贮之，将瘗于野。至城门，阍吏发视之，乃人之一手也。（曾慥《类说》作》乃一人头”）执而拘诸吏，凡八十日，复为死鸜鹆，乃获免。（《广记》卷四百六十二，曾慥《类说》亦引）

    　　○染人

    　　广陵有染人，居九曲池南，梦一白衣少年求寄居焉，答曰：“吾家隘陋，不足以容君也。”乃入厨中。尔夕，举家梦之，既日，厨中得一白鳖，广尺余，两目如金，其人送诣紫极宫道士李栖一所，置之水中，则色如金，而目如丹，出水则白如故。栖一不能测，复送池中，遂不复见。（《广记》卷四百六十七）

    　　○海上人

    　　近有海上人，于鱼扈中得一物，是人一手，而掌中有面，七窍皆具，能动而不能语。传玩久之，或曰：“此神物也，不当杀之。”其人乃放置水上，此物浮水而去，可数十步，忽大笑数声，跃没于水。（《广记》卷四百六十七）

    Explanation

    194

    Translation of the Source Text

    The Young Man from Guangling

    In Guangling, there was a young man who kept a parrot, which he loved very much. He kept it in a cage for eighty days until it died. He then placed it in a small coffin and intended to bury it in the wild. When they reached the city gate, the gatekeeper opened the coffin to inspect it and found it to be a human hand. (According to Zeng Zao's Lei Shuo, it was said to be a human head.) The officials seized and detained it for eighty days, during which it became a dead parrot again, and thus escaped punishment. (From Guang Ji Volume 462, also cited in Zeng Zao's Lei Shuo.)

    The Dyer

    In Guangling, there was a dyer living south of Jiuquchi Pond. He dreamed of a white-clad young man asking to stay with him. He replied, "My home is narrow and humble, not worthy of accommodating you." So he entered the kitchen. That night, the whole family dreamed about him. The next day, they found a white turtle in the kitchen, about a foot wide with golden eyes. The man sent it to Daoist Master Li Xi-yi at Zijigong Palace, where it turned golden when placed in water and its eyes turned red, but returned to its original white color when taken out of the water. Master Li could not understand it, so he returned it to the pond, and it was never seen again. (From Guang Ji Volume 467.)

    The Man from the Sea

    Recently, there was a man from the sea who found an object in a fish trap. It turned out to be a human hand with a face on the palm and all seven orifices present. It could move but not speak. It was passed around for a long time, and someone said it was a divine object and should not be killed. The man then placed it in the water, and the object floated away for several dozen steps, suddenly laughed out loud a few times, and then jumped into the water and disappeared. (From Guang Ji Volume 467.)

    195

    ○契丹

    　　卢文进，幽州人也，至南，封范阳王。尝云陷契丹中，屡又绝塞射猎，以给军食，正昼方猎，忽天色晦黑，众星粲然，众皆惧，捕得蕃人问之，乃所谓笪却日也。此地以为寻常，当复矣。顷之乃明，日犹午也。又云，常于无定河见人脑骨一条，大如柱，长可七尺云。（《广记》卷四百八十）

    　　○杨蘧

    　　王赞，中朝名士。有弘农杨蘧者，曾至岭外，见杨朔荔浦山水，心常爱之，谈不容口。蘧尝出入赞门下，稍接从容，不觉形于言曰：“侍郎会见杨朔荔浦山水乎？”赞曰：“未曾打人唇绽齿落，安得见耶？”因大笑，此言岭外之地，非贬不去。（《广记》卷五百，按：今人李剑国考证此条实出《北梦琐言》卷五）

    Explanation

    195

    Translation

    契丹

    Lu Wenjin, a native of Youzhou, arrived in the south and was enfeoffed as Prince of Fanyang. He once said he was captured by the Khitans and often hunted beyond the frontier to provide food for the army. One day, while hunting at noon, the sky suddenly turned dark, and the stars shone brightly. Everyone was afraid. They captured a local and asked him, and he said it was what they call the "笪却日" (a day when the sun is blocked). In this region, it is considered ordinary, and it will return. After a while, the sky cleared, and the sun was still at noon. He also said that he often saw a human skull bone on the Wuding River, as large as a pillar and about seven feet long.

    杨蘧

    Wang Zan was a renowned scholar of the central court. There was a man from Hongnong named Yang Qu who once traveled to the south of the mountains and saw the mountains and waters of Yangshuo and Lixi, which he greatly loved and could not stop talking about. Yang Qu often visited Wang Zan's house, and after a while, he could not help but say, "Have you ever seen the mountains and waters of Yangshuo and Lixi, Sir?" Wang Zan replied, "I have never been beaten to the point of having my lips split and teeth broken, so how could I see them?" They both laughed. This means that the southern regions are not places one can go unless one is exiled.

    196

    ○洞中道士对棋

    　　婺源公山二洞，有穴如井。咸通末，有郑道士以绳缒下百余丈，旁有光，往视之，路穷阻水，隔岸有花木，二道士对棋，使一童子刺船而至，问：“欲渡否？”答曰：“当还。”童子回舟而去。郑复缒而出。明日井中有石笋塞其口，自是无入者。（曾慥《类说》）

    　　○波中妇人

    　　谢仲宣泛舟西江，见一妇人没波中，腰以下乃鱼也。竟不知人化鱼，鱼化人。（曾慥《类说》）

    　　○采菱遇蛟

    　　晋曲阿民谢盛，乘船入湖采菱，见一蛟来向船，盛以叉杀之，惧而还家。后数年亢旱，盛步至湖，见先叉在地，拾取之，忽心痛还家而卒。（曾慥《类说》。按：《广记》卷一三一题作《谢盛》，注出《幽明录》）

    　　○北斗君主簿

    Explanation

    Final Translation

    ○洞中道士对棋

    In the two caves of Gong Mountain in Wuyuan, there is a hole like a well. At the end of the Xiantong era, a Daoist priest named Zheng descended into the hole with a rope, more than a hundred zhang deep. There was light on the side, and upon looking, he found the path blocked by water, with flowers and trees on the opposite bank. Two Daoists were playing chess. He sent a child to row a boat to the other side and asked, "Do you want to cross?" The child replied, "We should return." The child rowed the boat back, and Zheng descended again and left. The next day, a stone bamboo shoot blocked the well, and no one entered after that. (From Lei Shuo by Zeng Zao)

    ○波中妇人

    Xie Zhongxuan sailed on the Xi River and saw a woman submerged in the water, with her lower body being a fish. It was unknown whether she was a human transformed into a fish or a fish transformed into a human. (From Lei Shuo by Zeng Zao)

    ○采菱遇蛟

    In the Jin Dynasty, a man from Qu'a named Xie Sheng went into the lake to collect water chestnuts. He saw a dragon-like creature approaching his boat and killed it with a spear, then returned home out of fear. Several years later, during a severe drought, Xie Sheng walked to the lake and found the spear he had used lying on the ground. He picked it up, suddenly experienced heart pain, and died at home. (From Lei Shuo by Zeng Zao. Note: Guang Ji Volume 131 titles this as Xie Sheng and cites You Ming Lu)

    ○北斗君主簿

    (Note: This part of the text is missing in the provided source. If there is additional content, it should be included here.)

    197

    许攸梦乌衣叟奉漆案上，有六封文书，拜跪曰：“府君当为北斗君，陈康为主簿。”既觉，康忽来谒，攸告之，康曰：“我作道师，死不过作社公，今得北斗主簿，主为忝矣。”明年同日而死。（曾慥《类悦》。按：《广记》卷二七六题作《许攸》，注出《幽明录》。）

    　　○杨祐患头风

    　　杨祐常患头风，医欲治之，祐曰：“吾生三日，时首向北户，觉风吹项，意甚患之，不能语耳，病源已远，不可治也。”（曾慥《类说》）

    　　○郑玄老奴

    　　王辅嗣注易，笑郑玄云老奴，甚无意，夜久忽闻外舀有著屐声，须臾入，自云是郑玄曰：“君年少，何以穿凿文句，妄讥老子？”言讫而去，辅嗣暴卒。（曾慥类说）

    　　○耻与魑魅争光

    　　嵇康灯下弹琴，忽一人，长丈余，著黑单衣革带，康熟视，乃吹火灭曰：“耻与魑魅争光。”（曾慥《类说》按：以上三条实出《类说》卷一一所节《幽明录》而非《稽神录》佚文）

    Explanation

    197

    Final Translation

    Xu You dreamed of an elderly man in black robes presenting a lacquer tray with six sealed documents. He bowed and knelt, saying, "Your Excellency will become the Lord of the North Star, and Chen Kang will serve as your clerk." Upon waking, Chen Kang suddenly came to pay respects. Xu You told him about the dream, and Chen Kang replied, "I am a Taoist priest, and in death, I will only become a local deity. Now that I have become a clerk of the North Star, it is truly an honor." The following year, they both died on the same day. (From Zeng Zao's Lei Yue.)

    Yang You often suffered from headaches. A doctor wanted to treat him, but Yang You said, "When I was three days old, my head was facing the northern window, and I felt the wind on my neck. I was deeply troubled by it and could not speak. The root of the illness is far too distant to be treated now." (From Zeng Zao's Lei Shuo.)

    Wang Bi, a famous commentator on the Yijing (Book of Changes), once mocked Zheng Xuan, calling him a "slave." Late one night, he suddenly heard the sound of footsteps outside. Soon after, a figure entered, introducing himself as Zheng Xuan and saying, "You are young, why do you force interpretations and mock an elder?" With that, he left. Wang Bi died suddenly shortly thereafter. (From Zeng Zao's Lei Shuo.)

    Ji Kang was playing the qin under a lamp when suddenly a tall figure, over ten feet tall, appeared, wearing a black single robe and a leather belt. Ji Kang looked at him closely and then blew out the lamp, saying, "I am ashamed to share glory with demons." (From Zeng Zao's Lei Shuo. Note: These three stories actually come from Lei Shuo Volume 11, excerpted from You Ming Lu rather than Ji Shen Lu.)

    198

    ○郑公场采银

    　　饶州郑公场，采银之所，山有涧水出底。天祐末，银夫十余人，傍涧凿地道，入数步，空阔明朗，山顶有穴如天窗，日光下照，楼阁四柱，石皆白银也。采银者复出，持斧而入将斫取之，俄而山摧，入者尽压死。顷之，流血自涧出，数日不绝，自是无敢入者。（曾慥《类说》）

    　　○李白旧宅酒

    　　沧州有李巡官，居洛阳空宅，其子夜读书，有皂衣肥短人被酒排闼而入，其子惧走，皂衣人怒曰：“李白尚与我为友，汝何为者耶？”其子疑其神仙，再拜延坐，皂衣曰：“吾有酒，与汝饮。”乃以席帽盛酒而至数杯，基父从户外窥见，以为怪魅，以砖掷之，皂衣走。视其帽，酒盖也。明日，粪壤中得一只，故老云李翰林旧宅也。（曾慥《类说》）

    Explanation

    198

    V. The Silver Mine of Zheng Gongchang

    In the silver mine of Zheng Gongchang, located in Raoyang Prefecture, during the end of the Tianyou period, more than ten silver miners dug a tunnel beside a stream. After entering a few steps, they found the interior spacious and bright. On the mountain top, there was a hole like a skylight, and sunlight shone down. There was a structure resembling a building with four pillars, and the stones were all made of silver. The miners then exited and returned with axes to cut and take the silver. Soon, the mountain collapsed, and those who entered were all crushed to death. Blood flowed out from the stream for several days and did not stop. From then on, no one dared to enter.

    VI. The Old Residence of Li Bai

    In Cangzhou, there was an official named Li Xun, who lived in an empty house in Luoyang. One night, his son was reading, and a short, fat person wearing black clothes, drunk, pushed open the door and entered. His son was frightened and ran away. The black-clothed person angrily said, "Li Bai still considers me a friend. What are you doing here?" His son suspected that the person was a spirit or a deity and bowed twice to invite him to sit. The black-clothed person said, "I have some wine. Let's drink together." He then brought some wine in a hat and poured several cups. Li Xun's father, seeing from outside the house, thought it was a monster or spirit and threw a brick at him. The black-clothed person ran away. When they looked at the hat, it was a wine bottle cap. The next day, they found a wine bottle in the excrement. The old people said it was the former residence of Li Haolong (a nickname for Li Bai).

    199

    ○老猿窃妇人

    　　晋州含山有妖鬼，好窃妇人。尝有士人行至含山，夜失其妻，旦而寻求；入深山，一大石，有五六妇人共坐，问曰：“君何至此？”具言其故，妇人曰：“贤夫人昨夜至此，在石室中，吾等皆经过为所窃也。将军窃人至此，与行容彭之术，每十日一试，取索练周缠其身及手足，作法运气，练皆断裂。每一试辄增一疋，明日当五疋。君明旦至此伺之，吾等当以六七疋急缠其身，俟君至即共杀之，可乎？”其人如期而往，见一人貌甚可畏，众妇以练缚之，至六疋乃直前格之，遂杀之，乃一老猿也。因获其妻，众妇皆得出，其怪遂绝。（曾慥《类说》）

    Explanation

    199

    ○ The Old Ape Steals Women

    In the mountain of Hán in the state of Jin, there was a supernatural spirit that liked to steal women. Once, a scholar was traveling to the mountain and lost his wife at night. The next day, he searched for her and entered the deep mountain. He saw a large rock where five or six women were sitting together. They asked, "Why have you come here?" The scholar explained the reason, and the women said, "Your virtuous wife was stolen here last night and is in a stone room. We have all been stolen by the old ape. The old ape steals people here and performs a magical ritual called 'Xing Rong Peng.' Every ten days, it tests its power by wrapping fine silk tightly around its body and limbs. It summons energy, but the silk all breaks. Each time, it adds one more piece of silk. Tomorrow, it will be five pieces. You should come here tomorrow to see what happens. We will wrap six or seven pieces of silk around it, and when you arrive, we will kill it together. Will that be okay?" The scholar came as planned and saw a person with a very frightening appearance. The women wrapped him with silk, and when they had six pieces, they attacked him and killed him. It turned out to be an old ape. The scholar then recovered his wife, and all the women were freed. The strange event finally ended. (Zeng Zhao, Class Sayings)

    200

    ○凶宅掘银

    　　寿州大将赵璘；本州有凶宅，人莫敢居，璘入居之，独据中堂，夜有物推床曰：“我等在此已久，为君所压，甚不快，君可速去。”鬼乃相与移其床于庭下，璘亦安寝。明日，于堂上置床处掘得银一窖，宅遂安。（曾慥《类说》）

    　　○紫薇宫题壁

    　　建业市有卜者，忽于紫薇宫题壁云：“昨日朝天过紫薇，玉坛风冷杏花稀。碧桃昵我传消息，何事人间更不归。”自是绝迹，人皆言其上升。（曾慥《类说》）

    　　●再补

    　　○鄂州小将（李剑国辑）

    Explanation

    200

    Final Translation

    Digging Silver from a Cursed House

    In Shouzhou, General Zhao Lin; there was a cursed house in the state, which no one dared to inhabit. Zhao Lin moved in and alone occupied the main hall. At night, something pushed his bed and said, "We have been here for a long time and have been greatly uncomfortable due to your presence. You should leave quickly." The ghosts then moved his bed to the courtyard, and Zhao Lin slept peacefully. The next day, when he dug where the bed had been placed in the main hall, he found a cache of silver. The house then became peaceful. (From Lei Shuo by Zeng Zao)

    Inscription on the Wall of Ziwěi Palace

    In Jianye market, there was a fortune-teller who suddenly wrote on the wall of Ziwěi Palace, saying, "Yesterday, I went to heaven and passed through Ziwěi. The jade altar was cold with sparse apricot flowers. The peach tree whispered messages to me, but why not return to the mortal world?" From then on, he disappeared, and people all said he ascended to heaven. (From Lei Shuo by Zeng Zao)

    Further Additions

    A Young Officer from Ezhou (Compiled by Li Jianguo)

    201

    鄂州小将某者，本田家子。既仕，欲结豪族，而谋其故妻。因相与归宁，杀之于路，弃尸江侧，并杀其同行婢。已而奔告其家，号哭云“为盗所杀”，人不之疑也。后数年，奉使至广陵，舍于逆旅。见一妇人卖花，酷类其所杀婢；既近，乃真是婢。见己亦再拜。因问：“为人耶鬼耶？”答云：“人也。往者为贼所击，幸而不死。既苏，得贾人船，寓载东下。今在此，与娘子卖花给食而已。”复问：“娘子何在？”曰：“在近。”“可见之乎？”曰：“可。”即随之而去。一小曲中，指一贫舍曰：“此是也。”婢先入。顷之，其妻乃出，相见悲涕，备述艰苦。某亦恍然，莫之测也。俄而设食具酒，复延入内室，置饮食于从者，皆醉。日暮不出。从者稍前觇之，寂若无人。因直入室中，但见白骨一具，衣服毁裂，流血满地。问其邻，云：“此空宅，久无居人矣。”（《广记》卷一三○，未题书名。《白孔六帖》卷九○《报怨》引《稽神录》，名《卖花娘子》）

    Explanation

    201

    A small officer from Ezhou, who was originally the son of a farmer, became an official and wished to marry into a noble family. He plotted against his former wife and, during a visit home, killed her on the road, abandoned her body by the river, and also killed the maid who was traveling with her. He then rushed to inform his family, crying and saying that she had been killed by bandits, and no one doubted him. Several years later, he was sent on a mission to Yangzhou and stayed at an inn. There, he saw a woman selling flowers who looked very much like the maid he had killed; when he approached her, he realized it was indeed the maid. She also recognized him and bowed twice. He asked, "Are you a living person or a ghost?" She replied, "I am a living person. I was struck by bandits in the past, but luckily I did not die. After regaining consciousness, I found a merchant's boat and traveled eastward. Now I am here, selling flowers with this woman to make a living." He then asked, "Where is your mistress?" She said, "She is nearby." "Can I see her?" He asked. "Yes," she replied. So he followed her and they went to a small alley, where she pointed to a poor house and said, "This is it." The maid went in first. Shortly after, his wife came out, and they met with tears, recounting their hardships. The officer was also dazed and could not comprehend what was happening. Soon after, they prepared food and wine, and invited him into the inner room, placing the food and drink in front of his attendants, who all became drunk. At dusk, they did not come out. One of his attendants cautiously peeked inside and found it as quiet as if no one were there. He then entered the room and saw only a pile of bones, with clothes torn and blood covering the ground. When he asked the neighbors, they said, "This is an empty house, and no one has lived here for a long time." (From Guang Ji Volume 130, untitled. Bai Kong Liu Tie Volume 90 Bao Yuan quotes Ji Shen Lu, titled The Flower-Selling Woman.)

    202

    ○食核桃（李剑国辑）

    　　杨子留后吴尧卿家，有佣赁者，役之既久。一日，持一大桃核，可容数升，以献尧卿。尧卿知其异，稍磨之取食。食尽，颇觉轻健。尧卿为吏，贪猥残虐，毕师铎之难，投所居后阁井中死。师铎求得类尧卿者杀之。后有得其故居者，窃知其尸在井中，取而得之，举体皆腐坏，而藏府有成金者。（《广记》卷四一○引《积神录》。“积”乃“稽”字之讹）

    Explanation

    202

    ○ Eating Hawthorn Nuts (Compiled by Li Jian Guo)

    Yangzi, the deputy governor of Wu Yaoqing's household, had a hired worker who had served for a long time. One day, the worker brought a large hawthorn nut, which could hold several liters, to present to Wu Yaoqing. Wu Yaoqing recognized its unusual nature and ground it slightly to eat it. After eating it, he felt quite light and healthy. Wu Yaoqing was a greedy, corrupt, and cruel official. During the crisis led by毕师铎, he was thrown into a well in the back of his residence and died.毕师铎 sought out someone similar to Wu Yaoqing and killed them. Later, someone who acquired his former residence secretly found out that his body was in the well, retrieved it, and found that the entire body was rotten and decayed, but the internal organs contained solid gold. (From Volume 410 of《广记》, citing《积神录》. "积" is a misprint for "稽".)

    203

    ○掬沙扑人（李剑国辑）

    　　新安人吴生尝病热死。既棺歛，忽有一鬼，被发跣足，自门而入，径至殡所，掬沙以扑人。人皆惊走，即闻椎声喧噪。良久，瞥见一人，衣冠俨然，入厨中，少顷即出，去。至墓，家人乃敢临视，棺已开，中亦空矣。数月，吴自建康附书云：“吾已死矣，有鬼救我，遂活。既寝，渴甚，即入厨中饮讫，性犹恍惚，不觉出门，今在都矣。”后岁余，乃归，人皆呼为“吴还魂”。（《白孔六帖》卷九○《再生》引《稽神录》）

    　　○木客（李剑国辑）

    　　鄱阳山中有木客，自言秦时造阿房宫采木者也。食木实，遂得不死（《能改》“死”作“绝”）。时就民间酤酒酣饮。为诗一章云：“酒尽君莫酤，壶倾我当发。城市多嚣尘，还山拜（《能改》作“弄”）明月。”（《集注分类东坡先生诗》卷二《虔州八境图》赵次公注引徐铉《小说》。《能改斋漫录》卷八《还山弄明月》亦引此段，题徐鼎臣《搜神记》）

    Explanation

    203

    Final Translation

    ○ Scooping Sand to Hit People (Compiled by Li Jianguo)

    A man from Xin'an named Wu Sheng once died from a severe fever. After he was placed in the coffin and sealed, suddenly a ghost appeared, with disheveled hair and bare feet, entering through the door and directly reaching the place where the body was laid out. The ghost scooped up sand to hit people. Everyone was startled and ran away, and immediately loud and chaotic sounds were heard. After a long time, someone saw a person dressed in formal attire entering the kitchen, staying there for a short while before leaving. When they arrived at the tomb, the family dared to approach and look inside. The coffin was already open, and it was empty. Several months later, Wu Sheng sent a letter from Jiankang saying, "I have already died, but a ghost saved me and brought me back to life. After I went to sleep, I was very thirsty and went into the kitchen to drink. I was still in a dazed state and did not realize I had left the house, and now I am in the capital." More than a year later, he returned home, and everyone called him "Wu the Reanimated" (Wu Huanhun).

    (Quoted from Volume 90, "Rebirth," of Bai Kong Liu Tie [White and Black Six Collections], citing Ji Shen Lu [Record of Divine Matters])

    ○ Wood Spirit (Compiled by Li Jianguo)

    In the mountains of Poyang, there is a wood spirit who claims to have been involved in the construction of the A-Fang Palace during the Qin dynasty, gathering wood. By eating the fruit of trees, it has achieved immortality (in Neng Gai [The Book of Corrections], "死" is written as "绝"). It occasionally goes into the village to buy wine and drink heartily. It composed a poem that says:

    "Drink up, do not buy more wine,
    Pour out the pot, and I will leave.
    Cities are full of noise and dust,
    Return to the mountains to worship (or play with) the moon."

    (Quoted from Volume 2, "Classified Annotations of Su Shi's Poems," Qian Zhou Ba Jing Tu [Eight Landscapes of Qianzhou], Zhao Cigong's notes, citing Xu Xuan's Xiao Shuo [Small Stories]. Also quoted in Volume 8, "Returning to the Mountains to Play with the Moon," of Neng Gai Zhai Man Lu [Random Notes from the Neng Gai Studio], attributed to Xu Dingchen's Suo Shen Ji [Records of the Supernatural])

    204

    ○干大（程毅中辑）

    　　洪州西山中有樵人，自称干大，众莫知其名。时出村落，与人相接，拱揖而已，未尝交一言。人欲问之，辄揖而去。有少年者，俟其出，拜之曰：“愿事先生。”干大惊欲去。少年急捉其衣褐，随之而往，干大曰：“尔何为者？”辄对曰：“愿事先生。”且拜且行，经历险绝，辄不踅舍。久之，乃坐涧水傍曰：“尔欲茶不？”少年曰：“诺。”即解衣襟间取茶末，置少年掌中，使掬水吞之讫。因卧，良久而寤，遂失干大。寻樵路而出，乃分宁县界，数日还家。少年自此轻健无疾。（《道藏》本《历世真仙体道通鉴》卷二十七《许大》引《稽神录》）

    Explanation

    204

    In the western mountains of Hongzhou, there lived a woodcutter who called himself Gan Da. No one knew his real name. He occasionally visited villages, greeted people with a bow, but never spoke a word. When people tried to ask him questions, he would bow and leave. One day, a young man waited for him to appear, bowed to him, and said, "I wish to serve you as your disciple." Gan Da was surprised and wanted to leave, but the young man quickly grabbed his robe and followed him. Gan Da asked, "What are you doing?" The young man replied, "I wish to serve you." They continued walking, with the young man bowing and following Gan Da through dangerous and difficult terrain, never stopping or turning back. After some time, they came to a stream where Gan Da sat down and asked, "Would you like some tea?" The young man said, "Yes." Gan Da took tea powder from his sleeve, placed it in the young man's hand, and told him to drink it with water. Afterward, Gan Da lay down, and the young man fell asleep. When he woke up, Gan Da had disappeared. The young man followed the path of the woodcutter and eventually found his way out, reaching the boundary of Fenning County. He returned home after several days. From that day on, the young man became light, strong, and free of illness.
